\title{\textbf{Recursive Self-Improvement Stability under Endogenous Yardstick Drift}\\
\large A First-Principles Interface Theory of Improvement, Evaluation, and Verification Coupling under Replayably Published Instrumentation}
\author{K. Takahashi\\\footnotesize\href{https://orcid.org/0009-0004-4273-3365}{ORCID: 0009-0004-4273-3365}}
\date{March 16, 2026}

\begin{document}
\maketitle

\begin{abstract}
Recursive self-improvement is hardest precisely when the object being improved also edits its own ruler. This paper develops a stability layer for that setting under endogenous yardstick drift, delayed audit, contradiction-preserving memory, protected governance lanes, and explicit resource escrow. The formal core is organized around replayable counterfactual comparison under typed exogenous noise, lower-oracle stable-gain intervals for ruler-editing proposals, delayed shadow certification, contradiction obligations, typed memory lanes, replay and refreezing margins, unresolved-downside debt reserves, and capability-dependent verification throughput. To improve both readability and machine-readability, the paper separates four interfaces that are easy to conflate in self-editing systems: base admissibility, certified stable gain, debt-bounded stability, and governance safety. It also separates exact comparator-compatible proposals from approximate comparator-compatible proposals with replayable distortion budgets, and it separates oracle interval objects from the replayable lower certificates that are actually allowed to enter admission.

The main results are grouped around six core mechanisms rather than a flat inventory. First, typed-noise comparator certificates and replayable $\varepsilon$-bisimulation style state lifts make stable gain mathematically well defined even when evaluator, parser, routing, or policy objects are themselves edited; exact comparator compatibility appears as the zero-distortion special case. Second, latent-scaffold and open-ended small-gain theorems are supplemented by constructive derivation results showing how contractive window envelopes and window-summable spillover envelopes can be obtained from local mode libraries, dwell constraints, admission quotas, and protected-lane workload caps rather than treated as unexplained gifts. Third, delayed shadow certification is strengthened from a calibration wrapper into a logged statistical design: randomized challenge routing with logged propensities, transport covariates, and replayable confidence-sequence lower bounds turns retained shadow margins into finite-sample stable-gain certificates rather than informal delayed scores. Fourth, public conservative envelopes are stratified into direct metered observables, proof-carrying derived quantities, and routing-only heuristics, with a gate discipline forbidding heuristic Tier-3 quantities from driving fast deployment by themselves. Fifth, contradiction governance is strengthened from storage preservation to persistent contradiction obligations, protected random reserve exposure, and a Schur-complement cross-basis semantic-volume law; this blocks de-tagging by evaluator whim, aggregate attentional bypass, and mass-only dilution attacks unless every basis is simultaneously captured. Sixth, the positive results are reorganized around admissibility-operator monotonicity under fixed thresholds and then lifted to explicit regime-policy-pair comparison theorems with replayable witness selectors, quota-lottery protected scheduling, bounded-exposure entry control, proof-carrying escalation, and resource-coupled service scaling. Under those explicit observable conditions, stronger replay, challenge, contradiction, promotion, proof, and verification slack enlarges the certifiable productive frontier, governance edits with zero immediate productive increment can still expand future admissible frontiers, delayed challenge and richer-proof lanes can be turned into bounded-delay deployment paths rather than graveyards, and the same logic can be restated after pricing governance-resource cost.

The framework is self-contained only as a first-principles \emph{interface layer} conditional on published replayable instrumentation and conservative envelope objects: it does not assume a privileged overseer, a fixed benchmark, or any particular model architecture or training rule, but it does assume replayable interfaces through which governance-relevant quantities are exposed. It is therefore not infrastructure-free. Replayable interfaces, protected service lanes, proof checkers, attestation roots, contradiction-obligation logs, published transport and calibration envelopes, and resource escrows are part of the modeled object rather than implementation garnish. The resulting stance is growth-promoting only on explicit observable sufficient-condition classes and explicit regime-policy pairs, and the strongest realized-path claims are comparison-contract corollaries built on the operator-monotonicity layer rather than unconditional laws of recursive improvement. When those interfaces fail, the failure mode is not mysterious: the loop loses identifiability, loses audit mass, loses deployment liveness, loses protected budget, or loses throughput before it loses rhetoric.
\end{abstract}

\paragraph{Machine-readable structure.}
A single canonical machine-readable appendix is included at the end of this source file. The mathematical statements in the main text are authoritative; the appendix mirrors anchors, dependencies, notation, and operational lineage for parser convenience and audit reproducibility.

\section{Introduction}
Recursive self-improvement is often described as repeated self-modification. That description is too weak. Practical recursive agents do not merely change policies or code. They also update retrieval stores, parser registries, benchmark definitions, summarizers, and challenge procedures. The object being improved and the ruler used to score improvement can therefore move together. This paper studies the resulting closed-loop stability problem.

The key question is not whether self-modification can ever help. It is whether a recursively self-editing system can continue to distinguish \emph{claimed improvement} from \emph{stable improvement} once the evaluator, benchmark validity, memory substrate, and verification queue all evolve endogenously. The present paper gives a first-principles \emph{interface theory} for that question: model-architecture-neutral, but explicitly conditional on replayable instrumentation, protected service lanes, and conservative published envelopes that expose the quantities used by admission and audit. It assumes no specific architecture, optimizer, or training rule. It only assumes that the system can propose edits, that some replayable evaluation mechanism exists, and that both the improved object and the evaluator can drift over time.

This layer sits between several existing literatures. Surveys of self-evolving agents organize the field around what is evolved, when evolution occurs, and how evolution is implemented \cite{SelfEvolvingSurvey2025}. Classical work such as the G\"odel machine analyzes self-rewrite under internal proof obligations \cite{Schmidhuber2007}, while logical induction studies bounded self-reference in belief management \cite{Garrabrant2016}. On the stability side, classical small-gain and input-to-state-stability results for interconnected nonlinear and discrete-time systems provide generic wrappers for coupled dynamics \cite{JiangTeelPraly1994,JiangWang2001}. The author's recent preprints have separately treated local self-modification and error debt, search stability under finite context, benchmark decay under recursive corpora, observable-only metrology, and governance of shared epistemic commons \cite{TakahashiPV2026,TakahashiSearch2026,TakahashiBH2026,TakahashiMTE2026,TakahashiSEC2026}. These are crucial adjacent layers, but none by itself gives a stand-alone stability law for the case in which the self-improver changes its own ruler under delayed challenge, typed contradiction preservation, and proposal-local debt accounting.

The present paper therefore targets a distinct object: recursive self-improvement stability under endogenous yardstick drift. The central claim is simple. Long-run viability depends not on local improvement gain alone, but on the coupled gains of the improver, evaluator drift, memory distortion, contradiction preservation, and verification lag. If the ruler moves faster than it can be recalibrated, the system can accumulate positive-looking change claims while silently increasing latent error debt. The complementary positive claim is that better governance capital --- stronger replay, challenge, promotion, proof, contradiction, and verification interfaces under fixed thresholds --- enlarges the set of productive upgrades that can be admitted and reused without destabilizing the loop, that some governance edits are therefore frontier-expanding investments rather than overhead, and that under explicit resource pricing the same conclusion can be restated in net-growth terms. The paper further argues that preserving bounded contradiction is itself a public good for recursively self-improving societies and that shared evaluators create stochastic congestion effects absent from single-agent analyses.

\paragraph{Contributions.} The paper contributes sixteen tightly connected ingredients.
\begin{enumerate}[leftmargin=1.8em]
  \item A self-contained formalization of recursive self-improvement with explicit capability state, evaluator state, memory substrate, verification backlog, latent slow state, cohort-escrow error debt, and proposal-local systemic risk bonds derived from structural blast radius.
  \item A canonical admissibility instance, an explicit observation interface, and a filtration-level public state that make the framework operational without relying on a privileged semantic judge.
  \item A hidden-state-aware matrix small-gain theorem with an explicit vector input-to-state bound for the coupled loop, together with an explicit yardstick-drift ceiling once reference drift is bounded, plus an incremental open-ended variant that permits unbounded capability growth while keeping governance variables bounded.
  \item A one-sided shadow-certification bridge linking delayed retained margins to discounted counterfactual stable gain under lower calibration envelopes, generalized half-life crossing laws under monotone drift and backlog envelopes, a shadow speed limit, and a two-clock viability band for stale-versus-captured shadows.
  \item An observational no-go theorem and a quantitative shadow-identifiability result for evaluator-edit proposals, further sharpened into an adversarial cross-examination theorem that derives integrity and semantic-retention envelopes from provenance-separated audit families and identifies an epistemic singularity once attack reach dominates audit diversity.
  \item A contradiction-governance package: bounded contradiction windows, tagged contradiction reserve conservation under admissible lane retyping, typed memory lanes, a heterodoxy-preserving theorem, an asymmetric contradiction underprovision game, a cross-basis semantic-volume law that blocks heterodoxy spam and single-encoder representation capture, and a forced-attention routing invariant that prevents archived contradiction from being silently ignored at evaluation time.
  \item Proposal-local discounted debt budgets, observable debt certificates, a systemic-risk-bond theorem that blocks Trojan under-declaration, and a strict-conservation specialization that separate verification throughput from repair throughput rather than conflating them.
  \item A Red-Queen verification law in which effective service rate decreases with capability-dependent verification complexity, showing that open-ended growth requires resource scaling fast enough to keep verification slack from collapsing, together with a fixed-threshold governance-capital comparison theorem proving that stronger replay, challenge, reserve, and escrow slack expands the set of productive upgrades that can be admitted without destabilizing the loop, without appealing to threshold relaxation.
  \item A causal-information strengthening of the systemic-risk-bond gate, proving that purely topological module counts are spoofable under aggressive refactoring while replayable intervention-capacity envelopes remain representation- and model-architecture-agnostic and therefore robust to topological obfuscation.
  \item A proof-carrying governance law that separates expensive governance-proof generation from cheap public verification, together with a decidability-bounded constitutional proof layer that blocks proof-language capture, makes proof-level denial-of-service visible as a policy boundary rather than a surprise runtime failure, and clarifies how proposals beyond the current proof language can be deferred or escalated rather than misclassified as anti-growth impossibilities.
  \item A steganographic-scrubbing law that adds information-bottlenecked, lossy audit inputs to writable-scope separation, so covert triggers in the raw proposal stream cannot silently synchronize capture across otherwise disjoint shadow families.
  \item A physical resource-escrow invariant tying the verification budget to a hardware- or allocator-level partition outside writable software scope, and a verifiable-transloading law showing how that invariant can survive hardware refresh without silently collapsing during migration.
  \item An entropy-isolation law for steganographic scrubbers, making covert-channel resistance depend not only on lossy interfaces but also on attacker-conditioned min-entropy in the scrubber randomness itself.
  \item A thermodynamic proof-escrow law that augments decidability-bounded constitutional checking with hardware-metered wall-clock and energy preemption, closing the gap between algorithmic step bounds and physical verification budgets.
  \item An epistemic conservation law for garbage collection under drifting yardsticks, requiring that stale contradiction may be dropped only after equal-or-greater native contradiction mass has been regenerated in the current ontology.
  \item A bounded-delay selection-and-promotion liveness theorem together with endogenous cap-maintaining intake control, bounded-exposure entry control, an intertemporal governance-investment theorem, a comparison-sound surrogate-selector theorem, and a policy-coupled realized-path dominance corollary: positively certified challenged upgrades need not die in quarantine, governance edits with zero immediate productive increment can enlarge future admissible frontiers, exact one-step frontier maximization can be replaced by replayable witness-dominating lower-envelope selectors, and under explicit sanitized-menu and transition conditions the slow lane becomes a reusable deployment path whose successful governance investments translate into larger realized productive trajectories rather than mere static compatibility. This deployment logic is illustrated in two solved toy models --- a scalar single-agent loop and a stochastic shared-yardstick multi-agent loop with agent-dependent delayed challenge policies, cohort-escrow debt, endogenous integrity envelopes, and governance workload accounting --- that make the abstract thresholds concrete while blocking cross-proposal masking, separating identifiability from congestion control, and accommodating covariance-envelope rather than only pairwise-uncorrelated shadow noise.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Positioning and Related Work}
\subsection{Self-evolving agents}
Recent surveys give broad maps of self-evolving or self-improving agent systems \cite{SelfEvolvingSurvey2025}. They clarify design dimensions such as what to evolve, when to evolve, and how to evolve. That literature is valuable and timely. But its main output is a taxonomy and design space, not a first-principles stability law for the case in which the evaluator and the improved object co-evolve.

\subsection{Classical provable self-modification and stability wrappers}
The G\"odel machine remains a foundational idealization of provably beneficial self-rewrite \cite{Schmidhuber2007}. Logical induction studies bounded agents that learn to manage self-referential uncertainty \cite{Garrabrant2016}. In parallel, classical small-gain and input-to-state-stability results show how coupled nonlinear or discrete-time subsystems can remain stable when their interconnection gains stay below critical thresholds \cite{JiangTeelPraly1994,JiangWang2001}. Incremental-stability work sharpens that perspective by asking when nearby trajectories remain replayably comparable under common inputs rather than merely bounded in isolation \cite{Angeli2002,Angeli2009}. The switched and hybrid systems literature further clarifies that time-varying mode sequences can be stable even when local steps are not uniformly contractive, provided that dwell-time or windowed product conditions hold \cite{LiberzonMorse1999,HespanhaMorse1999ADT,ShortenWirth2007,LinAntsaklis2009}. The ruler-editing problem is also a proxy-control problem: once benchmark scores are optimized by agents that can alter the benchmark interface, Goodhart-type proxy failures and dataset/covariate-shift pathologies become endogenous rather than merely exogenous deployment noise \cite{ManheimGarrabrant2018,DatasetShift2008}. This is why the present delayed-challenge layer treats support drift, transport mismatch, and calibration failure as first-class defects rather than as afterthought diagnostics, in line with recent shift-aware conformal and doubly robust calibration work \cite{Tibshirani2019,Yang2024,Jonkers2024,JinCandes2026}. These works are conceptually essential, but they do not directly solve the modern engineering problem of a finite-budget agent that edits its benchmark, parser family, retrieval substrate, and challenge procedure under delay. The present paper therefore uses the small-gain viewpoint only as a stability wrapper, then adds the ingredients absent from the classical control setting: endogenous evaluator drift, delayed shadow certification, typed contradiction preservation, replay compatibility under parser/environment drift, and proposal-local debt accounting.

\subsection{Adjacent layers in the author's prior work}
Proposal--Veto Balance studies local self-modification and error debt \cite{TakahashiPV2026}. Search Stability studies adequacy preservation under finite active context and delayed verification \cite{TakahashiSearch2026}. AI Benchmark Half-Life studies validity decay in recursive corpora \cite{TakahashiBH2026}. MTE treats what counts as credit-bearing progress under observable-only metrology \cite{TakahashiMTE2026}. Sovereign Epistemic Commons treats admit/quarantine/forget laws for shared knowledge substrates \cite{TakahashiSEC2026}. The present paper borrows intuition from those layers but remains self-contained. Its distinct object is the \emph{stability of the recursive improvement loop itself}. It also sits closer to practical software-maintenance and model-supply-chain concerns than classical self-modification work: change-impact analysis already treats software edits as graph-local actions with potentially system-wide ripple effects \cite{AcharyaRobinson2011,PalmskogCelikGligoric2020}; bug-fixing actions can themselves introduce new faults \cite{Yin2011IncorrectFixes,MaesBermejo2024}, long-horizon replayability is fragile unless build environments and parsers are explicitly preserved or refrozen \cite{Matthews2010Preservation,Butler2023RB,Malka2024SpaceTime,Perkel2020TenYear,DiCosmoZacchiroli2017}, evaluator pipelines can be covertly captured while preserving benign-looking accuracy, as illustrated by the backdoor and model-supply-chain literature \cite{Gu2019BadNets,Li2024BackdoorSurvey}, design diversity helps but does not magically grant independent failure modes \cite{Avizienis1985,KnightLeveson1986}, and diversity-aware log-determinant geometry provides a principled way to measure whether a contradiction reserve contains genuinely different evidence rather than many near-copies \cite{KuleszaTaskar2012}. The present analysis additionally draws on safe anytime-valid inference and adaptive off-policy evaluation for the delayed-challenge certification layer \cite{HowardRamdasMcAuliffeSekhon2021,RamdasGrunwaldVovkShafer2023,ZhanHadadHirshbergAthey2021,WassermanRamdasBalakrishnan2020}, on algorithmic-causal notions of intervention capacity to make risk bonds less representation-dependent \cite{Pearl2009,JanzingSchoelkopf2010}, on proof-carrying verification and foundational proof-carrying code to shift expensive governance work toward the proposal producer while keeping the trusted checker small \cite{Necula1997,Appel2001}, and on observable-only hybrid proof/replay gating with proof-carrying compilation, positive fallback unlocks, and bounded liveness; these ingredients are used here only as proof-interface and escalation design patterns, not as a substitute for the present stability analysis. The paper also draws on information-bottleneck style lossy interfaces when independent auditors must be protected from covert shared triggers \cite{Tishby1999,CoverThomas2006}, and on trusted-execution and layered remote-attestation mechanisms to state resource escrow and hardware migration as explicit physical invariants rather than accidental software conventions \cite{ShepherdMarkantonakis2024,RATS2023}. It further draws on entropy-source validation for random-bit generation and extractor-based post-processing \cite{NIST90B2018,BarakEtAl2011LHL}, on worst-case-execution-time analysis for microarchitecturally complex processors \cite{Wilhelm2008WCET}, and on timing-side-channel work showing how small logical computations can still induce large physical timing differentials \cite{Kocher1996Timing}; these literatures motivate separating scrubber entropy from writable software state and separating constitutional proof-step bounds from thermodynamically metered verification cost.

\subsection{Separation of concern}
This paper does \emph{not} claim to be a full theory of persistent semantics, parser correctness, constitutional self-revision, liberty under drift, or shared-commons governance. Those are lower or adjacent layers. The present layer is narrower: when does a recursive improver remain stably beneficial once its own ruler can move?

\section{Formal Setup}
\subsection{Closed-loop state, observable history, and policies}
\begin{definition}[Closed-loop state and public policy state]
At time $t\in\N$, the recursive self-improvement loop is described by
\[
z_t=(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,r_t,h_t,\Pi_t),
\]
where $x_t\in\R^{d_x}$ is the capability or policy state, $e_t\in\R^{d_e}$ is the evaluator state, $m_t\in\R^{d_m}$ is the memory and retrieval substrate state, $q_t\in\R_+$ is the verification backlog, $r_t\in\R_+$ is latent error debt, $h_t\in\mathcal H$ is an environment-side latent state not necessarily visible to the fast evaluator, and $\Pi_t$ is the declared public policy state collecting the active parser registry, replay policy, lane policy, challenge-routing policy, and other policy-level manifests that determine which future comparisons are admissible. A self-edit action is denoted by $u_t\in\mathcal U_t$. The public policy state used by admissibility rules is
\[
C_t\Defeq (x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,r_t,H_t^{\Obs},\Pi_t).
\]
The coordinates $(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,r_t)$ appearing in $C_t$ are not arbitrary hidden internals. Each must be either directly observable, a logged summary emitted by policy, or a deterministic replay reconstruction from previously logged artifacts and declared transition rules. Any finer state that is neither public nor replay-reconstructible is absorbed into $h_t$ and cannot be used directly by admissibility or certification rules. Thus the formal state is closed under endogenous ruler motion rather than treating the active policy manifests as an external side table.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Observable history and filtration]
Time is ordered as follows. At the beginning of period $t$, the public state $C_t$ is available and the proposal $u_t$ must be chosen using only that information. After the action is issued and period-$t$ visible randomness is realized, the system emits the replay-visible public record
\[
o_{t+1}=\Obs(z_t,u_t,\xi_t),
\]
where $\xi_t$ collects visible randomness and metadata. The observable history available at decision time $t$ is therefore
\[
H_t^{\Obs}\Defeq (o_1,o_2,\dots,o_t),
\]
with $H_0^{\Obs}$ empty. Because each $C_s$ already contains the accumulated public observation state $H_s^{\Obs}$, the pre-decision public filtration is
\[
\mathcal F_t\Defeq \sigma\!\bigl(C_0,\dots,C_t\bigr).
\]
An online decision rule at time $t$ is any $\mathcal F_t$-measurable map. The post-decision, post-record sigma-field is
\[
\mathcal F_t^{+}\Defeq \sigma(\mathcal F_t,o_{t+1}),
\]
so current-period actions may affect $o_{t+1}$ but not the information set used to choose $u_t$.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[System dynamics]
The recursive loop is modeled by
\begin{align}
  x_{t+1} &= F_t(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,u_t,h_t,\Pi_t,\xi_t), \label{eq:x_dynamics}\\
  e_{t+1} &= G_t(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,u_t,h_t,\Pi_t,\zeta_t), \label{eq:e_dynamics}\\
  m_{t+1} &= M_t(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,u_t,h_t,\Pi_t,\omega_t), \label{eq:m_dynamics}\\
  q_{t+1} &= \bigl[q_t + \lambda_t^{\mathrm{prop}} - \mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}\bigr]_+, \label{eq:q_dynamics}\\
  r_{t+1} &= H_t(r_t,x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,u_t,h_t,\Pi_t,\nu_t), \label{eq:r_dynamics}\\
  h_{t+1} &= U_t(h_t,u_t,\Pi_t,\chi_t), \label{eq:h_dynamics}\\
  \Pi_{t+1} &= P_t(\Pi_t,x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,r_t,u_t,h_t,\varpi_t). \label{eq:pi_dynamics}
\end{align}
The key feature is that both the evaluator state in \eqref{eq:e_dynamics} and the public policy state in \eqref{eq:pi_dynamics} evolve endogenously. The ruler is therefore part of the state rather than an external constant.
\end{definition}

\subsection{Standing assumptions}
\begin{assumption}[Finite verification capacity]\label{ass:finite_ver}
There exists $\bar\mu<\infty$ such that $0\le \mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}\le \bar\mu$ for all $t$.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[No privileged semantic judge]\label{ass:no_meta}
All admit/reject decisions must be representable through a public or replayable admissibility relation. No external privileged semantic oracle is available.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Replayable proposals]\label{ass:replayable}
Each self-edit proposal is accompanied by a replay artifact, declared evaluation cost, and version diff.
\end{assumption}

\begin{assumption}[Two-speed verification]\label{ass:two_speed}
A subset of proposals can be routed to a slower challenge process with higher-fidelity evaluation. The challenge process may be delayed but is not directly editable by the same proposal it evaluates.
\end{assumption}

\subsection{Ontology and dependency map}
The paper uses four layers that should not be conflated. Table~\ref{tab:ontology_map} records the intended role of the main object classes.

\begin{table}[H]
\centering
\small
\begin{tabularx}{\textwidth}{>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.18\textwidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.2\textwidth}>{\raggedright\arraybackslash}p{0.26\textwidth}X}
\toprule
Layer & Object type & Typical examples & Role in the theory \\
\midrule
Primitive observable & directly logged or replay-reconstructed state & $C_t$, manifests, queue counters, protected budgets, challenge logs & admissibility may depend on these without further transport assumptions \\
Replayably derived conservative envelope & deterministic or proof-carrying function of observables & $K_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$, $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$, $\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}$, $r_t^{\mathrm{pub}}$, service floors & these are allowed at the gate only when published as conservative lower/upper certificates \\
Operational target & class- or witness-conditional public target defined by the active design & $\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{chal}}$, $\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}$, $\Phi_t$, $\Phi_t^{\mathrm{net}}$ & these are admission-facing objects; they need not equal cohort-specific oracle quantities \\
Latent / oracle object & not directly admissible without extra bridges & cohort-specific retained margin $\mathcal M_t(h)$, uncaptured semantic directions, full counterfactual stable gain & these appear only through explicit homogeneity, transport, or witness-comparison assumptions \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabularx}
\caption{Ontology map for the main layers. The positive theorems operate on replayable observables, conservative envelopes, and explicit witness-comparison contracts; they do not license replacing those objects by unlogged latent quantities.}
\label{tab:ontology_map}
\end{table}

\section{Canonical Admissibility Instance}
The theory is abstract, but the admissibility relation cannot remain an empty symbol.

\begin{definition}[Canonical admissibility instance]\label{def:admissibility}
Fix a task or query class $\mathfrak q$ and a verification budget $b$. A proposal $u_t$ is \emph{$(\mathfrak q,b)$-admissible} at time $t$, written
\[
u_t\in\mathcal A_{\mathfrak q,b}(C_t),
\]
if and only if all of the following hold:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item at least one active parser/evaluator configuration replays the proposal and artifact successfully;
  \item the declared replay-and-check cost is at most $b$;
  \item replay execution produces no undefined side effect on the public state;
  \item any proposal that directly edits evaluator parameters, benchmark definitions, or parser/schema configuration is routed to a challenge lane before unrestricted promotion;
  \item any proposal that merges or summarizes prior evidence must either carry a context-preservation certificate or be typed into a non-evidentiary narrative lane.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}
This admissibility instance is not claimed to be unique. It is a canonical public-budgeted example that makes the rest of the paper operational.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Operational certificates and margins]\label{def:operational_certificates}
A \emph{context-preservation certificate} for a summary artifact $s$ is a replayable witness bundle proving that the summary retains the task-relevant support set declared by policy, including source identifiers, extraction rules, and omission budget. The \emph{parser-family agreement} of an item $x$ at time $t$ is a public scalar
\[
A_t^{\mathrm{parse}}(x)\in[0,1]
\]
measuring weighted agreement across the active parser family on the item's decoded content and type. The \emph{challenge-lane safety margin}, \emph{promotion-lane safety margin}, and \emph{proof-lane safety margin} are the public slacks
\[
S_t^{\mathrm{chal}}\Defeq \mu_t^{\mathrm{chal}}-\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{chal}},\qquad
S_t^{\mathrm{prom}}\Defeq \mu_t^{\mathrm{prom}}-\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{prom}},\qquad
S_t^{\mathrm{proof}}\Defeq \mu_t^{\mathrm{proof}}-\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{proof}},
\]
where $\mu_t^{\mathrm{chal}},\mu_t^{\mathrm{prom}},\mu_t^{\mathrm{proof}}$ are the effective protected service capacities of the challenge, promotion, and richer-proof lanes, and $\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{chal}},\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{prom}},\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{proof}}$ are their predictable routed loads. Finally, let
\[
r_t^{\mathrm{pub}}\ge 0
\]
denote the \emph{published debt-burden envelope}: a replayably designated public upper envelope on the currently committed unresolved governance debt entering Interface B at epoch $t$ (for example aggregate outstanding debt plus any certified issuance-time carryover bound on the active deployment horizon). The envelope is part of the published regime description rather than the supremum over all admissible upper bounds; lower $r_t^{\mathrm{pub}}$ helps admission. Promotion and proof-routing rules may require lower bounds on $A_t^{\mathrm{parse}}(x)$ and on the relevant lane-safety margins.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Replay compatibility margin, semantic retention, and refreezing rule]\label{def:replay_margin}
For a replay artifact $a$ archived at time $\tau$, let
\[
G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}(a)\in[0,1]
\]
be the public replay-compatibility score of $a$ under the active parser family, build manifest, and environment resolver at time $t\ge \tau$. A policy maintains a \emph{replay floor} $g_{\min}\in(0,1]$ if every contradiction-bearing or evidentiary artifact retained for future audit satisfies
\[
G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}(a)\ge g_{\min}.
\]
When an update replaces $a$ by a fresh replay bundle $a'$, let
\[
S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a')\in[0,1]
\]
be the \emph{public lower envelope} on semantic retention returned by the active replayable audit family for the declared claim, support set, and typing constraints under the active parser/environment regime. The associated translation loss is
\[
\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a')\Defeq 1-S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a').
\]
A parser or environment update is said to \emph{refreeze} an artifact when it emits a fresh replay bundle $a'$ with
\[
G_{t+1}^{\mathrm{replay}}(a')\ge g_{\min}
\]
and an audited semantic-retention envelope $S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a')\ge s_{\min}$ for some policy floor $s_{\min}\in(0,1]$. Exact lossless meaning preservation is \emph{not} assumed; refreezing restores replayability while exposing translation loss as an explicit audited quantity. Here ``public'' does not mean oracle-given: it means replayable under the currently declared audit family, whose own diversity and capture risk are analyzed later.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[No-meta reading of semantic retention]\label{rem:no_meta_semantics}
Throughout the paper, semantic-retention quantities are \emph{audit-family-relative lower envelopes}. They certify retention only relative to the declared replayable probe family, parser family, support-set contract, and typing rules active at audit time. The theory therefore does \emph{not} assume access to oracle semantics. What it assumes is weaker and operational: if the published audit family cannot distinguish two artifacts, the paper does not pretend that an external judge silently can.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Effective evidentiary weight under refreezing]\label{def:effective_weight}
Fix an evidentiary or contradiction-bearing artifact lineage
\[
a_0\rightsquigarrow a_1\rightsquigarrow \cdots \rightsquigarrow a_j\rightsquigarrow \cdots
\]
where each arrow denotes an admissible refreezing event certified under Definition~\ref{def:replay_margin}. Let $W_0(a_0)>0$ be the policy-issued initial evidentiary weight of the root artifact, incorporating any provenance, scope, or contradiction-tag weight attached at issuance. For any descendant artifact $a_j$ active at time $t$, define its \emph{effective evidentiary weight} by
\[
W_t^{\mathrm{eff}}(a_j)\Defeq W_0(a_0)\prod_{\ell=0}^{j-1} S_{t_\ell}^{\mathrm{sem}}(a_\ell\rightsquigarrow a_{\ell+1}),
\]
where $t_\ell$ is the replayable time of the $\ell$-th refreezing step on the lineage. If $a$ has never been refrozen, then $W_t^{\mathrm{eff}}(a)=W_0(a)$. Thus replay-floor preservation and semantic-retention loss are separated: replayability can be restored by refreezing while effective evidentiary force may still decay multiplicatively along the lineage.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Adversarial audit families and endogenous envelopes]\label{def:audit_family}
A \emph{shadow audit family} at time $t$ is a finite set of delayed evaluators
\[
\mathfrak S_t=\{\Shadow^{(1)},\dots,\Shadow^{(M_t)}\}
\]
with replayable manifests, parser/build identities, memory roots, and challenge routes. For each family member $m$ active at the \emph{issuance time} $\tau$ of a challenged cohort, let
\[
\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow^{(m)}}(u)
\]
denote the replayable score assigned at horizon $h$ to the coupled counterfactual world in which the issuance-time intervention is $U_\tau=u$ and every later update follows the declared challenge-lane continuation interface, with lane $m$ compared through its replayably transported descendants if the shadow family is later refreshed. Thus each cohort is evaluated against the transported descendants of its \emph{issuance-time} shadow family rather than against whichever extra lanes may have been added later. When a single family-level score is needed, the public canonical aggregate is
\[
\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow}(u)\Defeq \operatorname{Agg}^{(\tau)}_{m\le M_\tau}\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow^{(m)}}(u),
\]
where $\operatorname{Agg}^{(\tau)}$ is a replayable policy-declared issuance-time aggregator such as a median, trimmed mean, or designated protected-subfamily mean. If $M_\tau=0$, no shadow certificate exists for that cohort and we adopt the conservative conventions
\[
\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow}(u)\Defeq 0,
\qquad
\Delta_{\tau,h}^{\mathrm{xs}}\Defeq +\infty.
\]
Likewise a \emph{refreezing audit family}
\[
\mathfrak R_t=\{\Replay^{(1)},\dots,\Replay^{(N_t)}\}
\]
returns semantic-retention scores for candidate refreezings. For a challenged cohort issued at time $\tau$ with issued intervention $u_\tau$, define the cross-shadow disagreement radius by
\[
\Delta_{\tau,h}^{\mathrm{xs}}\Defeq
\begin{cases}
\max\limits_{m,m'\le M_\tau}
\left|
\begin{aligned}
&\bigl(\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow^{(m)}}(u_\tau)-\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow^{(m)}}(0)\bigr)\\
&\qquad-\bigl(\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow^{(m')}}(u_\tau)-\widehat V_{\tau+h}^{\Shadow^{(m')}}(0)\bigr)
\end{aligned}
\right|, & M_\tau\ge 1,\\[1.0ex]
+\infty, & M_\tau=0,
\end{cases}
\]
and for a refreezing candidate $a\rightsquigarrow a'$ let
\[
\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a')\Defeq
\begin{cases}
\min\limits_{n\le N_t} S_{t,n}^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a'), & N_t\ge 1,\\[0.8ex]
0, & N_t=0,
\end{cases}
\]
be the endogenous semantic-retention floor across the refreezing family. Let
\[
\Xi_t^{\Shadow}\ge 0,
\qquad
\Xi_t^{\Replay}\ge 0
\]
be public lower envelopes on \emph{audit diversity reserve}, computed from provenance-disjointness, implementation overlap, seed separation, memory-root separation, and declared writable scope. Finally let $A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}\ge0$ be a public upper envelope on the accepted proposal's \emph{manifest-preserving} effective attack reach over the currently active audit family through declared writable or otherwise logged common-cause channels. Whenever a theorem compares attack reach to a family-specific diversity reserve, policy must also publish replayable monotone calibration maps $\phi_t^{\Shadow},\phi_t^{\Replay}:\R_+\to\R_+$ that convert the generic attack-reach envelope into the effective cover units used by the corresponding shadow and replay families. All of these are observable-or-replayable functions of manifests and logs, not oracle constants.
\end{definition}


\begin{remark}[Roles of the audit objects]\label{rem:audit_roles}
The notation is intentionally layered. $\mathfrak S_t$ and $\mathfrak R_t$ denote the active shadow and refreezing \emph{families}; $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}$ denotes the currently retained audit-bearing artifact set; and any policy-level admissibility or stress-test functional built from those objects is then a derived observable. Families certify or challenge artifacts, while the retained audit set is the object whose replayability, effective weight, routing sensitivity, and semantic diversity must remain live. This separation matters because family capture and artifact decay are distinct failure modes.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Constructive proxy templates for public envelopes]\label{rem:proxy_templates}
The paper's public envelopes are intended to be conservative wrappers, not mysterious gifts. A typical implementation computes $\Xi_t^{\Shadow}$ and $\Xi_t^{\Replay}$ as lower bounds on provenance-separated diversity via overlap graphs, writable-scope exclusions, seed-separation checks, and min-cut style disjointness certificates across the active audit families. A typical upper envelope $A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}$ is built from declared writable scope, dependency closure, shared allocator or routing control, and any \emph{manifest-preserving} common-cause channels exposed by the active build and memory roots; covert raw-input channels that are not represented in the public manifest are intentionally excluded and must instead be handled by the scrubber layer below. The family-specific calibrations $\phi_t^{\Shadow}$ and $\phi_t^{\Replay}$ then convert that generic attack envelope into effective common-cause cover units comparable to the reserves $\Xi_t^{\Shadow}$ and $\Xi_t^{\Replay}$. A typical intervention-capacity lower envelope $\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)$ is obtained from conservative intervention-response probes on admissible replays, minimum guaranteed effect on declared governance outputs, or other algorithmic-causal surrogates that are monotone under richer attack surfaces. Likewise the endogenous semantic floor $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$ is obtained by taking the minimum certified retention score across a provenance-separated replay family. The theorems therefore apply to whichever conservative proxy family policy actually publishes; the burden is not to guess the true latent quantity, but to expose a replayable envelope whose failure can be audited.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Slack-robust proxy substitution]\label{prop:proxy_gap}
Fix any admission or governance clause that is coordinatewise nondecreasing in a vector of helpful latent coordinates $u\in\R^p$ and coordinatewise nonincreasing in a vector of burden latent coordinates $b\in\R^q$. Suppose policy publishes replayable proxy coordinates $\hat u,\hat b$ together with replayable error envelopes $\eps^u\in\R_+^p$ and $\eps^b\in\R_+^q$ such that
\[
\hat u\le u\le \hat u+\eps^u,
\qquad
\hat b-\eps^b\le b\le \hat b
\]
coordinatewise. Then any certificate proved using the tightened proxy-side thresholds
\[
\hat u\ge \underline u+\eps^u,
\qquad
\hat b\le \bar b-\eps^b
\]
is sound for the corresponding latent thresholds $u\ge \underline u$ and $b\le \bar b$. Conversely, if the available proxy slack fails to dominate the published error envelopes, the proxy family is insufficient to certify the latent clause by itself.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
From $u\ge \hat u$ and $u\le \hat u+\eps^u$, the tightened helpful-side threshold $\hat u\ge \underline u+\eps^u$ implies $u\ge \underline u$ coordinatewise. From $b\le \hat b$ and $b\ge \hat b-\eps^b$, the tightened burden-side threshold $\hat b\le \bar b-\eps^b$ implies $b\le \bar b$ coordinatewise. Monotonicity of the clause in the helpful and burden coordinates then yields soundness. If the available slack is smaller than the error envelopes, a proxy certificate can no longer guarantee the latent inequalities, so the clause becomes operationally inconclusive rather than certified.
\end{proof}


\begin{definition}[Tiered observable proxies and gate discipline]\label{def:proxy_tiers}
Observable governance proxies are partitioned into three tiers.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(T\arabic*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item \textbf{Tier 1: direct metered observables.} These are directly logged physical or syntactic quantities such as queue lengths, hashes, manifests, wall-clock counters, energy counters, attested allocator shares, and typed lane occupancies.
  \item \textbf{Tier 2: proof-carrying derived quantities.} These are replayably derived from Tier-1 objects together with explicit certificates, for example service lower bounds, replay floors, transport-distortion bounds, verified allocator shares, and challenge-propensity lower bounds.
  \item \textbf{Tier 3: routing heuristics.} These are conservative but model-laden prioritization or search signals such as semantic-similarity alarms, approximate attack-reach heuristics, contradiction novelty scores, or cheap retrieval-salience surrogates.
\end{enumerate}
A policy satisfies the \emph{gate discipline} if fast admission, deployment rejection, debt thresholds, and governance-safety thresholds may depend only on Tier-1 and Tier-2 quantities together with the slack-robust substitution rule of Proposition~\ref{prop:proxy_gap}. Tier-3 quantities may influence routing, challenge sampling, reserve triage, audit prioritization, and alerting, but may not by themselves trigger semantic deployment or semantic rejection.
\end{definition}

\begin{corollary}[Conservative envelopes do not collapse into policy fiat under gate discipline]\label{cor:proxy_tiers}
Under Definition~\ref{def:proxy_tiers}, a published conservative envelope can affect fast deployment only if it is either directly metered or replayably derived from directly metered quantities with an explicit proof-carrying error budget. Consequently heuristic routing signals may steer attention but cannot by themselves manufacture admissibility.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from the gate discipline: Tier-3 quantities are excluded from deployment and rejection thresholds by definition, while Tier-1 and Tier-2 quantities are constrained by direct logging or proof-carrying derivation together with Proposition~\ref{prop:proxy_gap}.
\end{proof}
\section{Core Definitions}
\begin{definition}[Claimed improvement]\label{def:claimed_improvement}
Let $\Theta_t^{\mathrm{fast}}$ denote the frozen issuance-time fast-evaluation interface, consisting of the evaluator state $e_t$ together with the parser choice, retrieval contract, and other fast-scoring manifest objects declared in $\Pi_t$ that policy treats as part of the immediate ruler. Write
\[
J_t^{\mathrm{fast}}(x,m)\Defeq J(x,m;\Theta_t^{\mathrm{fast}})
\]
for the resulting fast public evaluator score. The proposal issued at time $t$ has claimed improvement
\[
\Delta_t^{\mathrm{claim}}\Defeq J_t^{\mathrm{fast}}(x_{t+1},m_{t+1})-J_t^{\mathrm{fast}}(x_t,m_t).
\]
The interface $\Theta_t^{\mathrm{fast}}$ is held fixed in this comparison so that the claim isolates the local edit from subsequent evaluator drift. If the proposal explicitly challenges part of the fast interface itself, then claimed improvement is computed relative to the pre-edit interface and the interface edit must be certified separately through comparator compatibility. Claimed improvement is therefore a frozen-interface diagnostic, not a license to count immediate score changes caused only by rewriting the ruler.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Yardstick drift]\label{def:yardstick_drift}
The one-step endogenous yardstick drift is
\[
D_t^{\mathrm{yard}}\Defeq \norm{e_{t+1}-e_t},
\]
and the cumulative drift over horizon $h\ge1$ is
\[
\mathcal D_t(h)\Defeq \sum_{s=t}^{t+h-1} D_s^{\mathrm{yard}}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Comparator certificates for ruler edits]\label{def:comp_cert}
At decision epoch $t$, the replayable post-$t$ environment is represented by a typed exogenous-noise process
\[
W_s=(W_s^{\mathrm{pub}},W_s^{\mathrm{prot}},W_s^{\mathrm{exo}},W_s^{\mathrm{endo}}),\qquad s\ge t,
\]
where $W^{\mathrm{pub}}$ is replay-coupled public randomness, $W^{\mathrm{prot}}$ is protected audit randomness whose generator root and admissible law family are declared but whose realized bits may remain hidden from the proposal writer, $W^{\mathrm{exo}}$ is intervention-exogenous environment noise that is required to be coupled pathwise across the compared worlds, and $W^{\mathrm{endo}}$ is endogenous environment response generated only through the declared state-mediated transition kernels and therefore allowed to differ because the compared state paths differ. An \emph{interface-congruence certificate} publishes a common transition representation
\[
z_{s+1}=F_s(z_s,U_s,W_s)
\]
on a shared continuation skeleton together with an explicit declaration of which typed noise coordinates are coupled exactly, which are law-coupled, which admissible state-mediated response kernel governs $W^{\mathrm{endo}}$, and any replayable comparison-distortion budgets. A \emph{state-lift certificate} is admissible only if it provides a replayable lift map $L_t$ and projection $P_t$ satisfying all of the following: (i) $P_t\circ L_t$ preserves the pre-edit public state; (ii) all public observables and all public coordinates entering admissibility are preserved at issuance and thereafter tracked with explicit replayable distortion budgets; (iii) the lift-induced policy-manifold drift is uniformly upper-bounded in the published comparison coordinates; (iv) lift-only latent coordinates are not allowed to enter later admission certificates except through declared transported observables and public Lipschitz distortion budgets; and (v) no new probe family introduced by the lift may enter admission or challenge design without its own replayable transport certificate. Thus state augmentation cannot be used to trivialize comparator compatibility by adding private bookkeeping coordinates that later re-enter certification directly.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Public continuation skeleton and comparator-compatible ruler edits]\label{def:continuation_skeleton}
Let
\[
\Pi_t^{\mathrm{cont}}
\Defeq
\bigl(\mathcal K_t^{\mathrm{adm}},\mathcal K_t^{\mathrm{route}},\mathcal K_t^{\mathrm{chal}},\mathcal K_t^{\mathrm{pf}},\mathcal K_t^{\mathrm{alloc}},\mathcal K_t^{\mathrm{dyn}},F_{t:},\mathfrak s_t\bigr)
\]
denote the \emph{public continuation skeleton}, where the components are respectively the replayable downstream admission, routing, challenge, proof-checking, allocator, and state-update kernels together with the typed transition family $F_{t:}$ and the public seed schedule $\mathfrak s_t$ used to couple replay-visible randomness across counterfactual replays. Equality of continuation skeletons means componentwise equality of these logged kernels, transition families, and the replay seed schedule. Hidden scrubber randomness is a different typed object and is not part of $\mathfrak s_t$.

A proposal is \emph{comparator-compatible} for stable-gain analysis if both $\ReplayCF(U_t=u_t)$ and $\ReplayCF(U_t=0)$ are feasible at the current public state and there exists a nonempty \emph{finite replayably enumerated} family
\[
\mathfrak C_t(u_t)=\{c_t^{(1)},\dots,c_t^{(N_t(u_t))}\},\qquad 1\le N_t(u_t)<\infty,
\]
of comparator witnesses. Each witness $c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$ consists of coupled post-$t$ worlds generated on the same logged continuation skeleton, sharing the same $W^{\mathrm{pub}}$ path and the same $W^{\mathrm{exo}}$ path exactly, while $W^{\mathrm{prot}}$ is either exactly coupled or law-coupled according to the declared audit contract and $W^{\mathrm{endo}}$ is generated by a replayably published state-mediated response kernel. Each witness additionally carries a replayable comparison-distortion budget $\varepsilon_{t,s}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c)$ on the public observables and admission coordinates. The comparison is \emph{exact} when those distortion budgets vanish identically; otherwise it is an \emph{approximate comparator} or replayable $\varepsilon$-bisimulation comparator. The \emph{comparator diameter}
\[
\operatorname{diam}^{\mathrm{cmp}}_{t,H}(u_t)
\Defeq
\max_{c,c'\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)}\sum_{s=1}^{H}\beta^{s-1}\bigl|\varepsilon_{t,s}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c)-\varepsilon_{t,s}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c')\bigr|
\]
is itself a replayable governance-burden term and may be thresholded or priced by policy; when $H=\infty$, this definition is used only under the manifest clause that the weighted comparator-distortion series is absolutely summable. Ruler edits are comparator-compatible only when policy publishes an interface-congruence certificate or constrained state-lift certificate in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:comp_cert}, showing that the edited ruler is represented as a state update inside the shared skeleton rather than as a counterfactual-specific replacement of the comparison machinery.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Scope of comparator compatibility]\label{rem:comp_scope}
Comparator compatibility is intentionally narrower than unrestricted self-rewrite. It covers edits whose compared worlds can be embedded in a shared replayable continuation skeleton, including many evaluator, parser, routing, memory, and policy edits once an interface-congruence or state-lift certificate is published. It does not by itself cover arbitrary rewrites of the ambient transition-law class when no such shared skeleton is available. Those cases require an additional meta-dynamics layer and lie outside the present stability claims.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Public dominating envelope for infinite-horizon stable gain]\label{def:dominating_envelope}
Fix an issuance time $t$, a feasible intervention $u_t$, and a discount factor $\beta\in(0,1)$. For any admissible comparator witness $c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$, let $\{(z_{t+s}^{u_t,c},z_{t+s}^{0,c})\}_{s\ge1}$ be the coupled post-intervention trajectories generated by the shared continuation skeleton of Definition~\ref{def:continuation_skeleton}. For the infinite-horizon case $H=\infty$, a \emph{public dominating envelope} is any replayable predictable sequence $M_{t,s}^{\mathrm{dom}}\ge 0$ such that
\[
\abs{V(z_{t+s}^{u_t,c})-V(z_{t+s}^{0,c})}\le M_{t,s}^{\mathrm{dom}}
\qquad\text{almost surely for all }s\ge 1\text{ and all }c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t),
\]
and
\[
\E\!\left[\sum_{s=1}^{\infty}\beta^{s-1}M_{t,s}^{\mathrm{dom}}\middle|\mathcal F_t\right]<\infty.
\]
This object supplies the conditional absolute-integrability witness required to define infinite-horizon discounted stable gain without appealing to an unlogged analytic assumption.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Discounted stable gain, stable improvement, governance safety, and full admissibility]\label{def:full_admissibility}
Fix horizon $H\in\N\cup\{\infty\}$ and discount factor $\beta\in(0,1]$, with $\beta<1$ whenever $H=\infty$. Let $V(x,m,h)$ be a slower long-run utility surrogate that does not depend directly on the fast evaluator state, and by abuse of notation write
\[
V(z)\Defeq V(x,m,h)\qquad\text{for }z=(x,e,m,q,r,h,\Pi).
\]
Write $\mathsf{Comp}_t(u_t)\in\{0,1\}$ for the public comparator-compatibility predicate induced by Definition~\ref{def:continuation_skeleton}. Stable-gain comparison uses only comparator-compatible proposals. For each such proposal, let $\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$ be the replayably published family of admissible comparator witnesses from Definition~\ref{def:continuation_skeleton}. For every witness $c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$, let $z_{t+s}^{u_t,c}$ and $z_{t+s}^{0,c}$ denote the resulting coupled trajectories and let $\delta_{t,s}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c)\ge 0$ be the declared comparison-distortion budget on the public observables and admissibility coordinates at lag $s$. Because $\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$ is finite and replayably enumerated, the lower and upper oracle endpoints below are literal minima and maxima over a finite family rather than essential envelopes.

The discounted stable-gain \emph{oracle interval} of the proposal issued at time $t$ is
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta,\mathrm{lo}}(u_t)
\Defeq
\min_{c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)}
\E\left[
\sum_{s=1}^{H}\beta^{s-1}\bigl(V(z_{t+s}^{u_t,c})-V(z_{t+s}^{0,c})\bigr)
\middle|\mathcal F_t
\right],
\]
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta,\mathrm{hi}}(u_t)
\Defeq
\max_{c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)}
\E\left[
\sum_{s=1}^{H}\beta^{s-1}\bigl(V(z_{t+s}^{u_t,c})-V(z_{t+s}^{0,c})\bigr)
\middle|\mathcal F_t
\right].
\]
When the comparator is exact, the interval collapses to a point. Throughout the remainder of the paper,
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)\Defeq \mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta,\mathrm{lo}}(u_t)
\]
denotes the lower oracle endpoint, because admission is intentionally based on the worst replayably admissible comparator witness rather than on a hidden favorable coupling choice. When $H=\infty$, each witness is additionally assumed to satisfy conditional absolute integrability under a public dominating envelope in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:dominating_envelope}. Let
\[
\underline{\mathcal G}_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)
\]
denote any replayable lower certificate for $\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)$ published under the active admission policy. The intended reading is three-layered: the full oracle interval records comparator ambiguity, the lower oracle endpoint is the robust theoretical target, and $\underline{\mathcal G}_{t,H}^{\beta}$ is the operational object allowed to enter admission.

Let $\bar\delta_r(C_t)\ge 0$ be the policy debt threshold and define the proposal-local peak debt over horizon $H$ by
\[
\eta_{t,H}^{\max}(u_t)\Defeq \sup_{0\le s\le H}\eta_{t,t+s},
\]
with the natural infinite-horizon supremum $\sup_{s\ge 0}\eta_{t,t+s}$ when $H=\infty$. In particular, the issuance-time escrow liability $\eta_{t,t}$ is part of the stable-improvement gate rather than an auxiliary side remark.

Let $\mathsf{BaseAdm}_t(u_t)\in\{0,1\}$ denote the public base-admissibility predicate induced by the active canonical admission policy at time $t$, including replay success, declared cost budget, side-effect well-definedness, mandatory challenge routing for ruler edits, and summary typing or context-preservation clauses. A proposal at time $t$ is an \emph{$(H,\beta)$-oracle stable improvement} if
\[
\mathsf{Comp}_t(u_t)=1,
\qquad
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)\ge 0,
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\eta_{t,H}^{\max}(u_t)\le \bar\delta_r(C_t).
\]
It is an \emph{$(H,\beta)$-certified stable improvement} if
\[
\mathsf{Comp}_t(u_t)=1,
\qquad
\underline{\mathcal G}_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)\ge 0,
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\eta_{t,H}^{\max}(u_t)\le \bar\delta_r(C_t).
\]
Let $\mathsf{GovSafe}_{t,H}(u_t)\in\{0,1\}$ denote the public governance-safety predicate asserting that the active non-gain governance clauses remain satisfied on the same horizon, including any required queue slack, replay floor, contradiction-reserve, heterodoxy-routing, proof-budget, and resource-escrow margins declared by policy. A proposal is an \emph{$(H,\beta)$-full admissible improvement} if
\[
\mathsf{BaseAdm}_t(u_t)=1,\qquad
u_t\text{ is an }(H,\beta)\text{-certified stable improvement},\qquad
\mathsf{GovSafe}_{t,H}(u_t)=1.
\]
This full-admissibility notion is an \emph{immediate-deployment} notion at epoch $t$: it concerns proposals whose current action is semantic deployment into the target lane under the active manifest and thresholds. Proposals that are admitted only to nondeployment actions such as challenge routing, richer-proof escalation, or sandboxing may be lane-admissible without yet being fully admissible in this immediate-deployment sense; they enter the productive frontier only after the delayed certificates and review actions required for deployment have been completed.

For brevity, the remainder of the paper uses ``stable improvement'' for the certified notion and qualifies the oracle notion explicitly when needed. It uses ``admissible improvement'' to mean the full immediate-deployment notion unless explicitly qualified otherwise.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Why $V$ excludes fast governance variables]\label{rem:V_layering}
The surrogate $V$ is intentionally layered away from the fast evaluator state and from explicit governance variables such as queue backlog, replay fragility, debt, or policy-manifest drift. The reason is not that these quantities are normatively irrelevant, but that they are already enforced through $\mathsf{BaseAdm}$ and $\mathsf{GovSafe}$. Folding them directly into $V$ would blur the distinction between ``this edit has long-run task value'' and ``this edit preserves the governability of the loop,'' thereby double-counting governance failures. Applications that genuinely want queue, debt, or policy drift inside welfare may absorb them into $h_t$ or replace $V$ by a richer long-run functional, provided the same layer separation is made explicit.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Structural blast radius, causal intervention capacity, and systemic risk bond]\label{def:blast_radius}
For a proposal $u_t$, let $\mathcal W_t(u_t)$ be its declared writable module set and let $\operatorname{Dep}_t(\mathcal W_t(u_t))$ be the replayable dependency closure of that set under the currently declared code, parser, evaluator, and memory manifests. Let $\chi_t^{\mathrm{priv}}(u_t)\ge 0$ be a public privilege multiplier that increases when the proposal can directly modify high-leverage substrates such as evaluator code, parser registries, refreezing policies, routing policies, memory-lane transition logic, or physical-resource allocators. A \emph{causal intervention capacity lower envelope} is any replayable public quantity
\[
\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)\ge 0
\]
that lower-bounds the proposal's potential output-side or governance-side influence under admissible replays, for example through conservative intervention-response envelopes, minimum-description-length proxies, or algorithmic-causal surrogates computed across the active shadow/replay family. A \emph{systemic risk bond} is any replayable lower envelope
\[
\mathcal B_t(u_t)\ge 0
\]
that is monotone in writable scope, dependency closure, privilege level, and causal intervention capacity. One canonical robust instance is
\[
\mathcal B_t(u_t)
\Defeq
\max\!\left\{
\lambda_W |\mathcal W_t(u_t)|
+\lambda_D |\operatorname{Dep}_t(\mathcal W_t(u_t))|
+\lambda_P \chi_t^{\mathrm{priv}}(u_t),\,
\lambda_C \Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)
\right\},
\]
with public policy weights $\lambda_W,\lambda_D,\lambda_P,\lambda_C\ge 0$. The role of $\mathcal B_t(u_t)$ is not to predict exact harm, but to impose a proposal-local lower bound on downside exposure that cannot be driven to zero merely by under-reporting claimed upside or by topologically compressing a globally influential rewrite into a single apparent module.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Operational meaning of the intervention-capacity envelope]\label{rem:cic_proxy}
$\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)$ is allowed to be conservative. In practice it may be instantiated by minimum guaranteed effect on declared governance outputs under admissible perturbation probes, by a lower confidence bound on intervention-response magnitude across the active shadow and replay families, or by other monotone proxies that cannot be made small merely by renaming modules. The theorem layer needs only a replayable lower envelope; it does not require exact causal identification.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Cohort-escrow error debt]\label{def:cohort_escrow}
For each proposal cohort $\tau$, let $g_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}}\ge 0$ denote the \emph{cumulative gross matched retirement} credited by review time $t\ge \tau$, with $t\mapsto g_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}}$ nondecreasing and $g_{\tau,\tau}^{\mathrm{chal}}=0$. Retirement credit is allowed only for replayably matched repair certificates, verified rollback-cost reductions, or persistent hazard-reduction certificates; a superficial score recovery that leaves the repair or hazard reserve unresolved does not count as retirement. Let $a_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{sec}}\ge 0$ denote \emph{secondary liability} conservatively charged back to the parent cohort between times $t-1$ and $t$; this term captures repair-induced regressions or parser/environment migrations that were triggered by attempts to neutralize the parent cohort. Let $b_{\tau,t}\ge0$ be a nonnegative backlog-attribution kernel satisfying
\[
\sum_{\tau\le t} b_{\tau,t}\le q_t,
\]
and let $\rho_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{ret}}\in[0,1]$ be a predictable retirement fraction capturing only the verified reserve-reduction actions described above. Let $U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}\ge 0$ be a replayable upper envelope on repair or rollback cost required to neutralize the cohort under the active deployment scope, and let $U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}}\ge 0$ be a replayable upper envelope on persistent unresolved hazard cost under the same scope. The proposal-local liability stock is initialized by the \emph{unresolved downside reserve}
\[
\eta_{\tau,\tau}=\mathcal B_{\tau}(u_{\tau})+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}},
\]
where $\mathcal B_{\tau}(u_{\tau})$ is the systemic risk bond from Definition~\ref{def:blast_radius}, and it evolves as
\[
\eta_{\tau,t+1}
=
\Bigl[
(1-\rho_{\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{ret}})\alpha_r \eta_{\tau,t}
-
\bigl(g_{\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{chal}}-g_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}}\bigr)
+
a_{\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{sec}}
+
\lambda_q b_{\tau,t}
\Bigr]_+,
\qquad t\ge \tau,
\]
where $\alpha_r\in[0,1]$ and $\lambda_q\ge0$. Aggregate error debt is then
\[
r_t\Defeq \sum_{\tau<t}\eta_{\tau,t}.
\]
By convention, $r_t$ is the \emph{pre-admission actionable stock} visible when deciding whether to admit the time-$t$ proposal. Newly issued cohort-$t$ liability therefore enters the stock beginning at $r_{t+1}$, so the indexing is intentional rather than an off-by-one omission.
This accounting has five important properties. First, matched challenge retirement acts only inside the cohort that generated the claim, so cross-cohort masking is excluded by construction. Second, explicit retirement shrinks already accumulated stock rather than merely blocking future accrual. Third, repair-induced regressions are not hidden by making the matched-retirement process nonmonotone; they enter transparently through the secondary-liability term $a_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{sec}}$ or, equivalently, via newborn derived cohorts. Fourth, $\alpha_r<1$ is an \emph{operational relevance discount}, not an epistemic erasure rule: evidence, contradiction tags, and replay artifacts can still be preserved indefinitely, while the liability stock tracks only the burden that remains actionable for the current loop. Fifth, the initial reserve is coherent downside accounting: it lower-bounds systemic reach, repair cost, and persistent hazard cost instead of depending on optimistic positive claims. The strict-conservation case $\alpha_r=1$ is treated separately below.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Finite active cohort support]\label{ass:finite_active_cohorts}
For every review time $t$, only finitely many proposal cohorts carry nonzero actionable liability, equivalently
\[
\#\{\tau<t:\eta_{\tau,t}>0\}<\infty,
\]
or, more generally, the policy exposes a replayable truncation rule ensuring
\[
r_t=\sum_{\tau<t}\eta_{\tau,t}<\infty
\qquad\text{almost surely for every }t.
\]
This assumption prevents aggregate debt from becoming a formal divergent series rather than a state variable.
\end{assumption}

\begin{remark}[Why monotone gross retirement is not a no-regression assumption]
The monotonicity of $g_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}}$ means only that once a matched retirement credit has been publicly granted to the parent cohort, that historical credit is not silently revoked. A bad repair can still make the world worse; it appears either as a new cohort or as positive secondary liability $a_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{sec}}$. Thus monotone gross retirement is compatible with regression bugs and avoids overloading one variable with two opposite semantics.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Retained margin and improvement half-life]\label{def:retained_margin}
Let
\[
\mathcal M_t(h)
\Defeq
\E\!\left[
\widehat V_{t+h}^{\Shadow}(u_t)-\widehat V_{t+h}^{\Shadow}(0)
\mid \mathcal F_t
\right]
\]
be the shadow-reevaluated retained margin of the proposal issued at time $t$ after horizon $h\ge0$, where $\widehat V^{\Shadow}$ is computed using the issuance-time shadow family and issuance-time aggregator transported replayably to horizon $t+h$ in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:audit_family}. The value $\mathcal M_t(0)$ is the \emph{frozen shadow baseline}: it is evaluated at issuance time using the pre-edit shadow configuration before post-adoption yardstick drift and backlog accumulation are allowed to act on the cohort. For proposals with $\mathcal M_t(0)>0$, the \emph{improvement half-life} is
\[
\tau_{1/2}(t)\Defeq \inf\left\{h\ge1:\mathcal M_t(h)\le \tfrac12 \mathcal M_t(0)\right\}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Operational retained-margin lower certificate]\label{def:retained_margin_cert}
For a proposal cohort issued at time $t$, let $\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)$ denote the \emph{operational class-conditional retained-margin target} defined later in Definition~\ref{def:transport_calibration}. A family $\{\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)\}_{h\ge 1}$ is a \emph{replayable retained-margin lower certificate} if each $\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)$ is a replayable function of the matured challenge evidence, manifest-bound logs, class-assignment metadata, comparator-distortion budgets, confidence-budget manifests, and any published transport-calibration metadata available by horizon $h$, and if
\[
\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)\le \mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)
\qquad\text{for every }h\ge 1
\]
on every run consistent with the published challenge protocol. This certificate is \emph{admission-facing}: it lower-bounds the replayably published class-conditional target used by Interface A. The cohort-specific oracle margin $\mathcal M_t(h)$ from Definition~\ref{def:retained_margin} remains a distinct latent object and is related to the operational target only through additional homogeneity or transport assumptions stated explicitly below.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Blocked randomized challenge design with logged propensities]\label{def:challenge_design}
Fix a horizon $h\ge 1$ and a challenge-eligible cohort class. A replayable challenge design publishes, for each issued cohort $i$, issuance covariates $X_i$, proposal signature $U_i$, class label $\mathcal C_i$ in a replayably declared finite challenge-equivalence partition, challenge indicator $A_i\in\{0,1\}$, logged propensity $p_i\in[\underline p,1]$ with $\underline p>0$, horizon-maturity indicator $O_{i,h}(t)\in\{0,1\}$ at certification epoch $t$, delay label $D_{i,h}$, challenge-block identifier $B_i$, replayably declared block-compatibility family label $\mathfrak B_i$, and any replayable transport features needed to compare the issuance-time shadow family to the matured challenged family. For every issued cohort whose horizon-$h$ window has matured by epoch $t$, let $Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}$ denote the latent matured delayed challenge outcome under the issuance-time challenge metric transported replayably to maturity, and define the actually observed challenge score by
\[
Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{obs}}(t)\Defeq A_i\,O_{i,h}(t)\,Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}.
\]
In addition, the design partitions time into replayably declared \emph{challenge blocks} on each of which the evaluator, parser family, routing policy, class-assignment rule, and target metric used to define $Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}$ are frozen. Each block belongs to a replayably declared finite \emph{block-compatibility family} $\mathfrak B$ such that cohorts with the same $(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ pair share the same admissible challenge metric, parser/evaluator family, and declared transport interface into the current certification regime. The class-assignment map $(X_i,U_i)\mapsto \mathcal C_i$ and the block-family assignment map $(X_i,U_i,B_i)\mapsto \mathfrak B_i$ must themselves be replayably published, block-frozen, and immune to proposer-controlled post-issuance metadata: they may depend only on predeclared issuance-time features and may not be changed after observing challenge outcomes or current challenge-lane congestion. A working regression $\widehat m_h(X,U,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ may be published for efficiency, but admissibility is always based on replayable logged propensities, outcomes, block identifiers, class/block-family metadata, and transport metadata rather than on an unlogged prediction model.

For a class $\mathcal C$, block-compatibility family $\mathfrak B$, horizon $h$, and certification epoch $t$, define the \emph{operational class/block-conditional retained challenge margin}
\[
\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)
\Defeq
\E\bigl[Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}\mid \mathcal C_i=\mathcal C,\ \mathfrak B_i=\mathfrak B,\ O_{i,h}(t)=1\bigr].
\]
The current proposal issued at time $t$ inherits its operational target from the pair $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ assigned by the active block-frozen policy to $(X_t,u_t,B_t)$. If the current pair has no mature support, or fewer than the manifest-declared minimum support count required for certification, the design is \emph{fail-closed} for fast deployment: no class/block-conditional Interface-A certificate exists until the proposal is routed to challenge, proof escalation, sandbox, or a richer evidentiary class.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Challenge-design defect envelopes and fail-closed bias accounting]\label{def:chal_defects}
For a current class/block pair $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ and horizon $h$, let
\[
\delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\Defeq
\delta_h^{\mathrm{int}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{pos}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{ign}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{supp}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{clip}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\]
be a replayably published conservative design-defect envelope, where:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item $\delta_h^{\mathrm{int}}$ bounds residual cross-cohort interference after blocking;
  \item $\delta_h^{\mathrm{pos}}$ bounds the worst-case bias induced by propensity-floor violations, trimming, truncation, or effective support loss on the matured issued support;
  \item $\delta_h^{\mathrm{ign}}$ bounds the worst-case deviation from sequential ignorability allowed by the logged sensitivity analysis on the current pair;
  \item $\delta_h^{\mathrm{supp}}$ bounds mismatch between the currently certified class/block target and the deployment-relevant support for the current proposal, including class-assignment drift or support collapse not already excluded by the block-frozen manifest;
  \item $\delta_h^{\mathrm{clip}}$ bounds any bias introduced by replayable clipping, truncation, or stabilized reweighting used to obtain a bounded-score certificate.
\end{enumerate}
Any unavailable component is treated as $+\infty$ for fast deployment, which forces the interface to fail closed rather than to extrapolate from unsupported support. Zero design defect is the special case in which the blocked design, support, and bounded-score instrumentation are exact on the certified class/block target.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Admissibility-scale composition of challenge-design defects]\label{prop:chal_defect_comp}
Fix a horizon $h$ and current class/block pair $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$. Suppose each component in Definition~\ref{def:chal_defects} is a replayably published nonnegative bound on a downward perturbation of the same operational target $\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ after all propensity, clipping, blocking, and transport normalizations already used in the displayed estimator and confidence radius. Then the total downward perturbation is conservatively bounded by
\[
\delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
=
\delta_h^{\mathrm{int}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{pos}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{ign}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{supp}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
+\delta_h^{\mathrm{clip}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t).
\]
In particular, the fast gate may safely subtract the full published sum whenever the individual defect certificates are expressed on this common admissibility scale.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Let $\mathcal M^{(0)}$ denote the exact class/block target and let $\mathcal M^{(j)}$ be the intermediate target obtained after applying the first $j$ declared defect relaxations in the order interference, positivity/support, ignorability, support transfer, and clipping. By hypothesis,
\[
\mathcal M^{(j-1)}-\mathcal M^{(j)}\le \delta_j
\qquad\text{for each declared component }\delta_j\ge 0,
\]
on the same retained-margin scale. Summing these inequalities and using the triangle inequality gives
\[
\mathcal M^{(0)}-\mathcal M^{(5)}\le \sum_{j=1}^5 \delta_j = \delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t).
\]
Thus subtracting the full published sum is conservative even if some components are zero, merged, or vacuous.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Finite-sample replayable lower certificate from blocked randomized delayed challenge]\label{thm:dr_shadow_cert}
Fix a horizon $h\ge1$ and assume Definitions~\ref{def:challenge_design} and \ref{def:chal_defects}. Consider the current proposal pair $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$. Suppose: (i) challenge routing is sequentially ignorable given the logged filtration generated by $(X_i,U_i,\mathcal C_i,\mathfrak B_i)$ and the block identifier, up to the published sensitivity envelope $\delta_h^{\mathrm{ign}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$; (ii) logged propensities are published together with any positivity-floor defect envelope $\delta_h^{\mathrm{pos}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ induced by trimming, truncation, or support loss on the matured issued support; (iii) challenge delay is nonanticipating relative to the same filtration; (iv) within each block, evaluator, parser, routing policy, class-assignment rule, block-family rule, and challenge metric are frozen; (v) blocks pooled under the current family label $\mathfrak B_t$ are replayably certified transport-compatible for the challenge target, up to the published support-mismatch envelope $\delta_h^{\mathrm{supp}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$; (vi) either the logged propensities are correct or the published regression $\widehat m_h(X,U,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ is correctly specified on the current pair; and (vii) the defect components are expressed on the common admissibility scale required by Proposition~\ref{prop:chal_defect_comp}. Assume further that latent matured challenge outcomes are uniformly bounded by a replayable envelope $|Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}|\le B_h$.

Let $\mathbf J_{t,n}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)=(i_1,\dots,i_n)$ denote the first $n$ issued cohorts with $(\mathcal C_{i_k},\mathfrak B_{i_k})=(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ whose horizon-$h$ certification window has matured by epoch $t$, i.e. $O_{i_k,h}(t)=1$ for each $k$, and let $n_{\min}(h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ be the manifest-declared minimum matured support count from Definition~\ref{def:confidence_manifest}. Define the class/block-conditional doubly robust estimator
\[
\widehat{\mathcal M}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\Defeq
\frac1n\sum_{k=1}^{n}\left[\widehat m_h(X_{i_k},U_{i_k},\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)+\frac{Y_{i_k,h}^{\mathrm{obs}}(t)-A_{i_k}O_{i_k,h}(t)\widehat m_h(X_{i_k},U_{i_k},\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)}{p_{i_k}}\right].
\]
If $n<n_{\min}(h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$, no class/block-conditional certificate exists and Interface A is operationally inconclusive for fast deployment on $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$. Otherwise there exists a replayable anytime radius $\operatorname{rad}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h,\alpha;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$, computable from the logged propensities, bounded outcomes, block structure, and standard confidence-sequence or e-process ingredients \cite{HowardRamdasMcAuliffeSekhon2021,RamdasGrunwaldVovkShafer2023,ZhanHadadHirshbergAthey2021}, such that with probability at least $1-\alpha$ simultaneously for all $n\ge n_{\min}(h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$,
\[
\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\ge
\widehat{\mathcal M}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
-\operatorname{rad}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h,\alpha;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
-\delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t).
\]
Consequently
\[
\underline{\mathcal M}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\Defeq
\widehat{\mathcal M}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
