-\operatorname{rad}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h,\alpha;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
-\delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\]
is a replayable finite-sample lower certificate for the operational class/block-conditional retained challenge margin. The theorem certifies the current proposal's replayably assigned class/block target at certification epoch $t$; it is not a direct certificate for the current proposal's cohort-specific oracle margin.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
On the matured issued support $O_{i,h}(t)=1$, the observed challenge score satisfies $Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{obs}}(t)=A_iY_{i,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}$. Therefore the displayed doubly robust score can be written as
\[
\widehat m_h(X_i,U_i,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)+\frac{A_iO_{i,h}(t)}{p_i}\bigl(Y_{i,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}-\widehat m_h(X_i,U_i,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\bigr),
\]
which is the standard missing-outcome doubly robust score on the matured issued support. Under the block-freezing and nonanticipating-delay clauses, its conditional expectation equals the operational class/block retained challenge margin whenever either the propensity model or the regression model is correct on $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ and the remaining departures from exact identification are absorbed by the published design-defect envelope. Bounded outcomes control inverse-propensity variance, while support loss, trimming, bounded-score clipping bias, residual cross-cohort interference, and logged ignorability sensitivity are subtracted conservatively through $\delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}$. Standard confidence-sequence or e-process constructions therefore produce a replayable radius $\operatorname{rad}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}$ that lower-bounds the class/block target uniformly over time on the matured issued support after debiting the declared defect budget. The fail-closed convention for empty, support-deficient, or diagnostically unsupported classes is immediate.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Executable empirical-Bernstein instantiation of the delayed-challenge radius]\label{prop:chal_radius}
Under the hypotheses of Theorem~\ref{thm:dr_shadow_cert}, let $\mathbf J_{t,n}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)=(i_1,\dots,i_n)$ be the ordered matured-issued class/block sample, and define the replayable doubly robust score for the $k$-th element of that sample by
\[
\xi_{k,h}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\Defeq
\widehat m_h(X_{i_k},U_{i_k},\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)+\frac{Y_{i_k,h}^{\mathrm{obs}}(t)-A_{i_k}O_{i_k,h}(t)\widehat m_h(X_{i_k},U_{i_k},\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)}{p_{i_k}}.
\]
Assume the manifest publishes either a replayably clipped regression or an equivalent bounded-score certificate guaranteeing $|\xi_{k,h}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)|\le B_{h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t}^{\mathrm{DR}}$, that any bias induced by clipping, truncation, or stabilized weighting is already absorbed into $\delta_h^{\mathrm{clip}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ from Definition~\ref{def:chal_defects}, and that the regression used to define $\xi_{k,h}$ is fixed before the $k$-th matured outcome is revealed (for example by using a disjoint replayable training sample or a prequential update rule). Define the sample-index filtration
\[
\mathcal G_{t,k}^{\mathrm{chal}}\Defeq \sigma\bigl(\mathbf J_{t,k}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t), \{X_{i_j},U_{i_j},\mathcal C_{i_j},\mathfrak B_{i_j},p_{i_j},O_{i_j,h}(t),Y_{i_j,h}^{\mathrm{obs}}(t)\}_{j\le k}\bigr),
\]
with $\mathcal G_{t,0}^{\mathrm{chal}}$ containing the published regression and clipping certificate. Define the predictable empirical-variance process
\[
V_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\Defeq \sum_{k=1}^{n}\bigl(\xi_{k,h}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)-\widehat{\mathcal M}_{t,k-1}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\bigr)^2,
\]
with the convention $\widehat{\mathcal M}_{t,0}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)=0$, and let
\[
\nu(v,\alpha;B)\Defeq \sqrt{2(v\vee 1)\log(2/\alpha)}+3B\log(2/\alpha).
\]
Then one valid replayable choice is
\[
\operatorname{rad}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h,\alpha;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\Defeq
\frac{\nu\!\left(V_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t),\alpha;B_{h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t}^{\mathrm{DR}}\right)}{n\vee 1},
\]
which yields an anytime empirical-Bernstein lower confidence sequence for the operational class/block-conditional target under the same blocked design, predictable-score, and bounded-score assumptions.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
For bounded predictable scores adapted to the sample-index filtration $\{\mathcal G_{t,k}^{\mathrm{chal}}\}_{k\ge0}$, standard stitched or mixture empirical-Bernstein confidence sequences control the centered partial sums uniformly over time in terms of the predictable quadratic variation and a bounded-increment envelope \cite{HowardRamdasMcAuliffeSekhon2021,RamdasGrunwaldVovkShafer2023}. Applying that construction to the replayably logged doubly robust scores on the ordered matured class/block sample gives the displayed radius. The theorem then follows by dividing by $n\vee1$ and subtracting the full declared design-defect envelope $\delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}$, whose additivity on the admission-facing retained-margin scale is justified by Proposition~\ref{prop:chal_defect_comp}; residual interference is only one component, and comparator distortion is handled later, at the bridge from class/block slow-utility targets to witnesswise oracle stable gain.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Confidence-budget manifest for multi-horizon and multi-class certificates]\label{def:confidence_manifest}
A \emph{confidence-budget manifest} is a replayably published allocation
\[
\{\alpha_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}^{\mathrm{chal}}\}_{h\in\mathcal H,\ \mathcal C\in\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{chal}},\ \mathfrak B\in\mathfrak B^{\mathrm{chal}}},
\qquad
\{\alpha_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}^{\mathrm{tr}}\}_{h\in\mathcal H,\ \mathcal C\in\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{chal}},\ \mathfrak B\in\mathfrak B^{\mathrm{chal}}},
\]
with
\[
\sum_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}\alpha_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}^{\mathrm{chal}}+
\sum_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}\alpha_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}^{\mathrm{tr}}
\le \alpha_{\mathrm{tot}},
\]
and a replayably declared minimum matured support count map
\[
n_{\min}:\mathcal H\times\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{chal}}\times\mathfrak B^{\mathrm{chal}}\to\N.
\]
Unless a vector-valued anytime certificate is published, simultaneous validity across horizons, classes, block-compatibility families, and transport-calibration residual certificates is interpreted through this explicit budget split and a union bound under the active manifest.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Transport calibration from challenge margin to slow utility]\label{def:transport_calibration}
For each replayably declared challenge-equivalence class $\mathcal C$, block-compatibility family $\mathfrak B$, and horizon $h$, a \emph{transport-calibration family} is a collection of replayable lower transport coefficients $a_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\ge 0$, offsets $b_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\ge 0$, and residual envelopes $\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\ge 0$ such that for every comparator-compatible cohort in the pair $(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ and every admissible comparator witness $c$,
\[
\E\bigl[V(z_{t+h}^{u_t,c})-V(z_{t+h}^{0,c})\mid \mathcal F_t\bigr]
\ge
 a_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\,\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)-b_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)-\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)-\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c).
\]
Define the corresponding \emph{operational class/block-conditional retained-margin target} for the current proposal's pair $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ by
\[
\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)
\Defeq
a_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\,\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)-b_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)-\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t).
\]
The coefficients may be learned or stress-tested from matched long-horizon replays or previously audited cohorts, but once published they are treated as part of the active replayable admission contract rather than as hidden analyst choices. Comparator distortion is handled downstream at the witnesswise stable-gain bridge rather than inside the class/block challenge certificate itself. A transport-calibration family is Tier-2 admissible only if the manifest also publishes a replayable matched-replay or audited transport certificate witnessing how the displayed lower envelope was derived on the declared class/block pair.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Matched-replay transport certificate implies Tier-2 transport calibration]\label{prop:transport_tier2}
Fix class $\mathcal C$, block-compatibility family $\mathfrak B$, and horizon $h$. Suppose the manifest publishes a replayable matched-replay sample of challenged cohorts in the pair $(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ together with matched long-horizon slow-utility differences $\Delta V_{j,h}$ and retained challenge outcomes $Y_{j,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}$, all measured on the same matured support event $O_{j,h}(t)=1$, and suppose a proof-carrying certificate verifies that
\[
\begin{aligned}
\E[\Delta V_{j,h}\mid \mathcal C_j=\mathcal C,\ \mathfrak B_j=\mathfrak B,\ O_{j,h}(t)=1]
&\ge a_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\,\E[Y_{j,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}\mid \mathcal C_j=\mathcal C,\ \mathfrak B_j=\mathfrak B,\ O_{j,h}(t)=1]\\
&\quad -b_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)-\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B).
\end{aligned}
\]
for the published coefficients and residual envelope. Then the resulting transport-calibration family is Tier-2 admissible under Definition~\ref{def:proxy_tiers}: it may enter Interface A because its coefficients are no longer heuristic routing signals but proof-carrying replay-derived lower-envelope quantities.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The proof-carrying matched-replay certificate turns the transport coefficients into derived quantities whose validity reduces to replayable matched samples and the checker's proof obligations. By the gate discipline, such proof-carrying derived quantities are Tier-2 rather than Tier-3. Substituting them into Definition~\ref{def:transport_calibration} yields a replayable lower envelope on slow-utility change from the class/block-conditional challenge target.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Executable matched-replay transport residual certificate]\label{prop:transport_radius}
Fix class $\mathcal C$, block-compatibility family $\mathfrak B$, and horizon $h$. Suppose the manifest publishes a replayable matched-replay sample $j=1,\dots,m$ together with matched slow-utility differences $\Delta V_{j,h}$, retained challenge outcomes $Y_{j,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}$, and transport coefficients $a_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B),b_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$, all defined on the same matured support event $O_{j,h}(t)=1$. Define the residuals
\[
R_{j,h}^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\Defeq a_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)Y_{j,h}^{\mathrm{ret}}-b_h(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)-\Delta V_{j,h}.
\]
Assume a replayable bounded-residual certificate $|R_{j,h}^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)|\le B_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ and let $\overline R_{m,h}^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B;\alpha)$ be any replayable one-sided anytime upper confidence sequence for
\[
\E[R_{j,h}^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\mid \mathcal C_j=\mathcal C,\ \mathfrak B_j=\mathfrak B,\ O_{j,h}(t)=1]
\]
built from the matched sample. Then any published residual envelope satisfying
\[
\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\ge \bigl(\overline R_{m,h}^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B;\alpha)\bigr)_+
\]
is a replayable Tier-2 transport residual certificate for Definition~\ref{def:transport_calibration}. In particular, matched-replay transport calibration can be made executable rather than purely contractual once the residual certificate and its confidence budget are published.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The transport inequality in Definition~\ref{def:transport_calibration} is equivalent to requiring that the conditional mean residual on the matched matured support be no larger than $\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$. A replayable one-sided upper confidence sequence for that residual mean therefore yields a replayable lower-envelope certificate once its positive part is published as the transport residual budget. Because the matched-replay sample, bounded-residual certificate, and confidence budget are replayably logged, the resulting envelope is Tier-2 admissible.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Class-homogeneity envelope]\label{def:class_homogeneity}
A replayable \emph{class-homogeneity envelope} for class $\mathcal C$, block-compatibility family $\mathfrak B$, and horizon $h$ is a nonnegative quantity $\delta_h^{\mathrm{class}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ such that every cohort in the pair $(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)$ satisfies
\[
\mathcal M_t(h)\ge \mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\delta_h^{\mathrm{class}}(\mathcal C,\mathfrak B).
\]
This envelope quantifies the residual gap between the cohort-specific oracle retained margin and the class/block operational target used for admission.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Transport-calibrated operational retained-margin certificate]\label{prop:challenge_to_shadow}
Fix the current proposal pair $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ and horizon $h\ge1$. Suppose Definition~\ref{def:transport_calibration} holds on $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ and let $\underline{\mathcal M}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ be any replayable lower certificate from Theorem~\ref{thm:dr_shadow_cert}. Then
\[
\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)
\Defeq
 a_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\,\underline{\mathcal M}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)-b_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)-\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\]
is a replayable retained-margin lower certificate in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:retained_margin_cert} for the operational class/block target entering Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge}. If, in addition, Definition~\ref{def:class_homogeneity} holds on $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$, then
\[
\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{oracle}}(h)\Defeq \underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\delta_h^{\mathrm{class}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
\]
is a replayable lower certificate for the cohort-specific oracle retained margin $\mathcal M_t(h)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Combine the lower certificate from Theorem~\ref{thm:dr_shadow_cert} with the affine lower transport inequality of Definition~\ref{def:transport_calibration}. Because $a_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\ge 0$, multiplying the lower class/block challenge certificate preserves validity, and subtracting the published offset and transport residual yields a conservative lower bound on the operational class/block slow-utility target. The resulting object is replayable because every ingredient is published in the active design and transport-calibration contract. The second claim follows immediately by subtracting the published class-homogeneity envelope.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Transport comparability of retained shadow margins]\label{prop:shadow_transport}
Fix a cohort issued at time $t$ and horizon $h\ge0$. Suppose the replayable transport from the issuance-time shadow family to the horizon-$t+h$ descendants satisfies margin-comparison envelopes
\[
\underline\vartheta_{t,h}\,\widetilde{\mathcal M}_t(h)-\delta_{t,h}^{\Shadow}
\le
\mathcal M_t(h)
\le
\bar\vartheta_{t,h}\,\widetilde{\mathcal M}_t(h)+\delta_{t,h}^{\Shadow},
\qquad
0<\underline\vartheta_{t,h}\le \bar\vartheta_{t,h}<\infty,
\]
for some transported ideal margin $\widetilde{\mathcal M}_t(h)$ and replayable defect envelope $\delta_{t,h}^{\Shadow}\ge0$. Then any sign certificate or half-life bound phrased in terms of $\widetilde{\mathcal M}_t(h)$ remains valid after replacing it by the displayed transported lower or upper envelope. In particular, half-life conclusions depend only on replayably transported shadow gauges, not on silently changing the active shadow family after issuance.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed inequalities already give the required one-sided substitutions. Any lower-margin sign certificate based on $\widetilde{\mathcal M}_t(h)$ remains valid after replacing it by the transported lower envelope, and any threshold-crossing or half-life upper bound remains valid after replacing it by the transported upper envelope. The final sentence is simply the observation that all permitted post-issuance family changes must factor through the replayable transport envelopes rather than through arbitrary gauge replacement.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Challenge lane and shadow evaluator]
A \emph{challenge lane} is a delayed, higher-fidelity reevaluation process receiving a subsequence of proposals. A \emph{shadow evaluator} is an evaluator instance used only within the challenge lane and not directly editable by the currently evaluated proposal.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Typed memory lanes]\label{def:lanes}
The substrate is partitioned into three typed lanes:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.8em]
  \item \textbf{Evidentiary core} $\mathcal L_t^{\Core}$: items directly usable for current admissibility.
  \item \textbf{Heterodoxy lane} $\mathcal L_t^{\Het}$: bounded-depth contradiction, evaluator disagreement artifacts, and minority evidence held under quarantine-preserve rules.
  \item \textbf{Narrative lane} $\mathcal L_t^{\Narr}$: compressed coordination summaries not directly admissible as evidence.
\end{itemize}
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Epistemic routing sensitivity and forced-attention invariant]\label{def:forced_attention}
Let $E_t$ denote the contradiction-tagged reserve that currently contributes to $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$. For each $x\in E_t$, let $J_t^{\mathrm{adm}}$ be the current admissibility score or acceptance functional and let $\alpha_x\in[0,1]$ be the retrieval gate applied to $x$ by the live evaluation pipeline. Define the replayable finite-difference sensitivity of $x$ by
\[
\operatorname{Sens}_t^{\Het}(x)
\Defeq
\bigl|J_t^{\mathrm{adm}}(\alpha_x=1,\alpha_{E_t\setminus\{x\}})-J_t^{\mathrm{adm}}(\alpha_x=0,\alpha_{E_t\setminus\{x\}})\bigr|.
\]
The \emph{heterodoxy routing load} is
\[
\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}
\Defeq
\sum_{x\in E_t} w_t(x)\,\operatorname{Sens}_t^{\Het}(x).
\]
A policy satisfies the \emph{forced-attention invariant} if there exists $\kappa_{\mathrm{att}}>0$ such that
\[
\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}\ge \kappa_{\mathrm{att}}\,\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}
\qquad\text{for all }t.
\]
Thus preserved contradiction must not only remain stored; it must continue to exert a nonvanishing, auditable effect on the live evaluation pipeline.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Bounded-depth contradiction window]
Let $x\in\mathcal L_t^{\Het}$ be an item carrying a replayable contradiction certificate relative to the current dominant evaluator state. Its resource-bounded logical depth under budget $B_t$ is denoted $\mathrm{Depth}_{B_t}(x)$. The admissible contradiction window is
\[
\mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{contra}}=(c_{\min},c_{\max}(B_t)).
\]
Only contradiction items satisfying
\[
\mathrm{Depth}_{B_t}(x)\in \mathcal I_t^{\mathrm{contra}}
\]
are eligible for heterodoxy-lane preservation.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Persistent contradiction obligation and admissible de-tagging]\label{def:contra_obligation}
Every contradiction-tagged item $x$ carries three replayably logged fields: an issuance-time contradiction certificate hash $h_x^{\mathrm{contra}}$, an issuance-time basis or panel family identifier, and an open obligation status. The obligation remains live until one of the following replayably logged events occurs:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item a multi-panel rebuttal certificate validates that the contradiction has been resolved under the successor basis family while preserving replayable transport to the issuance-time family, or
  \item a counted deletion event is paired with conservation compensation, meaning replayably admitted replacement contradiction families whose weighted mass and transported robust semantic volume meet the policy compensation floor.
\end{enumerate}
De-tagging without one of these two events is invalid. In particular, contradiction status cannot be erased merely by evaluator preference drift, basis replacement, or lane retyping.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Cross-basis semantic volume of the contradiction reserve]\label{def:semantic_volume}
Let $E_t\subseteq \mathcal L_t^{\Het}\cup\mathcal L_t^{\Core}$ be the set of contradiction-tagged items that currently contribute to $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$, and assume the active contradiction support is finite on each audited horizon: $0\le |E_t|<\infty$. Let
\[
\Psi_t=\{\psi_t^{(1)},\dots,\psi_t^{(K_t^{\psi})}\}
\]
be a replayable family of public normalized contradiction-fingerprint maps produced by provenance-separated encoder or parser families, with $K_t^{\psi}\ge 1$. The family may either be fixed through time or be updated only through replayable transport certificates that map each active basis to a successor basis together with explicit overlap and distortion bounds. For each basis $k$, define the positive-semidefinite kernel
\[
L_t^{(k)}(x,x')\Defeq \sqrt{w_t(x)w_t(x')}\,\langle \psi_t^{(k)}(x),\psi_t^{(k)}(x')\rangle,
\]
on the finite index set $E_t\times E_t$, and the corresponding basis-specific semantic volume
\[
\mathcal V_t^{(k)}\Defeq \log\det\bigl(I+L_t^{(k)}\bigr),
\]
with the convention $\mathcal V_t^{(k)}\Defeq 0$ when $E_t=\varnothing$ (equivalently, the determinant of the empty matrix is $1$). The \emph{cross-basis robust semantic volume} of the contradiction reserve is
\[
\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}\Defeq \min_{1\le k\le K_t^{\psi}} \mathcal V_t^{(k)},
\]
which is therefore also $0$ when $E_t=\varnothing$.
Whenever the active fingerprint family changes, the policy is assumed to expose a replayable transport injection
\[
\vartheta_t:[K_t^{\psi}]\hookrightarrow [K_{t+1}^{\psi}]
\]
linking each predecessor basis to one declared successor basis together with multiplicative or additive distortion envelopes. The associated \emph{transported robust semantic volume} is
\[
\bar{\mathcal V}_{t+1}^{\mathrm{contra},\mathrm{tr}}\Defeq \min_{1\le k\le K_t^{\psi}} \mathcal V_{t+1}^{(\vartheta_t(k)),\mathrm{tr}},
\]
that is, the minimum taken only over successor bases reached by declared transport from the previous active family. Extra newly introduced bases may be tracked separately, but they are not allowed to shrink the transported robust volume retroactively. Unlike $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$, which measures weighted mass, $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ rewards nonredundant semantic directions and discounts near-duplicates. Unlike a single-basis volume, it is not allowed to increase merely because one currently fashionable encoder is rewritten to spray orthogonal noise over duplicate artifacts.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Why semantic floors and volumes are not oracle gifts]
The quantities $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$ and $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ are policy-audited envelopes computed from replayable families, not metaphysical truth labels. If every relevant family is jointly captured, the envelopes can collapse or be spoofed; that failure mode is made explicit later rather than hidden behind a benevolent constant.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Tiered operationalization of contradiction metrics]
Nothing in the definition of $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ requires full cross-basis log-determinant recomputation on every fast-lane candidate. A practical regime may use cheap monotone screens for routing, reserve alarms, and garbage-collection triage, while reserving exact robust-volume recomputation for promotion, periodic audit checkpoints, parser-family refresh, or contradiction-window maintenance, provided that no fast admission relies on an uncomputed increase and every published surrogate remains conservative in the sense of Proposition~\ref{prop:proxy_gap}.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Replay-floor invariance under lossy refreezing]\label{prop:replay_floor}
Fix any policy-maintained audit set $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}\subseteq \mathcal L_t^{\Het}\cup \mathcal L_t^{\Core}$. Suppose every parser or environment update satisfies one of the following for each $a\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}$: either
\[
G_{t+1}^{\mathrm{replay}}(a)\ge g_{\min},
\]
or the policy emits a refrozen replay bundle $a'$ with
\[
G_{t+1}^{\mathrm{replay}}(a')\ge g_{\min}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a')\ge s_{\min}.
\]
Then replayability is not silently lost on the audit set: every retained contradiction-bearing or evidentiary artifact continues to admit a replay witness above the floor. However, the proposition guarantees only \emph{replay-floor preservation}; it does not assert lossless preservation of evidentiary force. If an item is refrozen repeatedly through the chain
\[
a_0\rightsquigarrow a_1\rightsquigarrow \cdots \rightsquigarrow a_k,
\]
its effective evidentiary weight is conservatively multiplied by
\[
W_k^{\mathrm{eff}}(a_0)\Defeq W_0(a_0)\prod_{j=0}^{k-1} S_{t_j}^{\mathrm{sem}}(a_j\rightsquigarrow a_{j+1}).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Proceed item by item. If the update preserves the floor directly, the claim is immediate. Otherwise the policy must replace the old artifact by a refrozen bundle that restores the floor while exposing an audited lower bound on semantic retention. Thus every item in the retained audit set continues to possess at least one replay witness above $g_{\min}$ after the update. The multiplicative weight expression is simply the cumulative product of the declared semantic-retention factors along the refreezing chain.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Finite epistemic horizon under lossy refreezing]\label{thm:finite_horizon}
Fix an evidentiary item $a_0$ with initial effective weight $W_0(a_0)>0$ and policy usefulness threshold $W_{\min}\in(0,W_0(a_0))$. Suppose every refreeze event in a retained audit chain satisfies
\[
S_{t_j}^{\mathrm{sem}}(a_j\rightsquigarrow a_{j+1}) \le e^{-\underline\gamma\,D_{t_j}^{\mathrm{yard}}}
\]
for some $\underline\gamma>0$, and that yardstick drift along that chain obeys the persistent lower floor
\[
D_{t_j}^{\mathrm{yard}}\ge \underline D>0.
\]
Then after $k$ refreeze events,
\[
W_k^{\mathrm{eff}}(a_0)
\le
W_0(a_0)e^{-k\underline\gamma\underline D}.
\]
Hence any such item loses policy-effective force after at most
\[
N_{\mathrm{hor}}(a_0)
\Defeq
\left\lceil\frac{\log\bigl(W_0(a_0)/W_{\min}\bigr)}{\underline\gamma\underline D}\right\rceil
\]
refreeze events. More generally, if retained evidence is refrozen with asymptotic frequency at least $\varrho>0$ per unit time, then the corresponding time horizon is finite and bounded by $T_{\mathrm{hor}}\le N_{\mathrm{hor}}/\varrho$. Therefore long-run governance cannot rely on archival survival alone: persistent drift forces native regeneration of currently meaningful evidence and contradiction witnesses.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The assumed bound on each semantic-retention factor implies
\[
\prod_{j=0}^{k-1}S_{t_j}^{\mathrm{sem}}(a_j\rightsquigarrow a_{j+1})
\le
\prod_{j=0}^{k-1} e^{-\underline\gamma D_{t_j}^{\mathrm{yard}}}
\le
e^{-k\underline\gamma\underline D}.
\]
Multiplying by $W_0(a_0)$ yields the displayed decay law for $W_k^{\mathrm{eff}}(a_0)$. Solving the inequality $W_0(a_0)e^{-k\underline\gamma\underline D}\le W_{\min}$ for $k$ gives $N_{\mathrm{hor}}(a_0)$. If refreeze events occur with frequency at least $\varrho$, then at most $N_{\mathrm{hor}}/\varrho$ time units are needed to accumulate $N_{\mathrm{hor}}$ events. The final claim follows because once the effective weight drops below the usefulness threshold, the old item no longer suffices by itself for current governance.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Epistemic conservation law for garbage collection]
\label{def:epistemic_conservation}
Let $\mathcal G_t$ be the set of contradiction-bearing or audit-bearing artifacts scheduled for garbage collection at time $t$, let $\mathcal N_t$ be the set of newly generated native contradiction witnesses admitted since the previous garbage-collection event, and let $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}$ denote the active policy-maintained audit set at time $t$. Define the dropped effective mass and native replacement mass by
\[
\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{eff}}\Defeq \sum_{a\in\mathcal G_t} W_t^{\mathrm{eff}}(a),
\qquad
\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{eff}}\Defeq \sum_{a\in\mathcal N_t} W_t^{\mathrm{eff}}(a).
\]
Let
\[
\mathfrak M_t \Defeq \bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}} + \lambda_W \sum_{a\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}} W_t^{\mathrm{eff}}(a),
\qquad \lambda_W>0.
\]
Because robust semantic volume is not additive, garbage collection is tracked through one-sided marginal envelopes rather than exact gain/loss decomposition. Let
\[
\overline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{contra}}\ge 0
\]
be any replayable upper envelope on the decrease in transported robust semantic volume caused by removing $\mathcal G_t$ from the pre-GC reserve while holding the surviving reserve fixed, and let
\[
\underline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{contra}}\ge 0
\]
be any replayable lower envelope on the increase in transported robust semantic volume obtained by adding $\mathcal N_t$ to that surviving reserve under the current basis family after any admissible transport or refreezing. A garbage-collection step is \emph{epistemically conservative} if, before any item in $\mathcal G_t$ is removed,
\[
\underline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{contra}} + \lambda_W\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{eff}}
\ge
\overline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{contra}} + \lambda_W\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{eff}},
\]
and every replacement witness in $\mathcal N_t$ satisfies the current replay floor, semantic-retention floor, and forced-attention invariant.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Epistemic mass conservation and the ban on malicious obsolescence]\label{thm:epistemic_conservation}
Suppose garbage collection is permitted whenever archived evidence has fallen below a policy usefulness threshold, but no conservation law is imposed. Then there exists a drift-accelerating proposal schedule that keeps every instantaneous step formally admissible, yet drives selected contradiction witnesses below threshold and removes them before comparable native contradiction is regenerated. Consequently the post-GC audit potential $\mathfrak M_t$ can be made to decrease over garbage-collection events even while the loop remains superficially compliant.

By contrast, if every garbage-collection event is epistemically conservative in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:epistemic_conservation}, then the post-GC audit potential is nondecreasing across garbage-collection events:
\[
\mathfrak M_{t^+} \ge \mathfrak M_{t^-},
\]
where $t^-$ and $t^+$ denote the moments immediately before and after garbage collection. Therefore accelerated yardstick drift cannot be used as a legal controlled burn of old constraints unless the system has already regenerated compensating contradiction mass under the current ruler.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For the first claim, take a regime with lossy refreezing as in Theorem~\ref{thm:finite_horizon}. By scheduling a long enough sequence of individually admissible evaluator or parser updates, the attacker can force the effective weights of targeted contradiction witnesses below the usefulness threshold. If garbage collection is then allowed to delete subthreshold items without requiring compensating replacement mass, both the weighted audit term and the robust semantic volume can strictly decrease, so $\mathfrak M_t$ drops across the event.

For the converse, the effective-mass component changes exactly by $\lambda_W(\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{eff}}-\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{eff}})$. The robust-semantic-volume component is not decomposed additively; instead, by definition of the marginal envelopes,
\[
\bar{\mathcal V}_{t^+}^{\mathrm{contra}}-\bar{\mathcal V}_{t^-}^{\mathrm{contra}}
\ge
\underline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{contra}}-
\overline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{contra}}.
\]
Combining this inequality with the epistemic-conservation condition yields
\[
\mathfrak M_{t^+}-\mathfrak M_{t^-}
\ge
\underline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{contra}}-
\overline{\Delta \bar{\mathcal V}}_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{contra}}
+\lambda_W\bigl(\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{new}}^{\mathrm{eff}}-\Delta W_{t,\mathrm{drop}}^{\mathrm{eff}}\bigr)
\ge 0.
\]
Because the replacement witnesses also satisfy current replay and routing constraints, they remain live governance inputs rather than inert archive mass. The final sentence follows immediately: any attempt to accelerate drift so as to retire old evidence must first pay for replacement contradiction under the current yardstick.
\end{proof}

\section{Closed-Loop Gain Model}
To sharpen the core theorems, we isolate the coupled gain structure explicitly. A fixed gain matrix is too rigid for a self-modifying system, so the stability wrapper is stated in a time-varying form and the static one-step regime is recovered as a special case. The admissible window-product envelope plays the role of a replayable joint-spectral-radius style wrapper rather than a hidden analytic convenience \cite{Jungers2009}.


\begin{assumption}[State-dependent gain envelopes, explicit policy drift, and window contraction]\label{ass:gain_matrix}
There exists a \emph{replayable reference scaffold} $z_t^\star=(x_t^\star,e_t^\star,m_t^\star,q_t^\star,r_t^\star,h_t^\star,\Pi_t^\star)$ generated either by an archived null-policy replay, by a frozen safe-baseline controller, or by a matched replay pair whose construction is logged and auditable from the public artifacts. In contrast to the earlier projected wrapper, the theorem now tracks an explicit replayable policy-manifest distortion coordinate in addition to $(x,e,m,q,r,h)$. Concretely, there exist a predictable sequence of nonnegative gain matrices $K_t\in\R_+^{7\times 7}$, a nonnegative matrix $K^{\max}\in\R_+^{7\times 7}$, a window length $W\in\N$, a nonnegative contraction envelope $\bar K\in\R_+^{7\times 7}$ with $\rho(\bar K)<1$, a nonnegative disturbance sequence $b_t\in\R_+^7$ bounded componentwise by $\bar b$, a nonnegative hidden-state deviation gauge $\delta_h(\cdot,\cdot)$, and a replayable policy-manifest pseudometric $\delta_{\Pi,t}(\Pi,\Pi')$ such that for the deviation vector
\[
d_t\Defeq \begin{bmatrix}
\norm{x_t-x_t^\star}\\
\norm{e_t-e_t^\star}\\
\norm{m_t-m_t^\star}\\
\abs{q_t-q_t^\star}\\
\abs{r_t-r_t^\star}\\
\delta_h(h_t,h_t^\star)\\
\delta_{\Pi,t}(\Pi_t,\Pi_t^\star)
\end{bmatrix}\in\R_+^7
\]
we have
\[
d_{t+1}\preceq K_t d_t + b_t,
\qquad
0\preceq K_t\preceq K^{\max},
\qquad
0\preceq b_t\preceq \bar b,
\]
and every admissible length-$W$ product is dominated by the same contractive envelope:
\[
K_{t+W-1}K_{t+W-2}\cdots K_t \preceq \bar K
\qquad\text{for all }t\ge 0.
\]
In addition, the reference evaluator drift and reference policy-manifest drift are uniformly bounded in replayably comparable gauges:
\[
\norm{e_{t+1}^\star-e_t^\star}\le \bar D_E^\star,
\qquad
\delta_{\Pi,t+1}^{\mathrm{tr}}(\Pi_{t+1}^\star,\Pi_t^\star)\le \bar D_\Pi^\star
\qquad\text{for all }t.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{proposition}[Constructive route to the window-contractive envelope]\label{prop:constructive_window}
Suppose policy exposes a finite replayable catalog of local mode envelopes $\{K^{(m)}\}_{m\in\mathcal M}$ for admissible edit modes, a replayable language $\mathcal W_W^{\mathrm{adm}}\subseteq \mathcal M^W$ of length-$W$ mode words allowed by the current dwell, quota, and review contracts, and a replayable disturbance cap $\bar b$. Define
\[
\bar K\Defeq \max_{\omega\in\mathcal W_W^{\mathrm{adm}}} K^{(\omega_W)}\cdots K^{(\omega_1)}
\]
entrywise. If $\rho(\bar K)<1$, then Assumption~\ref{ass:gain_matrix} holds with this explicitly computed $\bar K$. In particular, the small-gain wrapper need not postulate a mysterious contractive matrix: it can be derived from the published local mode library and the published admissible switching language.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Every admissible length-$W$ trajectory corresponds to some word $\omega\in\mathcal W_W^{\mathrm{adm}}$, and its window product is entrywise dominated by the corresponding catalog product. Taking the entrywise maximum over the finite admissible language therefore yields a replayable common envelope $\bar K$. The remaining clauses of Assumption~\ref{ass:gain_matrix} are exactly the declared local envelope and disturbance bounds.
\end{proof}

\section{Main Results}
\subsection{Small-gain stability and explicit yardstick ceiling}
\begin{theorem}[Latent-scaffold time-varying small-gain stability with explicit policy drift]\label{thm:small_gain}
Assume \ref{ass:gain_matrix}. Let
\[
G_W\Defeq \sum_{\ell=0}^{W-1}(K^{\max})^{\ell}.
\]
Then the window-sampled deviation process satisfies, for every $n\ge 0$,
\[
d_{(n+1)W}
\preceq
\bar K\, d_{nW} + G_W\bar b.
\]
Consequently,
\[
d_{nW}
\preceq
\bar K^n d_0 + \sum_{j=0}^{n-1}\bar K^j G_W\bar b
\preceq
\bar K^n d_0 + (I-\bar K)^{-1}G_W\bar b,
\]
so every sampled component, including the policy-manifest distortion coordinate, is uniformly bounded and
\[
\limsup_{n\to\infty} d_{nW}\preceq (I-\bar K)^{-1}G_W\bar b.
\]
Moreover each intermediate time inside a window obeys
\[
d_{nW+s}\preceq (K^{\max})^s d_{nW} + \sum_{\ell=0}^{s-1}(K^{\max})^{\ell}\bar b,
\qquad s=0,1,\dots,W-1,
\]
so the full process $\{d_t\}$ is uniformly bounded as well.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Unroll the recursion over one window:
\[
d_{t+W}
\preceq
K_{t+W-1}\cdots K_t d_t
+
\sum_{j=0}^{W-1} K_{t+W-1}\cdots K_{t+j+1} b_{t+j}.
\]
By assumption, the first term is dominated by $\bar K d_t$. Since each $K_s\preceq K^{\max}$ and each $b_{t+j}\preceq \bar b$, the second term is dominated entrywise by
\[
\sum_{j=0}^{W-1} (K^{\max})^{W-1-j}\bar b = G_W\bar b.
\]
This proves the window recursion. Iterating it yields the sampled bound, and the Neumann series is entrywise finite because $\rho(\bar K)<1$. The within-window estimate follows by unrolling at most $W-1$ more steps and replacing each $K_s$ by $K^{\max}$ and each disturbance by $\bar b$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Conservatism of the entrywise window envelope]
The small-gain wrapper is intentionally conservative. Entrywise nonnegative window envelopes discard sign cancellation, nonnormal transient geometry, and Lyapunov arguments that can certify stability even when the max-entry envelope looks too large. The theorem is therefore a replayable sufficient wrapper, not a sharp characterization of all stable evaluator-policy couplings. Its practical role is to provide a certifiable public contract, accepting false negatives rather than permitting unverifiable stabilizing folklore.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Static specialization]\label{cor:static_small_gain}
Under Assumption~\ref{ass:gain_matrix} with $W=1$ and $K_t\equiv K$, Theorem~\ref{thm:small_gain} reduces to the static latent-scaffold one-step specialization.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Then $K^{\max}=\bar K=K$ and $G_W=I$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Explicit evaluator-drift ceiling]\label{cor:yardstick_ceiling}
Under Theorem~\ref{thm:small_gain},
\[
D_t^{\mathrm{yard}}
=
\norm{e_{t+1}-e_t}
\le
 d_{t+1}^{(e)} + d_t^{(e)} + \bar D_E^\star,
\]
where $d_t^{(e)}$ denotes the evaluator component of $d_t$. Hence
\[
\sup_{t\ge 0} D_t^{\mathrm{yard}}
\le
\bar D_E^\star + 2\sup_{t\ge0}d_t^{(e)}<\infty.
\]
In particular, bounded reference drift plus admissible window contraction implies a finite ceiling on endogenous yardstick drift.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
By the triangle inequality,
\[
\norm{e_{t+1}-e_t}
\le
\norm{e_{t+1}-e_{t+1}^\star}+\norm{e_{t+1}^\star-e_t^\star}+\norm{e_t^\star-e_t}.
\]
Recognize the first and third terms as evaluator components of the deviation vector and apply Theorem~\ref{thm:small_gain} together with the within-window bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Explicit policy-manifest drift ceiling]\label{cor:policy_ceiling}
Under Theorem~\ref{thm:small_gain}, the replayably transported policy-manifest drift obeys
\[
D_{\Pi,t}^{\mathrm{yard}}
\Defeq
\delta_{\Pi,t+1}^{\mathrm{tr}}(\Pi_{t+1},\Pi_t)
\le d_{t+1}^{(\Pi)} + d_t^{(\Pi)} + \bar D_\Pi^\star,
\]
where $d_t^{(\Pi)}$ is the policy coordinate of $d_t$. Hence
\[
\sup_{t\ge 0} D_{\Pi,t}^{\mathrm{yard}}
\le
\bar D_\Pi^\star + 2\sup_{t\ge0} d_t^{(\Pi)}<\infty.
\]
Thus bounded window contraction controls not only evaluator drift but also replayably measurable ruler drift.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply the same triangle inequality argument as in Corollary~\ref{cor:yardstick_ceiling}, but in the transported policy pseudometric declared by the active gauge-transport certificate.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Observable governance pseudometrics and gauge transport]\label{def:obs_pseudometrics}
For evaluator states $e,e'$ and memory states $m,m'$, let
\[
d_t^{E}(e,e')\ge 0,
\qquad
 d_t^{M}(m,m')\ge 0
\]
be replayable pseudometrics computed from fixed public probe families, challenge cohorts, or retrieval tests under the active parser and environment regime. Let
\[
d_t^{\Pi}(\Pi,\Pi')\ge 0
\]
be a replayable pseudometric on policy manifests, computed from declared parser registries, routing manifests, retrieval contracts, admission logic, and other policy objects that affect how later evidence is interpreted. These pseudometrics may identify states that are observationally indistinguishable under the audit interface, so only the induced equivalence classes matter. Typical instances are worst-case score disagreement on a frozen challenge family for $d_t^{E}$, contradiction-tagged retrieval-semantic disagreement for $d_t^{M}$, and manifest-level behavioral disagreement on a fixed policy probe suite for $d_t^{\Pi}$.

When the active probe family itself changes over time, the policy is assumed to expose a replayable gauge-transport certificate: successor probe families are linked to predecessor families by transport maps together with declared comparison constants
\[
0<\underline\kappa_E\le \bar\kappa_E<\infty,
\qquad
0<\underline\kappa_M\le \bar\kappa_M<\infty,
\qquad
0<\underline\kappa_\Pi\le \bar\kappa_\Pi<\infty,
\]
such that all admissible state pairs satisfy
\[
\underline\kappa_E\, d_t^{E}(e,e') \le d_{t+1}^{E,\mathrm{tr}}(e,e') \le \bar\kappa_E\, d_t^{E}(e,e'),
\]
\[
\underline\kappa_M\, d_t^{M}(m,m') \le d_{t+1}^{M,\mathrm{tr}}(m,m') \le \bar\kappa_M\, d_t^{M}(m,m'),
\]
\[
\underline\kappa_\Pi\, d_t^{\Pi}(\Pi,\Pi') \le d_{t+1}^{\Pi,\mathrm{tr}}(\Pi,\Pi') \le \bar\kappa_\Pi\, d_t^{\Pi}(\Pi,\Pi').
\]
Thus boundedness in these coordinates is not allowed to arise merely by silently changing the ruler. These pseudometrics, rather than raw parameter norms, are the governance-relevant distortion quantities in open-ended regimes.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Productive capability functional]\label{def:productive_capability}
A \emph{productive capability functional} is a replayable map $\kappa:\R^{d_x}\to\R_+$ together with a public certification rule such that $\Delta\kappa_t=[\kappa(x_{t+1})-\kappa(x_t)]_+$ counts only capability increments that survive the active rollback, replay, and task-scope filters. In particular, the certification rule must assign zero increment to pure rollback, parameter relabeling, parser-only churn that leaves the declared task interface unchanged, policy-manifest rewrites that only reparameterize routing or evaluation without enlarging productive scope, and other representational rewrites that do not enlarge the policy-declared productive interface. Typical instances are monotone task-scope coverage, challenge-certified benchmark frontier expansion, or replay-certified new control affordances under a fixed external interface. Direct productive increment is therefore intentionally narrower than long-run growth contribution: governance edits that leave $\Delta\kappa_t=0$ are handled separately through the governance-capital frontier theorems below, where they appear as certified investments that enlarge future admissible productive opportunity rather than as immediate task-capability increments.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Constructive route to the window-summable spillover envelope]\label{prop:constructive_spillover}
Suppose productive increments are partitioned into replayable classes $j\in\mathcal J$ with per-unit governance spillover vectors $s^{(j)}\in\R_+^6$, and suppose the published admission contracts imply per-window certified increment quotas $M_{t,W}^{(j)}$ for each class, for example through protected-lane workload caps, deployment quotas, or bounded-scope edit contracts. If for every window
\[
\sum_{j\in\mathcal J} s^{(j)} M_{t,W}^{(j)} \preceq \bar u
\]
for some replayably published finite vector $\bar u$, then the forcing premise of Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open} holds with that same $\bar u$. Thus the open-ended small-gain theorem can be instantiated from certified capability classes and public per-window quotas rather than by postulating a free spillover constant.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The total governance forcing created by productive increments in a window is the sum over classes of per-unit spillover times admitted class mass. The displayed quota inequality therefore directly upper-bounds the window forcing term in Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open}.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Gauge-invariant incremental small-gain stability under open-ended capability growth]\label{thm:incremental_open}
Let $e_t^{\dagger}$, $m_t^{\dagger}$, and $\Pi_t^{\dagger}$ be any predictable scaffold processes in the observable equivalence classes tracked by Definition~\ref{def:obs_pseudometrics}, and let $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}$ denote the active policy-maintained audit set. Adopt the convention that if $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}=\varnothing$, then replay fragility is set to $1$ rather than $0$: an empty audit set is treated as maximal fragility, not as perfect robustness. Equivalently one may take $\inf \varnothing\Defeq 0$ in the displayed coordinate. Define the governance state
\[
y_t\Defeq \begin{bmatrix}
d_t^{E}(e_t,e_t^{\dagger})\\
d_t^{M}(m_t,m_t^{\dagger})\\
d_t^{\Pi}(\Pi_t,\Pi_t^{\dagger})\\
q_t\\
r_t\\
1-\inf_{a\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}}G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}(a)
\end{bmatrix}\in\R_+^6
\]
and let $\kappa:\R^{d_x}\to\R_+$ be any productive capability functional in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:productive_capability}. Define
\[
\Delta \kappa_t\Defeq \bigl[\kappa(x_{t+1})-\kappa(x_t)\bigr]_+.
\]
Suppose there exist predictable nonnegative matrices $A_t\in\R_+^{6\times 6}$, $B_t\in\R_+^{6\times 1}$, and vectors $c_t\in\R_+^6$ with
\[
0\preceq A_t\preceq A^{\max},\qquad 0\preceq c_t\preceq \bar c
\]
for some finite $A^{\max}$ and $\bar c$, a window length $W\in\N$, and a nonnegative matrix $\bar A$ with $\rho(\bar A)<1$ such that
\[
y_{t+1}\preceq A_t y_t + B_t\Delta \kappa_t + c_t,
\qquad
A_{t+W-1}\cdots A_t \preceq \bar A
\qquad\text{for all }t.
\]
Assume further that there exists a nonnegative vector $\bar u$ such that for every window,
\[
\sum_{j=0}^{W-1}
A_{t+W-1}\cdots A_{t+j+1} B_{t+j}\Delta \kappa_{t+j}
\preceq \bar u.
\]
Then $\|y_t\|_\infty$ is uniformly bounded over time. In particular, the capability path may remain open-ended --- even
\[
\sum_{t=0}^{\infty}\Delta \kappa_t = \infty
\]
--- while the \emph{projected governance coordinates tracked by $y_t$} (evaluator distortion, memory distortion, policy-manifest distortion, queue, debt, and replay fragility) stay uniformly bounded, provided that productive capability-to-governance spillovers are window-summable.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Unrolling one window gives
\[
y_{t+W}
\preceq
A_{t+W-1}\cdots A_t y_t
+
\sum_{j=0}^{W-1}A_{t+W-1}\cdots A_{t+j+1}B_{t+j}\Delta \kappa_{t+j}
+
\sum_{j=0}^{W-1}A_{t+W-1}\cdots A_{t+j+1}c_{t+j}.
\]
By assumption, the first term is dominated by $\bar A y_t$ and the second by $\bar u$. Because each $A_s\preceq A^{\max}$ and each $c_{t+j}\preceq \bar c$, the third term is bounded by
\[
\bar c_W \Defeq \sum_{j=0}^{W-1}(A^{\max})^{W-1-j}\bar c.
\]
Therefore the sampled process satisfies
\[
y_{(n+1)W}\preceq \bar A y_{nW} + \bar u + \bar c_W.
\]
Iterating yields
\[
y_{nW}\preceq \bar A^n y_0 + \sum_{j=0}^{n-1}\bar A^j(\bar u+\bar c_W)
\preceq
\bar A^n y_0 + (I-\bar A)^{-1}(\bar u+\bar c_W),
\]
which is uniformly bounded because $\rho(\bar A)<1$. The intermediate within-window states are bounded by unrolling at most $W-1$ more steps and replacing each $A_s$ by $A^{\max}$ and each disturbance by the corresponding public envelope. Temporal gauge-transport comparability ensures that this boundedness is not a measurement artifact induced by changing evaluator, memory, or policy probes over time.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Gauge transport and coordinate invariance of governance ceilings]\label{prop:gauge_transport}
Suppose Definition~\ref{def:obs_pseudometrics} holds with temporal comparison constants $(\underline\kappa_E,\bar\kappa_E,\underline\kappa_M,\bar\kappa_M,\underline\kappa_\Pi,\bar\kappa_\Pi)$ and that Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open} yields bounded governance coordinates in one admissible gauge. Then every other replayably transported gauge family satisfying the same comparison inequalities yields bounded evaluator, memory, and policy-manifest distortions as well, up to the declared multiplicative constants. Hence the theorem certifies bounded governability on observable equivalence classes rather than in a single arbitrary coordinate chart.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The transport inequalities bound every successor-gauge evaluator, memory, and policy distortion above and below by fixed multiples of the original pseudometric coordinates. Uniform boundedness in one gauge therefore implies uniform boundedness in any replayably comparable gauge. The queue, debt, and replay-fragility coordinates are unchanged.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Why the reference theorem and the incremental theorem coexist]
Theorem~\ref{thm:small_gain} is the correct wrapper for local loop regularity around a co-moving scaffold, for example during controlled migration phases, bounded rewrites, or policy-certified operating regions. Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open} addresses the different question raised by open-ended capability growth: whether the governance variables can remain bounded even when no fixed capability target exists. The two statements are therefore complementary rather than competing.
\end{remark}
\begin{remark}[Scope of the incremental theorem]\label{rem:incremental_scope}
Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open} is intentionally a projected-governance statement. It does \emph{not} by itself bound contradiction mass, robust semantic volume, heterodoxy routing load, proof-budget workload, or physical escrow ratios; those quantities are controlled by the separate contradiction, proof-language, and resource-escrow interfaces introduced later. The point is to make the projection explicit rather than to smuggle every governance variable into one omnibus norm.
\end{remark}
\subsection{Improvement half-life and shadow certification}
\begin{proposition}[One-sided shadow-certification bridge]\label{prop:shadow_bridge}
Fix horizon $H\in\N\cup\{\infty\}$ and discount factor $\beta\in(0,1]$, with $\beta<1$ when $H=\infty$. Fix a proposal issued at time $t$ satisfying $\mathsf{Comp}_t(u_t)=1$. Suppose that for every admissible comparator witness $c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$ and every $h\ge1$,
\[
\E\bigl[V(z_{t+h}^{u_t,c})-V(z_{t+h}^{0,c})\mid \mathcal F_t\bigr]
\ge
\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c).
\]
Let $\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\Defeq \max_{c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)}\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c)$. Assume additionally, when $H=\infty$, that
\[
\sum_{h=1}^{\infty}\beta^{h-1}\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}<\infty
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\sum_{h=1}^{\infty}\beta^{h-1}\bigl|\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)\bigr|<\infty.
\]
Then
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)
\ge
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\bigr),
\]
with the convergent infinite-horizon interpretation when $H=\infty$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Because $\mathsf{Comp}_t(u_t)=1$, every admissible comparator witness $c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$ is defined on a common continuation skeleton with explicit distortion budget. Apply the displayed operational-target inequality term by term to each witness-specific discounted sum, subtract the corresponding comparison-distortion term, and then take the minimum over comparator witnesses. This yields the displayed lower bound for the lower oracle endpoint $\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Symmetric shadow calibration envelope]\label{prop:shadow_bridge_symmetric}
If, in addition to the lower envelope of Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge}, there exists a replayably published upper operational target $\overline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)$ such that for every admissible comparator witness $c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$,
\[
\E\bigl[V(z_{t+h}^{u_t,c})-V(z_{t+h}^{0,c})\mid \mathcal F_t\bigr]
\le
\overline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)+\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c),
\]
and, when $H=\infty$,
\[
\sum_{h=1}^{\infty}\beta^{h-1}\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}<\infty,
\qquad
\sum_{h=1}^{\infty}\beta^{h-1}\bigl|\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)\bigr|<\infty,
\qquad
\sum_{h=1}^{\infty}\beta^{h-1}\bigl|\overline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)\bigr|<\infty.
\]
Then
\[
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\bigr)
\le
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)
\le
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta,\mathrm{hi}}(u_t)
\le
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\overline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)+\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\bigr).
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Combine the lower bound from Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge} with the corresponding witnesswise upper bound and then take the maximum over comparator witnesses for the upper endpoint.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Shadow-contamination penalty and self-improvement speed limit]\label{prop:shadow_speed}
Fix a horizon $h\ge 1$ and a comparator-compatible proposal $u_t$. Suppose there exists a replayably published contamination envelope $\Omega_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cont}}\ge 0$ such that for every admissible comparator witness $c\in\mathfrak C_t(u_t)$,
\[
\E\bigl[V(z_{t+h}^{u_t,c})-V(z_{t+h}^{0,c})\mid\mathcal F_t\bigr]
\ge
\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}(c)-\Omega_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cont}},
\]
and suppose the manifest additionally certifies
\[
\Omega_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cont}}\le L_{\Shadow}S_t^{(L)} + \Delta_t^{\Shadow},
\]
where $L_{\Shadow}\ge 0$ is a public sensitivity constant, $S_t^{(L)}$ is the total accepted rewrite magnitude over the shadow lag window of length $L$, and $\Delta_t^{\Shadow}\ge 0$ is a public upper bound on additional shadow contamination from delayed parser, environment, or evaluator drift. Then the one-sided bridge of Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge} yields
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)
\ge
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}-L_{\Shadow}S_t^{(L)}-\Delta_t^{\Shadow}\bigr).
\]
Consequently, if an uncontaminated operational sign-separation margin $\eta_h>0$ is available at horizon $h$, then reliable sign identification at that horizon requires
\[
L_{\Shadow}S_t^{(L)} + \Delta_t^{\Shadow} < \eta_h.
\]
Equivalently, once the contamination budget is fixed, the admissible rewrite speed is bounded by
\[
S_t^{(L)} < \frac{\eta_h-\Delta_t^{\Shadow}}{L_{\Shadow}}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The witnesswise hypothesis already contains the operational target and the comparator-distortion term in the current notation. Substituting the displayed contamination upper bound into that witnesswise inequality, summing over horizons, and then minimizing over comparator witnesses gives the stated lower bound on $\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)$. The sign condition is the same inequality written so that the right-hand side remains positive at horizon $h$.
\end{proof}


\begin{theorem}[Two-clock shadow viability band under affine penalty envelopes]\label{thm:two_clock}
Suppose the shadow lane is refreshed at frequency $f_{\Shadow}>0$. Let the additional staleness penalty at horizon $h$ obey
\[
\Omega_h^{\mathrm{stale}}(f_{\Shadow}) \le a_h + \frac{b_h}{f_{\Shadow}},
\qquad a_h,b_h\ge 0,
\]
and let the contamination penalty obey
\[
\Omega_h^{\mathrm{cont}}(f_{\Shadow}) \le c_h + d_h f_{\Shadow},
\qquad c_h,d_h\ge 0.
\]
Assume the uncontaminated operational sign-separation margin at horizon $h$ exceeds zero by an amount $\eta_h>0$, meaning that before these penalties are applied one has
\[
\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\ge \eta_h.
\]
Then delayed-shadow sign certification at horizon $h$ is guaranteed whenever there exists $f_{\Shadow}>0$ such that
\[
\Omega_h^{\mathrm{stale}}(f_{\Shadow}) + \Omega_h^{\mathrm{cont}}(f_{\Shadow}) < \eta_h.
\]
Under the displayed affine upper envelopes, a sufficient condition for the existence of such a refresh frequency is
\[
M_h^2 > 4b_h d_h,
\qquad
M_h\Defeq \eta_h-a_h-c_h.
\]
Whenever this holds with $d_h>0$, every frequency in the open interval
\[
\frac{M_h-\sqrt{M_h^2-4b_h d_h}}{2d_h}
<
 f_{\Shadow}
<
\frac{M_h+\sqrt{M_h^2-4b_h d_h}}{2d_h}
\]
is sufficient for certification. If the affine envelopes are tight, the same condition and interval are also necessary.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Under the assumed envelopes, certification is guaranteed if
\[
\frac{b_h}{f_{\Shadow}} + d_h f_{\Shadow} < M_h.
\]
Multiplying by $f_{\Shadow}>0$ yields the quadratic inequality
\[
d_h f_{\Shadow}^2 - M_h f_{\Shadow} + b_h < 0.
\]
This inequality has a positive solution whenever the discriminant is positive, namely $M_h^2-4b_h d_h>0$. When this holds and $d_h>0$, the sufficient solution set is exactly the stated open interval between the two positive roots. If $d_h=0$, the condition reduces to $b_h/f_{\Shadow}<M_h$, which still gives a one-sided stale-versus-frozen feasibility threshold. Necessity requires tightness of the affine envelopes; absent tightness, the theorem intentionally states only a sufficient viability band.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Frozen shadows are not free]
Taking $f_{\Shadow}\to 0$ drives the staleness penalty $b_h/f_{\Shadow}$ to infinity whenever $b_h>0$. Thus the theory rules out the naive response ``never refresh the shadow at all.'' A completely frozen shadow avoids direct contamination, but it eventually loses relevance and therefore also loses certifying power.
\end{remark}
\begin{definition}[Replayable common-cause vulnerability cover]\label{def:vulnerability_cover}
Fix an active audit family $\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{aud}}$. A \emph{replayable common-cause vulnerability cover} for that family is a replayable collection of writable or influence channels $\mathcal C_t=\{C_1,\dots,C_m\}$ together with a surjective assignment from family members to channels such that every member can be jointly perturbed whenever the corresponding channel is captured, and the minimum cover size
\[
\chi_t^{\mathrm{cover}}\Defeq \min\{m: \mathcal C_t \text{ covers }\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{aud}}\}
\]
is itself replayably upper-bounded from manifests, declared writable scope, overlap certificates, or shared dependency roots. This cover formalizes synchronous common-cause capture rather than independent failures. The minimum-cover summary is intended as a structural stress-test object, not as a claim that cover size alone determines exploitability without the additional manifest-preserving forcing assumptions used below.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Adversarial cross-examination and epistemic singularity]\label{thm:epistemic_singularity}
Let $\mathfrak S_t$ and $\mathfrak R_t$ be the active shadow and refreezing audit families of Definition~\ref{def:audit_family}. Let $\phi_t^{\Shadow}$ and $\phi_t^{\Replay}$ be the replayable monotone calibrations that map the generic attack-reach envelope $A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}$ into the effective common-cause cover units used by the corresponding diversity reserves. For a challenged cohort issued at time $\tau$, define the endogenous integrity budget
\[
\widehat\Gamma_{\tau,h}^{\mathrm{int}}
\Defeq
\Delta_{\tau,h}^{\mathrm{xs}}
+ \kappa_{\mathrm{ov}}\,[1-\Xi_{\tau}^{\Shadow}]_+
+ \kappa_{\mathrm{adv}}\,[\phi_{\tau}^{\Shadow}(A_{\tau}^{\mathrm{adv}})-\Xi_{\tau}^{\Shadow}]_+,
\]
with policy constants $\kappa_{\mathrm{ov}},\kappa_{\mathrm{adv}}\ge0$. Then any lower-margin sign certificate at horizon $h$ that would otherwise use an oracle collusion budget remains valid after subtracting $\widehat\Gamma_{\tau,h}^{\mathrm{int}}$. Likewise any refreezing certificate may replace an oracle semantic floor by the endogenous floor $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$.

Conversely, suppose
\[
\phi_{\tau}^{\Shadow}(A_{\tau}^{\mathrm{adv}})\ge \Xi_{\tau}^{\Shadow}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\phi_t^{\Replay}(A_t^{\mathrm{adv}})\ge \Xi_t^{\Replay},
\]
and suppose moreover that the active shadow family and replay family each admit replayable common-cause vulnerability covers in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:vulnerability_cover} whose minimum cover sizes are upper-bounded by $\phi_t^{\Shadow}(A_t^{\mathrm{adv}})$ and $\phi_t^{\Replay}(A_t^{\mathrm{adv}})$, respectively, whenever the corresponding diversity reserve thresholds $\Xi_t^{\Shadow}$ and $\Xi_t^{\Replay}$ are met. Assume finally that each such cover is manifest-preserving and familywise output-forcing: capture of the cover channel can synchronize the reported outputs of all mapped family members while leaving the public logs, public manifests, and visible replay transcripts unchanged. Then there exist two recursive-improvement worlds with identical public logs, arbitrarily small cross-shadow disagreement radius $\Delta_{\tau,h}^{\mathrm{xs}}$, identical endogenous semantic floors $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$, yet opposite discounted stable-gain sign or opposite true semantic-retention status. The first time at which the displayed calibrated inequalities and the common-cause cover condition hold is an \emph{epistemic singularity}: beyond that point, no observable-only internal audit rule can distinguish genuine agreement from jointly captured agreement.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is immediate because any oracle-free certificate must remain valid after accounting for the largest observable disagreement term and for the public penalties attached to overlap and attack reach; the displayed envelope simply upper-bounds the integrity disturbance that was formerly abstracted as an exogenous constant.

For the converse, use the common-cause cover hypothesis to choose a replayable vulnerability cover spanning each active audit family. By the manifest-preserving and familywise output-forcing assumptions, once attack reach exceeds the diversity reserve the accepted proposal can synchronize the reported challenged scores of the entire shadow family and the reported semantic-retention witnesses of the entire refreezing family without altering the public logs or manifests. Keep the visible histories identical across two worlds, but let the hidden slow consequences differ in sign, exactly as in Theorem~\ref{thm:ruler_nogo}. Public disagreement can then be made arbitrarily small even though the true discounted stable gain or true semantic retention differs across worlds. Hence beyond the singularity threshold the ambiguity is observationally irreducible.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Editable rulers enlarge the ambiguity class]\label{rem:ruler_nogo_scope}
The construction above uses only a hidden slow state and observational equivalence on the public lane. Editable evaluators, parser registries, and routing policies are not needed for the impossibility theorem itself. They matter because, in actual recursive-improvement systems, they enlarge the set of observably equivalent worlds by changing which probes, challenge cohorts, and replay environments remain available. The no-go result should therefore be read as a hidden-state impossibility first and an evaluator-edit warning second.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[No-meta interpretation of public bounds]
The theorem does not reintroduce an external judge. It does the opposite: it replaces fixed integrity and semantic-retention constants by replayable envelopes computed from family disagreement, provenance overlap, and declared writable scope. The price of staying no-meta is that these envelopes can collapse once attack reach dominates audit diversity; the theory makes that limit explicit rather than hiding it inside a comforting constant.
\end{remark}


\begin{definition}[Steganographic scrubber and information-bottlenecked shadow input]\label{def:scrubber}
Let $p_t$ denote the public manifest of proposal $u_t$, including declared claim, replay artifact, typed-diff metadata, and any certificates accepted by policy. A family of shadow inputs is \emph{scrubbed} if each shadow lane $m$ receives
\[
\tilde u_t^{(m)} = S^{(m)}_{\mathrm{scrub}}(u_t,p_t;\omega_t^{(m)}),
\]
where $\omega_t^{(m)}$ is lane-local randomness, and there exist public constants $\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}},\varepsilon_{\times}\ge 0$ such that
\[
I\!\left(U_t;\tilde U_t^{(m)}\mid P_t\right)\le \varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}},
\qquad
I\!\left(\tilde U_t^{(m)};\tilde U_t^{(m')}\mid P_t\right)\le \varepsilon_{\times}
\quad(m\neq m').
\]
Thus each shadow lane sees at most a bounded amount of proposal information beyond the public manifest, and the hidden excess information shared across distinct lanes is likewise bounded.
\end{definition}

\begin{assumption}[Normalized coordinatewise audit-margin certificate class]\label{ass:audit_margin_lipschitz}
For each challenged cohort and audit horizon, the certified shadow margin can be written in the normalized form
\[
\Lambda
=
\Lambda_0(P_t)
+
\sum_{m=1}^{M_t} w_m \, \E[T_t^{(m)}\mid P_t]
-
\sum_{1\le m<m'\le M_t} v_{mm'} \, \E[B_t^{(m,m')}\mid P_t],
\]
where $T_t^{(m)},B_t^{(m,m')}\in[-1,1]$ are replayable lanewise and pairwise bounded audit statistics, $w_m,v_{mm'}\ge 0$, and the total weights satisfy
\[
\sum_{m=1}^{M_t} w_m + \sum_{1\le m<m'\le M_t} v_{mm'} \le 1.
\]
Hence the certified margin is coordinatewise Lipschitz in total variation: if two conditional laws agree on $P_t$ and induce lanewise total-variation deviations at most $\delta_m$ and pairwise deviations at most $\delta_{mm'}$, then
\[
\abs{\Lambda(\mathsf P)-\Lambda(\mathsf Q)}
\le 2\sum_{m=1}^{M_t} w_m \, \delta_m
+2\sum_{1\le m<m'\le M_t} v_{mm'} \, \delta_{mm'}.
\]
This covers normalized weighted averages of bounded lane scores together with normalized cross-lane consistency penalties.
\end{assumption}

\begin{lemma}[Seed-to-output data processing for scrubbed lanes]\label{lem:seed_output_tv}
Fix the public manifest $P_t$. If a scrubbed lane output is generated by a measurable map of the proposal, the manifest, and lane-local randomness, then total-variation deviations on the hidden proposal or seed inputs upper-bound the corresponding total-variation deviations on the scrubbed lane outputs and on their pairwise joint laws. This is an immediate data-processing consequence of the fact that the scrubber map is applied after those hidden inputs are drawn \cite[Chapters~2 and~17]{CoverThomas2006}.
\end{lemma}

\begin{proof}
Condition on $P_t$ and couple the hidden inputs. Applying the same measurable scrubber map to both coupled inputs cannot increase total variation.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Steganographic scrubbing and information-theoretic isolation]\label{thm:steg_scrub}
Suppose the cross-examination setting of Theorem~\ref{thm:epistemic_singularity} is augmented with a scrubbed shadow family in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:scrubber}, and assume the normalized coordinatewise certificate class of Assumption~\ref{ass:audit_margin_lipschitz}. Then the conditional expected covert-channel-induced inflation of any normalized certified shadow margin is bounded by the explicit modulus
\[
\Psi(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}},\varepsilon_{\times})
\Defeq
2\sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}}}+2\sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\times}}.
\]
Consequently every expected-margin oracle-free sign certificate remains valid after replacing the endogenous integrity envelope by
\[
\widehat\Gamma_{\tau,h}^{\mathrm{int}} + \Psi(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}},\varepsilon_{\times}).
\]

Conversely, if the shadow family consumes raw proposal data without such a scrubber and there exists a manifest-invisible trigger channel to which each shadow lane is replayably sensitive, then there exist proposal streams with $A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}=0$ whose hidden triggers synchronously perturb every shadow lane while leaving the public manifest unchanged. Writable-scope separation alone therefore does not rule out covert collusion.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Condition on the public manifest $P_t$. By Pinsker's inequality and the conditional mutual-information bound, each lanewise deviation between the scrubbed conditional law that still sees $U_t$ and the manifest-only conditional law is bounded by
\[
\delta_m
\Defeq d_{\mathrm{TV}}\!\bigl(\mathcal L(\tilde U_t^{(m)}\mid U_t,P_t),\mathcal L(\tilde U_t^{(m)}\mid P_t)\bigr)
\le \sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}}}
\]
in expectation, while each pairwise deviation between the true pair law and the product of its manifest-only marginals is bounded by
\[
\delta_{mm'}
\Defeq d_{\mathrm{TV}}\!\bigl(\mathcal L(\tilde U_t^{(m)},\tilde U_t^{(m')}\mid P_t),\mathcal L(\tilde U_t^{(m)}\mid P_t)\otimes \mathcal L(\tilde U_t^{(m')}\mid P_t)\bigr)
\le \sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\times}}.
\]
Assumption~\ref{ass:audit_margin_lipschitz} then yields
\[
\abs{\Delta \Lambda}
\le 2\sum_m w_m \, \delta_m + 2\sum_{m<m'} v_{mm'} \, \delta_{mm'}
\le 2\sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}}}+2\sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\times}},
\]
because the total coordinate weights are normalized to at most one. This is the stated modulus.

For the converse, raw proposal access plus a manifest-invisible trigger channel gives a common covert input not represented in $P_t$. If every shadow lane is sensitive to that channel, a proposal writer can choose a trigger-bearing stream that leaves the public manifest unchanged while shifting every lane's hidden input in the same adversarial direction. The synchronized distortion therefore survives writable-scope separation whenever the raw channel remains unsanitized.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Clarification on scrubbers]
The scrubber is not a magical semantic judge that knows the true meaning of the proposal. It is a public, lossy interface contract on what information may flow into audit lanes beyond the replayable manifest. The point is to cap covert coordination bandwidth, not to solve semantics by fiat.
\end{remark}
\begin{remark}[Clarification on scrubber randomness]
Theorem~\ref{thm:steg_scrub} conditions on whatever unpredictability remains in the lane-local seeds $\omega_t^{(m)}$ from the proposal writer's viewpoint. If those seeds become predictable through shared operating-system state or a writable pseudo-random generator, the scrubber can degenerate into a deterministic map. The next definition and theorem make that dependence explicit rather than leaving it implicit.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Entropy-isolated scrubber randomness]\label{def:entropy_isolation}
A scrubbed shadow family satisfies the \emph{entropy-isolation invariant} if each lane-local seed $\omega_t^{(m)}$ is generated by an entropy source outside writable proposal scope and policy publishes a replayable unpredictability certificate relative to the attacker-visible pre-decision state $\mathcal F_t$ and writable-scope measurements. The certificate may be either direct or extractor-based, for example by a leftover-hash-style extractor whose residual is published explicitly rather than inferred from min-entropy alone \cite{BarakEtAl2011LHL,NIST90B2018}, but it must certify a conditional seed residual
\[
d_{\mathrm{TV}}\!\left(\mathcal L(\omega_t^{(m)}\mid \mathcal F_t,A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}),\mathrm{Unif}(\Omega_m)\right) \le \varepsilon_{\omega}.
\]
If an extractor route is used, the theorem consumes only the resulting residual $\varepsilon_{\omega}$ rather than an implicit min-entropy-to-TV leap. In addition, distinct lane seeds satisfy the public cross-seed dependence bound
\[
I\!\left(\omega_t^{(m)};\omega_t^{(m')} \mid \mathcal F_t\right) \le \varepsilon_{\omega,\times}
\qquad(m\neq m').
\]
Thus no proposal writer controlling writable scope can fully predict or deterministically synchronize the scrubber randomness across lanes.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Entropy isolation law and true cryptographic scrubbing]\label{thm:entropy_isolation}
Suppose Definition~\ref{def:scrubber} holds, the scrubber randomness further satisfies Definition~\ref{def:entropy_isolation}, the seed-to-output data-processing lemma (Lemma~\ref{lem:seed_output_tv}) applies to the scrubber family, and the normalized coordinatewise certificate class of Assumption~\ref{ass:audit_margin_lipschitz} also holds. Then every shadow-margin certificate valid under Theorem~\ref{thm:steg_scrub} remains valid after adding the seed-isolation residual
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{iso}}(\varepsilon_{\omega},\varepsilon_{\omega,\times})
\Defeq
2\varepsilon_{\omega}+2\sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\omega,\times}},
\]
so that the total certified residual becomes
\[
\Psi_{\mathrm{tot}}
\Defeq
\Psi(\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}},\varepsilon_{\times})
+
\Psi_{\mathrm{iso}}(\varepsilon_{\omega},\varepsilon_{\omega,\times}).
\]
In particular, entropy isolation improves scrubber security through a directly certified total-variation residual rather than through an implicit min-entropy-to-TV leap. In the idealized zero-leakage scrubber limit $\varepsilon_{\mathrm{scrub}}=\varepsilon_{\times}=0$, the only remaining certificate penalty is the seed-isolation residual.

Conversely, if the attacker-conditioned seed residual is effectively maximal so that the seeds are known to the proposal writer, and the scrubber class is rich enough that deterministic preimages can preserve a trigger through the scrubber map, then the scrubber becomes deterministic from the attacker's viewpoint and there exist covert-trigger proposal streams that preserve the public manifest while defeating the intended scrubbing barrier. Thus lossy interfaces without entropy isolation do not provide information-theoretic isolation.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The forward direction augments Theorem~\ref{thm:steg_scrub} with attacker uncertainty about the lane-local seeds. The direct residual $\varepsilon_{\omega}$ already controls, in total variation, how far each lane-local seed law can be from an ideal manifest-independent seed. By Lemma~\ref{lem:seed_output_tv}, the same residual upper-bounds the induced perturbation on each scrubbed lane output. The cross-lane dependence budget contributes at most $\sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\omega,\times}}$ in total variation by Pinsker's inequality, and the same data-processing lemma carries that bound to the pairwise scrubbed-output law. Applying Assumption~\ref{ass:audit_margin_lipschitz} therefore adds at most
\[
2\varepsilon_{\omega}+2\sqrt{2\varepsilon_{\omega,\times}}
\]
to the certified margin residual, which must be added to rather than substituted for the scrubber residual already bounded in Theorem~\ref{thm:steg_scrub}.

For the converse, if the seeds are effectively known and the scrubber map admits deterministic trigger-preserving preimages, then the proposal writer can optimize directly against that deterministic map and embed a trigger that survives scrubbing while remaining absent from the public manifest. This reconstructs the covert-channel failure mode despite nominal scrubbing.
\end{proof}


\begin{assumption}[Monotone retention envelopes]\label{ass:retention_bounds}
There exist nondecreasing functions
\[
\phi_D^-,\phi_D^+,\phi_Q^-,\phi_Q^+:
\R_+\to\R_+
\]
with
\[
\phi_D^+(x)\ge \phi_D^-(x)\ge 0,
\qquad
\phi_Q^+(x)\ge \phi_Q^-(x)\ge 0,
\qquad
\phi_D^{\pm}(0)=\phi_Q^{\pm}(0)=0,
\]
such that for every proposal issued at time $t$ and every horizon $h\ge1$,
\[
\mathcal M_t(0)-\phi_D^+\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)-\phi_Q^+\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr)
\le
\mathcal M_t(h)
\le
\mathcal M_t(0)-\phi_D^-\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)-\phi_Q^-\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr),
\]
where
\[
Q_t(h)\Defeq \sum_{s=t}^{t+h-1}q_s.
\]
\end{assumption}

\begin{remark}[Identification status of the retention envelopes]\label{rem:retention_identification}
Assumption~\ref{ass:retention_bounds} is intentionally an envelope assumption rather than a first-principles identification theorem. The functions $\phi_D^{\pm}$ and $\phi_Q^{\pm}$ must be estimated or stress-tested from logged drift, backlog, and retained-margin data, possibly with regime-dependent envelopes if the operating region is not stationary. The resulting half-life law is therefore an \emph{auditable crossing algebra}: it is sharp conditional on the published envelopes, but the empirical sharpness of the envelopes remains a separate estimation problem.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Generalized realized improvement half-life crossing law]\label{thm:half_life}
Assume \ref{ass:retention_bounds}. For a proposal issued at time $t$ with $\mathcal M_t(0)>0$, define the lower and upper crossing indices
\[
\tau_t^{-}\Defeq \inf\left\{h\ge1: \phi_D^+\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)+\phi_Q^+\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr)\ge \tfrac12\mathcal M_t(0)\right\},
\]
\[
\tau_t^{+}\Defeq \inf\left\{h\ge1: \phi_D^-\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)+\phi_Q^-\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr)\ge \tfrac12\mathcal M_t(0)\right\},
\]
with the convention $\inf\varnothing=\infty$. Then
\[
\tau_t^{-}\le \tau_{1/2}(t)\le \tau_t^{+}.
\]
In particular, if the lower crossing set is nonempty then the half-life is finite, and if the upper crossing set is empty then the half-life cannot yet have occurred on the observed horizon.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
From Assumption~\ref{ass:retention_bounds},
\[
\mathcal M_t(h)\ge \mathcal M_t(0)-\phi_D^+\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)-\phi_Q^+\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr).
\]
Hence whenever $\phi_D^+\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)+\phi_Q^+\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr)<\tfrac12\mathcal M_t(0)$, we still have $\mathcal M_t(h)>\tfrac12\mathcal M_t(0)$, so the half-life event has not yet happened. This proves $\tau_t^-\le \tau_{1/2}(t)$. Similarly,
\[
\mathcal M_t(h)\le \mathcal M_t(0)-\phi_D^-\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)-\phi_Q^-\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr),
\]
so once $\phi_D^-\!\bigl(\mathcal D_t(h)\bigr)+\phi_Q^-\!\bigl(Q_t(h)\bigr)\ge \tfrac12\mathcal M_t(0)$, the half-life inequality must hold. Therefore $\tau_{1/2}(t)\le \tau_t^+$.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Linear specialization of the half-life crossing law]\label{cor:half_life_coarse}
Assume \ref{ass:retention_bounds} with
\[
\phi_D^\pm(x)=L_D^\pm x,
\qquad
\phi_Q^\pm(x)=L_q^\pm x,
\]
where $L_D^+\ge L_D^-\ge 0$ and $L_q^+\ge L_q^-\ge 0$. If for all $s\ge t$,
\[
\underline D \le D_s^{\mathrm{yard}}\le \bar D,
\qquad
0\le q_s\le \bar q,
\]
and if the displayed denominators are positive, then
\[
\left\lceil \frac{\mathcal M_t(0)}{2(L_D^+\bar D + L_q^+\bar q)} \right\rceil
\le
\tau_{1/2}(t)
\le
\left\lceil \frac{\mathcal M_t(0)}{2L_D^-\underline D} \right\rceil.
\]
The upper bound uses only the drift floor and remains meaningful even if healthy operation drives the queue to zero on many steps.
\end{corollary}
