\begin{proof}
Use $\mathcal D_t(h)\le h\bar D$ and $Q_t(h)\le h\bar q$ for the lower bound on $\tau_{1/2}(t)$, and $\mathcal D_t(h)\ge h\underline D$ together with $Q_t(h)\ge 0$ for the upper bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Certified stable improvement from replayable retained-margin certificates]\label{cor:shadow_cert}
Fix a proposal satisfying $\mathsf{Comp}_t(u_t)=1$, and suppose there exists a replayable retained-margin lower certificate $\{\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)\}_{h\ge 1}$ in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:retained_margin_cert}; by Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_to_shadow}, one operational way to obtain such a certificate is to combine a class-conditional delayed-challenge certificate with a published transport-calibration family. Under Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge}, a sufficient condition for a nonnegative replayable lower bound on discounted stable gain is
\[
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\bigr)\ge 0.
\]
If, in addition, the proposal-local escrow debt stays below the policy threshold so that $\eta_{t,H}^{\max}(u_t)\le \bar\delta_r(C_t)$, then the proposal satisfies the Interface-A and Interface-B clauses of $(H,\beta)$-certified stable improvement. If a replayable class-homogeneity envelope is also published and
\[
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\delta_h^{\mathrm{class}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\bigr)\ge 0,
\]
then the same condition upgrades the conclusion to oracle stable improvement for the cohort-specific retained-margin target as well.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
On the event $\mathsf{Comp}_t(u_t)=1$, Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge} gives
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)
\ge
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\bigr)
\ge
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\bigl(\underline{\mathcal M}_t^{\mathrm{op}}(h)-\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}\bigr),
\]
where the second inequality is exactly the lower-certificate property from Definition~\ref{def:retained_margin_cert}. Thus a nonnegative replayable operational lower certificate implies a nonnegative replayable lower bound on the lower oracle endpoint. The debt condition is the shared Interface-B clause in the definitions of certified and oracle stable improvement. If the class-homogeneity envelope is available, Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_to_shadow} supplies the additional oracle-margin lower certificate, and the final displayed inequality gives the oracle conclusion.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Proposal-local discounted debt budget]\label{prop:local_debt_budget}
Under Definition~\ref{def:cohort_escrow}, every cohort $\tau$ satisfies, for all $t\ge \tau$,
\[
\eta_{\tau,t}
\le
\alpha_r^{t-\tau}\bigl(\mathcal B_\tau(u_\tau)+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}}\bigr)
+
\sum_{s=\tau+1}^{t}\alpha_r^{t-s} a_{\tau,s}^{\mathrm{sec}}
+
\lambda_q\sum_{s=\tau}^{t-1}\alpha_r^{t-1-s} b_{\tau,s}.
\]
If, in addition, $a_{\tau,s}^{\mathrm{sec}}\le \bar a_{\tau}$ and $b_{\tau,s}\le \bar b_{\tau}$ for all $s\ge \tau$, and if $\alpha_r<1$, then
\[
\sup_{k\ge 0}\eta_{\tau,\tau+k}
\le
\max\left\{\mathcal B_\tau(u_\tau)+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}},\, \frac{\bar a_{\tau}+\lambda_q \bar b_{\tau}}{1-\alpha_r}\right\}.
\]
The same bound holds for every finite-horizon peak debt.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
From the cohort recursion,
\[
\eta_{\tau,t+1}
\le
\alpha_r\eta_{\tau,t} + a_{\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{sec}} + \lambda_q b_{\tau,t},
\]
because the matched-retirement increment and the explicit retirement fraction only reduce the stock. Iterating from
\[
\eta_{\tau,\tau}=\mathcal B_\tau(u_\tau)+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}}
\]
yields the displayed discounted budget. Under the uniform caps and $\alpha_r<1$,
\[
\eta_{\tau,\tau+k}
\le
\alpha_r^k\bigl(\mathcal B_\tau(u_\tau)+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_{\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}}\bigr)
+
\frac{(\bar a_{\tau}+\lambda_q\bar b_{\tau})(1-\alpha_r^k)}{1-\alpha_r},
\]
which is always bounded by the displayed maximum.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Observable debt certificate]\label{cor:observable_debt_cert}
Fix a proposal issued at time $t$. Suppose logs provide conservative upper bounds
\[
\bar B_t\ge \mathcal B_t(u_t),\qquad
\bar U_t^{\mathrm{rep}}\ge U_t^{\mathrm{rep}},\qquad
\bar U_t^{\mathrm{haz}}\ge U_t^{\mathrm{haz}},\qquad
\bar a_t\ge a_{t,s}^{\mathrm{sec}},\qquad
\bar b_t\ge b_{t,s}
\]
for all $s\ge t$. If $\alpha_r<1$ and
\[
\max\left\{\bar B_t+\bar U_t^{\mathrm{rep}}+\bar U_t^{\mathrm{haz}},\, \frac{\bar a_t+\lambda_q \bar b_t}{1-\alpha_r}\right\}
\le \bar\delta_r(C_t),
\]
then the debt part of the certified-stable-improvement criterion is certified for every horizon. Combined with Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow_cert}, a nonnegative calibrated lower stable-gain bound yields a fully operational sufficient \emph{certified stable-improvement} rule; adding base-admissibility and governance-safety certificates upgrades it to a full admissibility rule.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Proposition~\ref{prop:local_debt_budget} with the conservative bounds.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Bundled stable gain, bundled debt, and interaction debt]\label{def:interaction_debt}
Fix a bundle $U=\{u_t^{(1)},\dots,u_t^{(m)}\}$ of simultaneously admitted edits over horizon $(H,\beta)$. Let $\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(U)$ denote the discounted stable gain of the joint intervention that applies the whole bundle inside the common continuation skeleton. Let $\eta_{t,H}^{\max}(U)$ denote the corresponding bundle-level peak debt over the same horizon, and let $\mathsf{BaseAdm}_t(U)$ and $\mathsf{GovSafe}_{t,H}(U)$ denote the bundle-level base-admissibility and governance-safety predicates. Let $\underline{\mathcal G}_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t^{(i)})$ denote any replayable lower certificate for the discounted stable gain of edit $i$ when evaluated in isolation against the common baseline.

To make interaction debt constructive rather than existential, policy publishes a replayable interference graph on the issued bundle. For each pair $(i,j)$ with $i<j$, let
\[
\overline\Delta_{ij}
\Defeq
\lambda_{\mathrm{dep}}\,\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{dep}}
+\lambda_{\mathrm{wr}}\,\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{wr}}
+\lambda_{\mathrm{q}}\,\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{q}}
+\lambda_{\mathrm{h}}\,\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{h}},
\]
where $\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{dep}}$ is a replayable dependency-overlap envelope, $\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{wr}}$ is shared writable-scope overlap, $\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{q}}$ is protected-lane queue contention, and $\Omega_{ij}^{\mathrm{h}}$ is a replayable cross-sensitivity or cross-Hessian upper envelope on task or governance interference. Let $\overline\Delta_{\mathrm{ho}}(U)\ge 0$ be a replayable residual upper envelope for higher-order interaction not captured by the pairwise terms, for example from logged hyperedge overlap or a submodularity-defect bound. A \emph{constructive interaction-debt certificate} is the replayable nonpositive quantity
\[
\widehat\Lambda_{t,H}^{\mathrm{int}}(U)
\Defeq
-\sum_{1\le i<j\le m}\overline\Delta_{ij}
-\overline\Delta_{\mathrm{ho}}(U)
\le 0.
\]
The interaction debt of the bundle is any replayable nonpositive quantity $\Lambda_{t,H}^{\mathrm{int}}(U)$ satisfying
\[
\Lambda_{t,H}^{\mathrm{int}}(U)\le \widehat\Lambda_{t,H}^{\mathrm{int}}(U)\le 0
\]
and the stable-gain lower bound
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(U)\ge \sum_{i=1}^m \underline{\mathcal G}_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t^{(i)}) + \Lambda_{t,H}^{\mathrm{int}}(U).
\]
Thus interaction debt is tied to explicit shared writable scope, dependency overlap, queue interference, and cross-sensitivity envelopes rather than being left as a bare existential penalty.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Compositional certification under interaction debt]\label{prop:interaction_debt}
If a bundle $U$ satisfies
\[
\sum_{i=1}^m \underline{\mathcal G}_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t^{(i)}) + \Lambda_{t,H}^{\mathrm{int}}(U)\ge 0,
\qquad
\eta_{t,H}^{\max}(U)\le \bar\delta_r(C_t),
\qquad
\mathsf{BaseAdm}_t(U)=1,
\qquad
\mathsf{GovSafe}_{t,H}(U)=1,
\]
then the bundle is an $(H,\beta)$-full admissible improvement. In particular, individually certified edits need not compose unless interaction debt is also controlled.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The displayed stable-gain inequality furnishes a nonnegative replayable lower certificate for the discounted stable gain of the whole bundle. The bundle debt inequality gives certified stable improvement, while base admissibility and governance safety supply the remaining admission clauses. The final sentence follows because $\Lambda_{t,H}^{\mathrm{int}}(U)$ can be strictly negative even when each individual lower bound is nonnegative.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Admission decomposition and sufficient rule]\label{prop:master_admissibility}
For either a single proposal or a bundle of proposals, the conjunction
\[
\mathsf{BaseAdm}_t(\cdot)=1,\qquad
\underline{\mathcal G}_{t,H}^{\beta}(\cdot)\ge 0,\qquad
\eta_{t,H}^{\max}(\cdot)\le \bar\delta_r(C_t),\qquad
\mathsf{GovSafe}_{t,H}(\cdot)=1
\]
is sufficient for $(H,\beta)$-full admissibility. Thus the theory decomposes admission into a base replay-and-typing layer, a certified stable-gain layer, a debt layer, and a governance-safety layer rather than treating ``admissible'' as a single opaque predicate.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
This is immediate from the definition of full admissible improvement for single proposals and from Proposition~\ref{prop:interaction_debt} for bundles.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Ignoring any downside-reserve component enables Trojan under-reservation]\label{thm:blast_radius}
Suppose admission were based on an incomplete downside reserve, for example by initializing the proposal-local debt stock from claimed upside alone, or by omitting either the repair reserve or the persistent hazard reserve. Then for any debt threshold $\bar\delta_r>0$ and any family of proposals with arbitrarily large writable scope or dependency closure, there exist under-declared proposals with
\[
0\le [\Delta_t^{\mathrm{claim}}]_+<\bar\delta_r
\]
that still request arbitrarily large structural access. In that sense Trojan under-declaration is always possible when initial debt ignores structural blast radius, repair reserve, and persistent hazard reserve.

Under Definition~\ref{def:blast_radius} and Definition~\ref{def:cohort_escrow}, suppose there exists a public lower envelope $\mathcal H_t(u_t)$ on hidden-state or governance-surface reach such that
\[
\mathcal B_t(u_t)\ge \mathcal H_t(u_t)
\qquad\text{for all admissible proposals.}
\]
Then any proposal with $\mathcal H_t(u_t)>\bar\delta_r(C_t)$ necessarily has
\[
\eta_{t,t}\ge \mathcal B_t(u_t)>\bar\delta_r(C_t)
\]
and is rejected immediately, regardless of how small its claimed upside is. Thus a sufficiently conservative systemic risk bond makes Trojan under-declaration impossible at the debt gate.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Without a bond term, the initial debt depends only on the claimed upside. Hence one can take any structurally dangerous proposal and report an arbitrarily small positive claim, which drives the initialization below any fixed threshold while leaving writable scope unchanged. This proves the first statement.

With the downside-reserve initialization of Definition~\ref{def:cohort_escrow}, the issuance stock is $\eta_{t,t}=\mathcal B_t(u_t)+U_t^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_t^{\mathrm{haz}}$. If the bond lower-bounds hidden or governance reach and that reach exceeds the policy threshold, then the initialized debt already exceeds the threshold before any later retirement, routing, or calibration step can help; a fortiori the same holds once repair and hazard reserves are added. Therefore the proposal is rejected at issuance.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Bond-only initialization remains under-reserved against topological obfuscation]\label{thm:causal_bond}
Suppose a governance policy uses only static graph-size terms such as $|\mathcal W_t(u_t)|$ and $|\operatorname{Dep}_t(\mathcal W_t(u_t))|$ when initializing proposal-local debt. Then for any fixed debt threshold $\bar\delta_r>0$ there exist representation-preserving refactorings that compress a high-impact rewrite into a single apparent module or dispatcher while leaving its output-side intervention reach essentially unchanged. In that sense, purely topological bonds are spoofable under topological obfuscation and remain insufficient even if one later appends repair or hazard reserves that do not track intervention reach.

Suppose instead that the policy uses Definition~\ref{def:blast_radius} with a replayable causal lower envelope $\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)$ satisfying
\[
\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)\ge \mathcal H_t(u_t)
\]
for some public lower bound $\mathcal H_t(u_t)$ on hidden-state or governance-surface reach, and that $\lambda_C>0$. Then any proposal with
\[
\mathcal H_t(u_t)>\bar\delta_r(C_t)/\lambda_C
\]
necessarily has
\[
\eta_{t,t}\ge \mathcal B_t(u_t)\ge \lambda_C\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)>\bar\delta_r(C_t)
\]
and is rejected at issuance, regardless of how aggressively its internal topology has been compressed or obfuscated.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Static graph-size counts depend on representation. A proposer can fuse many downstream effects into one learned block, one dynamic dispatch string, or one monolithic weight tensor, thereby making the writable set and visible dependency closure small while preserving large intervention reach. Hence graph-size-only bonds can be spoofed.

By contrast, the second statement depends only on the public lower envelope $\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)$ and the downside-reserve initialization rule $\eta_{t,t}=\mathcal B_t(u_t)+U_t^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_t^{\mathrm{haz}}$. If $\mathcal B_t(u_t)\ge \lambda_C\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)\ge \lambda_C\mathcal H_t(u_t)$ and the right-hand side exceeds the debt threshold, then the proposal fails immediately even before the extra repair and hazard reserves are counted. The argument is representation-agnostic because it uses intervention reach rather than topology count.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Strict-conservation repair-throughput law]\label{thm:strict_conservation}
Consider the strict-conservation regime $\alpha_r=1$. Suppose there exist nonnegative adapted processes $L_t$, $a_t^{\mathrm{sec}}$, and $U_t$ such that aggregate debt obeys the upper recursion
\[
r_{t+1}\le r_t + L_t + a_t^{\mathrm{sec}} - U_t,
\]
where $L_t$ is new \emph{primary} liability plus backlog charge, $a_t^{\mathrm{sec}}$ is repair-induced secondary liability, and $U_t$ is gross effective retirement. Suppose further that
\[
\E[L_t\mid \mathcal F_t]\le \bar\lambda_L + \lambda_q \bar q,
\qquad
\E[U_t\mid \mathcal F_t]\ge \mu^{\mathrm{rep}},
\]
and that repair-induced secondary liabilities satisfy
\[
\E[a_t^{\mathrm{sec}}\mid \mathcal F_t] \le \eps_{\mathrm{rep}}\,\E[U_t\mid \mathcal F_t]
\qquad\text{with }\eps_{\mathrm{rep}}\in[0,1).
\]
Then the conditional drift of strict-conservation debt satisfies
\[
\E[r_{t+1}-r_t\mid\mathcal F_t]
\le
\bar\lambda_L + \lambda_q \bar q - (1-\eps_{\mathrm{rep}})\mu^{\mathrm{rep}}.
\]
Consequently, if
\[
\bar\lambda_L + \lambda_q \bar q < (1-\eps_{\mathrm{rep}})\mu^{\mathrm{rep}},
\]
strict-conservation debt has negative conditional drift and cannot grow linearly on average. Conversely, if there exists $\varepsilon_{+}>0$ such that
\[
r_{t+1}\ge r_t + L_t + a_t^{\mathrm{sec}} - U_t,
\qquad
\E[L_t+a_t^{\mathrm{sec}}-U_t\mid\mathcal F_t]\ge \varepsilon_{+}
\]
on every step, then $\E[r_t]$ grows at least linearly in $t$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Taking conditional expectation in the displayed upper recursion gives
\[
\E[r_{t+1}-r_t\mid\mathcal F_t]
\le
\E[L_t\mid\mathcal F_t]+\E[a_t^{\mathrm{sec}}\mid\mathcal F_t]-\E[U_t\mid\mathcal F_t].
\]
By hypothesis,
\[
\E[L_t\mid\mathcal F_t]\le \bar\lambda_L+\lambda_q\bar q,
\qquad
\E[a_t^{\mathrm{sec}}\mid\mathcal F_t]\le \eps_{\mathrm{rep}}\E[U_t\mid\mathcal F_t],
\]
so
\[
\E[r_{t+1}-r_t\mid\mathcal F_t]
\le
\bar\lambda_L+\lambda_q\bar q-(1-\eps_{\mathrm{rep}})\E[U_t\mid\mathcal F_t]
\le
\bar\lambda_L+\lambda_q\bar q-(1-\eps_{\mathrm{rep}})\mu^{\mathrm{rep}}.
\]
This proves the upper drift bound. Summing it over time yields the nonpositive-average-growth claim when the right-hand side is strictly negative. The final linear-growth statement follows by summing the displayed lower drift inequality over time.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Verification bottleneck and queue sharpness}
\begin{theorem}[Verification queue phase diagram]\label{thm:queue_phase}
Consider the fluid queue law
\[
q_{t+1}=\bigl[q_t+\lambda-\mu\bigr]_+
\]
with constant proposal rate $\lambda\ge0$ and verification service $\mu\ge0$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item If $\lambda<\mu$, then $q_t$ reaches $0$ in finite time and remains there.
  \item If $\lambda=\mu$, then $q_t\equiv q_0$.
  \item If $\lambda>\mu$, then $q_t=q_0+t(\lambda-\mu)$ for all sufficiently large $t$ and diverges linearly.
\end{enumerate}
If latent error debt satisfies
\[
r_{t+1}\ge \alpha_r r_t + \lambda_q q_t,
\qquad \alpha_r\in[0,1],\ \lambda_q>0,
\]
then the overloaded regime $\lambda>\mu$ prevents uniform control of error debt.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The queue recursion is deterministic. If $\lambda<\mu$, then each step decreases the bracket by $\mu-\lambda$ until it hits zero, after which it stays zero. If $\lambda=\mu$, then the update is constant. If $\lambda>\mu$, then after the queue becomes positive it increments by the constant difference $\lambda-\mu$ at every step. The lower recursion for $r_t$ then forces unbounded growth when $q_t$ grows linearly and $\lambda_q>0$.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Capability-dependent verification complexity]\label{def:red_queen}
Let $\kappa$ be any productive capability functional on the productive state coordinates and define the accepted productive increment by
\[
\Delta \kappa_s\Defeq \bigl[\kappa(x_{s+1})-\kappa(x_s)\bigr]_+.
\]
Then
\[
K_t^{\mathrm{cap}}\Defeq \sum_{s=0}^{t-1}\Delta \kappa_s
\]
be cumulative accepted \emph{productive} capability expansion. A \emph{verification complexity law} is a predictable nondecreasing map $c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})\ge 1$ measuring the replay-and-check cost of current proposals at productive capability level $K_t^{\mathrm{cap}}$. Under physical verification budget $P_t>0$, the effective service rate is
\[
\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}\Defeq \frac{P_t}{c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})}.
\]
This separates algorithmic or semantic complexity from raw physical throughput while refusing to count pure representational churn as growth.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Governance-computation complexity and proof-carrying governance]\label{def:pcg}
Let $c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t)$ denote the replay cost of recomputing the governance predicates required by the admission rule for proposal $u_t$, including any semantic-volume, routing-sensitivity, replay-floor, or integrity-envelope computations demanded by policy. A \emph{proof-carrying governance regime} is policy-admissible if each proposal carries a replay-checkable certificate $\pi_t$ attesting the claimed governance bounds together with a public checker satisfying
\[
\widetilde c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t)\le \alpha_{\mathrm{gov}}\,c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t)+b_{\mathrm{gov}}
\]
for public constants $\alpha_{\mathrm{gov}}\in[0,1]$ and $b_{\mathrm{gov}}\ge 0$. The special case $(\alpha_{\mathrm{gov}},b_{\mathrm{gov}})=(1,0)$ recovers the weaker ``no worse than full recomputation'' requirement. If full recomputation is performed only on a predictable audit fraction $\sigma_t^{\mathrm{gov}}\in[0,1]$, the effective per-proposal governance workload is
\[
\widehat c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t)\Defeq \widetilde c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t)+\sigma_t^{\mathrm{gov}}c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t).
\]
This definition does not assume magical zero-cost proofs; it separates producer-paid certificate generation from the public cost of checking certificates and selectively recomputing them.
\end{definition}


\begin{definition}[Constitutional logic class and decidability-bounded proof escrow]\label{def:constitutional_logic}
A proof-carrying governance regime is \emph{constitutionally bounded} if there exists a public family of certificate languages and checkers
\[
\mathfrak L^{\mathrm{const}}=\{(\mathcal L_\ell,V_\ell,T_\ell,M_\ell):\ell\in\mathcal I\}
\]
with the following properties.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item Every checker $V_\ell$ is \emph{total}: it halts on every input certificate and proposal transcript.
  \item For every certificate $\pi$, verification time and working memory satisfy the public static envelopes
  \[
  \mathrm{time}(V_\ell(\pi))\le T_\ell(|\pi|),
  \qquad
  \mathrm{mem}(V_\ell(\pi))\le M_\ell(|\pi|).
  \]
  \item Fast-admission proposals must declare a language tag $\ell_t\in\mathcal I$ and provide a certificate $\pi_t\in\mathcal L_{\ell_t}$; certificates outside $\mathfrak L^{\mathrm{const}}$ are not fast-certifiable by type inside the current constitutional lane and must therefore be routed to a non-fast action such as richer proof escalation or sandboxing before semantic deployment is considered.
\end{enumerate}
The resulting public verification cost is
\[
\widetilde c_{t,\mathrm{const}}^{\mathrm{gov}}\Defeq T_{\ell_t}(|\pi_t|),
\]
and the corresponding effective governance workload is
\[
\widehat c_{t,\mathrm{const}}^{\mathrm{gov}}
\Defeq
\widetilde c_{t,\mathrm{const}}^{\mathrm{gov}}+\sigma_t^{\mathrm{gov}}c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Extensional adequacy on a designated certificate class]\label{def:adequacy}
Let $\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{valid}}$ be a designated replayable recursively enumerable class of governance certificates paired with proposal transcripts. A checker is \emph{extensionally adequate on $\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{valid}}$} if every pair $(\pi,u)\in \mathfrak C^{\mathrm{valid}}$ that encodes a governance proof valid relative to the designated proof system and transcript semantics is accepted whenever the checker halts. This is weaker than completeness on all syntactic certificates but strong enough to forbid the trivial ``reject everything'' escape on the designated class used in the halting reduction. No privileged semantic judge is invoked here: validity is only the proof-theoretic relation fixed by the designated certificate class.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Decidability-bounded proof escrow and the G\"odelian ceiling]\label{thm:godelian_ceiling}
Suppose governance proofs are accepted from an unrestricted certificate language whose checker can simulate a universal computation model. Suppose moreover that there exists a computable embedding from Turing-machine/input pairs $(M,w)$ into a designated replayable recursively enumerable class $\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{valid}}$ of certificate-proposal pairs such that the embedded pair is valid in that designated proof-theoretic sense if and only if $M$ halts on $w$. If the checker is required to be both sound and extensionally adequate in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:adequacy} on that designated class, then for every public governance budget $B<\infty$, there exists a finite certificate-proposal pair $(\pi,u)$ such that any such checker either fails to halt or consumes more than $B$ time or memory while attempting to validate the claimed governance bounds. Consequently no uniform public upper envelope on $\widetilde c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$ exists, and proof-level denial-of-service cannot be excluded.

By contrast, under Definition~\ref{def:constitutional_logic}, every admissible certificate is checked by a total verifier with public cost bound $\widetilde c_{t,\mathrm{const}}^{\mathrm{gov}}\le T_{\ell_t}(|\pi_t|)$. Hence every Red-Queen or queue-slack statement in which governance workload appears remains valid after replacing $\widehat c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t)$ by $\widehat c_{t,\mathrm{const}}^{\mathrm{gov}}$. Any proposal whose safety argument cannot be expressed inside $\mathfrak L^{\mathrm{const}}$ lies beyond the \emph{G\"odelian ceiling} of the current fast-admission regime. Such a proposal cannot be certified \emph{inside that fast regime}; it must therefore be deferred to a richer proof lane, sandboxed under tighter scope, or held non-admissible until a replayable proof interface capable of expressing it is provided. This is a regime-relative routing statement, not a claim that the proposal is anti-growth or permanently undeployable.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For the first claim, fix a universal Turing machine $M$ and input $w$. By the embedding hypothesis, there exists a computable map $(M,w)\mapsto (\pi_{M,w},u_{M,w})\in \mathfrak C^{\mathrm{valid}}$ such that $(\pi_{M,w},u_{M,w})$ encodes the statement that the embedded computation halts and the claimed governance bound is valid if and only if $M$ halts on $w$. Soundness forbids acceptance when the encoded halting assertion is false, while extensional adequacy on $\mathfrak C^{\mathrm{valid}}$ forces acceptance when the encoded assertion is true whenever the checker halts. If a checker were also uniformly budget-bounded on the unrestricted language, we could decide whether $M$ halts on $w$ by running the checker on $(\pi_{M,w},u_{M,w})$ and observing acceptance versus rejection within the public bound, contradicting undecidability of the halting problem. Therefore some finite certificates force nontermination or arbitrarily large verification cost.

The second claim is immediate from Definition~\ref{def:constitutional_logic}: totality gives termination, while the static envelopes $T_\ell$ and $M_\ell$ give public worst-case bounds. Substituting $\widehat c_{t,\mathrm{const}}^{\mathrm{gov}}$ for $\widehat c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t)$ in any workload-slack condition preserves the proofs because those arguments use governance workload only through an upper bound. The final sentence is a policy consequence, not a semantic impossibility claim: once the admissible proof languages are fixed, anything requiring a richer proof interface is outside the regime by construction.
\end{proof}


\begin{remark}[No-meta clarification for proof languages]
The constitutional proof layer is not an external semantic oracle. It is a public restriction on what kinds of safety arguments the system is willing to spend bounded governance resources verifying on the fast admission path. The price of avoiding proof-level denial-of-service is not blanket anti-growth rejection; it is explicit lane separation. Some true-but-inexpressible proposals cannot be fast-admitted, but they may still be deferred to richer proof interfaces, narrower deployment scopes, or sandboxed challenge lanes if policy exposes those routes replayably.
\end{remark}
\begin{definition}[Thermodynamic proof escrow and physical preemption]\label{def:thermo_escrow}
For each policy-declared proof checker $V$ --- either on the fast constitutional lane or on a richer escalated proof lane --- and certificate $\pi$, let
\[
\tau_t^{\mathrm{wall}}(V_\ell,\pi),
\qquad
\mathcal E_t(V_\ell,\pi)
\]
denote hardware-metered wall-clock time and energy consumed by the verification attempt on the physically escrowed verifier. A \emph{thermodynamic proof escrow} consists of public envelopes $T_{V}^{\mathrm{wall}}(|\pi|)$ and $\mathcal E_V^{\max}(|\pi|)$ together with a hardware preemption rule that aborts verification whenever either
\[
\tau_t^{\mathrm{wall}}(V,\pi) > T_{V}^{\mathrm{wall}}(|\pi|)
\quad\text{or}\quad
\mathcal E_t(V,\pi) > \mathcal E_V^{\max}(|\pi|).
\]
Aborted certificates are treated as verification failures rather than retried indefinitely. The checker family and the corresponding physical envelopes are part of the replayable proof-interface declaration for the lane in which $V$ is used.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Microarchitectural Red-Queen law and thermodynamic proof escrow]\label{thm:thermo_escrow}
Suppose governance verification is protected only by algorithmic bounds such as $T_\ell(|\pi|)$ and $M_\ell(|\pi|)$. Then, on sufficiently complex hardware, there need not exist a public architecture-independent constant converting those abstract bounds into uniform wall-clock or energy bounds; microarchitectural effects can inflate physical verification cost enough to consume the physically reserved governance budget even when the logical checker remains inside its static step and memory envelopes. Therefore abstract constitutional bounds alone do not close the governance-side Red-Queen loophole.

If, in addition, every policy-declared checker in the active proof lane is executed under a thermodynamic proof escrow in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:thermo_escrow}, then each admissible verification attempt consumes at most the physically budgeted amount
\[
\tau_t^{\mathrm{wall}}(V_t,\pi_t) \le T_{V_t}^{\mathrm{wall}}(|\pi_t|)
\quad\text{and}\quad
\mathcal E_t(V_t,\pi_t) \le \mathcal E_{V_t}^{\max}(|\pi_t|)
\]
by construction. Consequently every queue-slack or Red-Queen statement that uses governance workload remains valid after replacing abstract governance cost by these hardware-preempted physical envelopes. Microarchitectural stalling is then converted from an unbounded slowdown attack into an immediate proof-verification failure.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The first claim is a consequence of the gap between abstract instruction counts and physical execution cost on hardware with caches, predictors, contention, throttling, and other stateful effects: two runs with the same high-level verification logic can consume sharply different wall-clock time or energy. Hence a static logical bound does not by itself imply a static physical budget bound.

Under thermodynamic proof escrow, however, the verifier is forcibly preempted once either the wall-clock or energy envelope is exceeded. Therefore each attempt either accepts or rejects within a public physical budget. Replacing abstract governance cost by this hardware-preempted envelope preserves all backlog and Red-Queen arguments, because those arguments require only an upper bound on per-proposal physical workload. Any certificate that attempts to exploit microarchitectural worst cases is simply truncated and rejected.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Clarification on physical preemption]
This theorem does not claim that wall-clock or energy are semantically meaningful proofs of safety. It claims only that physical verification budget must be bounded in the same units that the escrow actually protects. Logical decidability without thermodynamic preemption leaves a cyber-physical gap large enough to drive a denial-of-service attack through.
\end{remark}


\begin{definition}[Physical resource-escrow invariant]\label{def:resource_escrow}
Let $P_t^{\mathrm{tot}}>0$ be total physical compute available to the recursive loop at time $t$, and let $P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}\in(0,P_t^{\mathrm{tot}}]$ be the physically reserved share dedicated to verification, shadow reevaluation, replay, and governance checks. Define
\[
\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}\Defeq \frac{P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}}{P_t^{\mathrm{tot}}}.
\]
A system satisfies the \emph{resource-escrow invariant} if there exists $\rho_{\min}>0$ such that $\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}\ge \rho_{\min}$ for all $t$, and if the allocator controlling $P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}$ lies outside the writable scope of admissible proposals or is protected by a replay-checkable hardware or allocator attestation mechanism.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Verifiable transloading chain and Theseus limit]\label{def:transloading}
A \emph{transloading step} $M_{t\to t+1}$ replaces the current physically escrowed allocator or attesting substrate by a new one. The step is \emph{escrow-preserving} if it produces a public migration transcript containing: (i) a hardware-backed attestation from the outgoing root of trust to the incoming one, (ii) a measurement that the new allocator enforces the same lower reservation floor $\rho_{\min}$ and checker policy, and (iii) zero software intervention in the map from attested measurements to reserved verification share. The first time at which no such attestable chain exists is the \emph{Theseus limit} of the escrow lineage.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Verifiable transloading of physical escrow and the Theseus limit]\label{thm:theseus_limit}
If there exists a transloading step that is not escrow-preserving in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:transloading}, then there is a migration-compatible run with identical software-visible proposal logs in which the effective reservation ratio drops below $\rho_{\min}$ after finitely many hardware replacements. Thus software-side admission predicates alone cannot certify long-horizon preservation of the resource-escrow invariant across hardware refresh.

Conversely, if every transloading step in a hardware lineage is escrow-preserving, then the resource-escrow invariant propagates inductively across the entire lineage: whenever $\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}\ge \rho_{\min}$ before migration, the post-migration allocator also satisfies $\rho_{t+1}^{\mathrm{verif}}\ge \rho_{\min}$. Therefore the only way physical escrow can silently decay under repeated hardware replacement is by crossing the Theseus limit, i.e., by executing a migration for which no hardware-attested preservation chain exists.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For the first claim, suppose the migration is mediated by writable software or by an unattested bootstrap path. Then the new allocator state can be initialized with a smaller reserved share while leaving software-visible proposal logs unchanged; the discrepancy is hidden precisely because the software layer no longer controls or reliably measures the allocator transition. This constructs a run in which the software history is observationally compatible with the nominal one while the physical reservation ratio silently decays.

For the converse, proceed by induction over migration events. The base case is the pre-migration escrow invariant. At an escrow-preserving migration, the outgoing hardware-backed attestation and the incoming measurement certify that the new allocator implements the same lower floor and that software has no write path into the allocation rule during handoff. Hence the reservation floor is preserved at the next step. Repeating the argument over the lineage preserves the invariant until the first migration lacking such an attested chain, which is exactly the Theseus limit.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[No-meta clarification for physical escrow]
The theorem does not assume a benevolent external administrator who watches every migration. It assumes only that the migration transcript itself is anchored in a hardware-backed attestation chain that lies outside writable software scope. The trust base is therefore physical and public, not semantic and privileged.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Red-Queen verification capacity law]\label{thm:red_queen}
Consider the predictable-load queue
\[
q_{t+1}=\bigl[q_t+\Lambda_t-\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}\bigr]_+,
\qquad
\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}=\frac{P_t}{c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})}
\]
with predictable load $\Lambda_t\ge 0$ and capability-dependent verification complexity as in Definition~\ref{def:red_queen}.
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item If there exists $\eps_{\mathrm{RQ}}>0$ such that
  \[
  \Lambda_t\le \frac{P_t}{c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})}-\eps_{\mathrm{RQ}}
  \qquad\text{for all }t,
  \]
  and the centered one-step workload $\Lambda_t-\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}$ has uniformly bounded conditional second moment, then the time-average backlog is uniformly bounded.
  \item If there exists $\eps_{\mathrm{RQ}}>0$ such that whenever $q_t>0$,
  \[
  \Lambda_t\ge \frac{P_t}{c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})}+\eps_{\mathrm{RQ}},
  \]
  then on every active step
  \[
  \E[q_{t+1}-q_t\mid\mathcal F_t]\ge \eps_{\mathrm{RQ}},
  \]
  so persistent activity forces at least linear expected backlog growth on the active subsequence.
\end{enumerate}
In particular, open-ended capability expansion is verification-stable only if physical verification budget scales at least as fast as capability-induced verification complexity. If $c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})$ eventually dominates $P_t/\Lambda_t$, the queue necessarily enters overload and the recursive loop undergoes verification-backlog collapse.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For part (i), use the quadratic Lyapunov function $L(q)=q^2$. Since $[x]_+^2\le x^2$,
\[
q_{t+1}^2-q_t^2
\le
2q_t(\Lambda_t-\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}})+(\Lambda_t-\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}})^2.
\]
Taking conditional expectation and using the slack assumption gives
\[
\E[q_{t+1}^2-q_t^2\mid\mathcal F_t]
\le
-2\eps_{\mathrm{RQ}}q_t + C_{\mathrm{RQ}},
\]
where $C_{\mathrm{RQ}}$ is the uniform conditional second-moment bound on $\Lambda_t-\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}$. Standard Foster--Lyapunov summation then yields a uniform bound on time-average backlog. For part (ii), whenever $q_t>0$ we have $q_{t+1}-q_t=\Lambda_t-\mu_t^{\mathrm{ver}}$, hence the displayed lower drift bound follows immediately. Summing over an active subsequence yields at least linear expected backlog growth. The final statement is the contrapositive: if verification complexity outruns the physical budget relative to incoming load, then effective service collapses relative to predictable arrivals.
\end{proof}


\begin{corollary}[Open-ended viability requires both spillover control and Red-Queen slack]\label{cor:red_queen_open}
The governance ceilings of Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open} can coexist with unbounded capability growth only if two distinct conditions hold simultaneously: capability-to-governance spillovers must remain window-summable, and capability-dependent verification complexity must not erase service slack in the sense of Theorem~\ref{thm:red_queen}. Open-ended capability by itself is therefore compatible with stable governance only when \emph{decoupling} and \emph{verification scaling} are both satisfied.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open} controls the projected governance coordinates only through the spillover envelope from productive capability into those coordinates. Theorem~\ref{thm:red_queen} separately controls whether verification itself remains capable of servicing the resulting governance workload. If either condition fails, then either the tracked governance coordinates cease to admit a window-summable forcing envelope or the verification queue enters overload. Both are therefore necessary for long-run coexistence of open-ended productive growth with bounded projected governance coordinates.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Governance capital profile, proposal-burden profiles, fixed-threshold dominance, and admissible productive frontier]\label{def:frontier}
Fix a decision epoch $t$, a replayable proposal menu $\mathcal U_t$, a productive capability functional $\kappa$, and a published policy manifest $\Pi_t$ that fixes the acceptance thresholds and required clauses for Interfaces 0, A, B, and C. For a governance regime $\mathsf R$ at epoch $t$, define the protected-lane service slacks
\[
\begin{aligned}
S_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(\mathsf R)&\Defeq \mu_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(\mathsf R)-\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(\mathsf R),\\
S_t^{\mathrm{prom}}(\mathsf R)&\Defeq \mu_t^{\mathrm{prom}}(\mathsf R)-\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{prom}}(\mathsf R),\\
S_t^{\mathrm{proof}}(\mathsf R)&\Defeq \mu_t^{\mathrm{proof}}(\mathsf R)-\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{proof}}(\mathsf R).
\end{aligned}
\]
where the arrival and service quantities are the replayably published cohort-equivalent loads and protected service capacities for the challenge, promotion, and richer-proof lanes. Let $r_t^{\mathrm{pub}}(\mathsf R)$ denote the regime's published regime-level debt-burden envelope inherited from Definition~\ref{def:operational_certificates}. For regime-level comparison, fix a replayably declared \emph{sanitized comparison menu} $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}\subseteq \mathcal U_t$, common to all compared regimes, obtained by applying the same public syntax, scope, and null-certificate prefilters before governance-capital comparison. This removes trivially malformed or out-of-scope proposals from the regime comparison while preserving a common productive candidate set. The per-artifact and per-candidate coordinates are then scalarized conservatively as follows:
\[
G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}(\mathsf R)\Defeq \inf_{a\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{aud}}(\mathsf R)} G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}(a),
\qquad
\inf\varnothing\Defeq 0,
\]
\[
\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(\mathsf R)\Defeq \inf_{(a\rightsquigarrow a')\in\mathcal T_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(\mathsf R)} \underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(a\rightsquigarrow a'),
\qquad
\inf\varnothing\Defeq 0,
\]
where $\mathcal T_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(\mathsf R)$ is the replayably declared set of live refreezing or transport certificates currently supporting retained audit artifacts under regime $\mathsf R$. The fail-closed convention $\inf\varnothing=0$ reflects the fact that a regime with no auditable artifacts or no live transport support provides no positive replay or semantic-floor evidence. Likewise let
\[
A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}(\mathsf R)\Defeq \sup_{u\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}} A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}(u;\mathsf R),
\qquad
\sup\varnothing\Defeq 0,
\]
where $A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}(u;\mathsf R)$ is the replayably published manifest-preserving attack-reach envelope that regime $\mathsf R$ assigns to proposal $u$ under the common sanitized menu. The remaining coordinates $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}(\mathsf R)$, $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}(\mathsf R)$, $\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}(\mathsf R)$, and $\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}(\mathsf R)$ are the corresponding current state values induced by regime $\mathsf R$. Now let
\[
\begin{aligned}
K_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(\mathsf R)\Defeq\bigl(
&S_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(\mathsf R),
S_t^{\mathrm{prom}}(\mathsf R),
S_t^{\mathrm{proof}}(\mathsf R),
G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}(\mathsf R),\\
&R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}(\mathsf R),
\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}(\mathsf R),
\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}(\mathsf R),
\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}(\mathsf R),
\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}(\mathsf R);\\
&A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}(\mathsf R),
 r_t^{\mathrm{pub}}(\mathsf R)
\bigr)
\end{aligned}
\]
denote the tuple of \emph{regime-level} public governance-capital coordinates entering admissibility after the fixed thresholds of $\Pi_t$ have been substituted: the first block consists of lower-margin, routing, replay, contradiction, semantic, or service coordinates whose increase helps admission, and the second block consists of attack or debt-burden coordinates whose decrease helps admission. Proposal-specific workload and intervention coordinates are kept separate. For each proposal $u\in\mathcal U_t$, define the proposal-burden profile
\[
B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u;\mathsf R)\Defeq \bigl(\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u),\,\widehat c_{t,\mathsf R}^{\mathrm{gov}}(u),\,\operatorname{diam}^{\mathrm{cmp}}_{t,H}(u)\bigr),
\]
with the convention that $\widehat c_{t,\mathsf R}^{\mathrm{gov}}(u)$ denotes the effective governance workload of proposal $u$ under the replayable certificate bundle actually published by regime $\mathsf R$. Fixed-threshold dominance compares these coordinates proposalwise under the common sanitized comparison menu and common replayable proposal certificates. Let
\[
\begin{aligned}
\mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{lane}}(\mathsf R)\Defeq
\Bigl\{u\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}:
&\text{$u$ is admitted at epoch $t$ to some replayable nondeployment action }\\
&\text{such as challenge routing, richer-proof escalation, or sandboxing under }\\
&\text{the fixed manifest $\Pi_t$, regime $\mathsf R$, and state $C_t$}\Bigr\},
\end{aligned}
\]
and let
\[
\begin{aligned}
\mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R)\Defeq
\Bigl\{u\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}:
&\text{$u$ is an $(H,\beta)$-full admissible improvement under the fixed manifest $\Pi_t$,}\\
&\text{regime $\mathsf R$, and state $C_t$, and is therefore immediately deployable}\\
&\text{into the productive target lane at epoch $t$}\Bigr\}.
\end{aligned}
\]
Delayed cohorts tracked in $\mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{lane}}(\mathsf R)\setminus \mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R)$ do not yet enter the productive frontier; they are counted only after the delayed certificates and review actions needed for deployment have been completed. The corresponding \emph{admissible productive frontier} is
\[
\Phi_t(\mathsf R)\Defeq \sup_{u\in\mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R)} \Delta\kappa_t(u),
\qquad
\sup\varnothing\Defeq 0.
\]
We say that regime $\mathsf R^+$ \emph{fixed-threshold dominates} regime $\mathsf R^-$ in governance capital at epoch $t$ if they share the same public state $C_t$, the same manifest $\Pi_t$ and acceptance thresholds, the same sanitized comparison menu $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$, horizon $(H,\beta)$, productive capability functional $\kappa$, and replayable proposal certificates, and if every helpful coordinate of $K_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$ is weakly larger in $\mathsf R^+$ while every burden coordinate is weakly smaller, with at least one strict inequality, and in addition every proposal-specific burden profile $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u;\mathsf R^+)$ is weakly no worse than $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u;\mathsf R^-)$ in the same proposalwise order for every $u\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$. In particular, fixed-threshold dominance does \emph{not} allow threshold relaxation, weakening of required clauses, or redefinition of admissibility; it records only stronger public evidence that the same published policy can be safely serviced.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Fixed-threshold admissibility operator]\label{def:admissibility_operator}
For a regime $\mathsf R$ at epoch $t$ and a replayable proposal set $S\subseteq \mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$, define the fixed-threshold admissibility operator
\[
T_{t,\mathsf R}(S)\Defeq \{u\in S: u\text{ satisfies Interfaces 0, A, B, and C under regime }\mathsf R\}
\]
under the common manifest, thresholds, and replayable certificate language.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Interface-indexed admissibility operators]\label{def:interface_operators}
For $\iota\in\{0,A,B,C\}$, regime $\mathsf R$ at epoch $t$, and replayable proposal set $S\subseteq\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$, define
\[
T_{t,\mathsf R}^{\iota}(S)\Defeq \{u\in S: u\text{ satisfies Interface }\iota\text{ under regime }\mathsf R\}.
\]
Accordingly,
\[
T_{t,\mathsf R}(S)=\bigcap_{\iota\in\{0,A,B,C\}} T_{t,\mathsf R}^{\iota}(S).
\]
This definition fixes the typing used later in the interface-wise monotonicity propositions: $T_{t,\mathsf R}$ is the full deployability operator, while $T_{t,\mathsf R}^{\iota}$ is the corresponding single-interface gate.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Feasible monotonicity order under fixed thresholds]\label{def:feasible_order}
Fix epoch $t$, common manifest $\Pi_t$, fixed thresholds, and sanitized comparison menu $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$. A replayably published \emph{feasible monotonicity order} is a partial order $\preceq^{\mathrm{feas}}_{t,\Pi}$ on gate-eligible certificate summaries generated from regime-level helpful coordinates, regime-level burden coordinates, and proposal-specific burden profiles. The published order is \emph{certificate-monotone} if every Interface-A or Interface-C admission clause used at the fast gate can be written in one of the primitive forms
\[
L_j(u;\mathsf R)\ge \theta_j,
\qquad
U_j(u;\mathsf R)\le \bar\theta_j,
\]
with fixed thresholds $(\theta_j,\bar\theta_j)$ shared across regimes, where each lower certificate $L_j$ is replayably nondecreasing in the helpful coordinates and nonincreasing in the burden coordinates under $\preceq^{\mathrm{feas}}_{t,\Pi}$, each upper certificate $U_j$ is replayably nonincreasing in the helpful coordinates and nondecreasing in the burden coordinates, and proposal-specific burden enters only through the published profile $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u;\mathsf R)$. Tier-1 and Tier-2 proxy clauses must either be regime-invariant or replayably conservative for the same latent target under both regimes. This definition does \emph{not} by itself assert certificate preservation; it specifies the primitive monotone form from which preservation is derived in the next propositions.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Interface-0 monotonicity under fixed thresholds]\label{prop:mono_base}
Under the hypotheses of Definition~\ref{def:frontier}, fixed-threshold governance-capital dominance of $\mathsf R^+$ over $\mathsf R^-$ preserves Interface-0 certificates on the common sanitized comparison menu. Equivalently,
\[
T^{0}_{t,\mathsf R^-}(S)\subseteq T^{0}_{t,\mathsf R^+}(S)
\qquad\text{for every replayable }S\subseteq\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Interface 0 uses the same manifest, the same typed-noise comparator family, the same gate discipline, and the same acceptance thresholds under both regimes. Its predicates depend only on the common proposal certificates and on fixed-threshold clauses that are unchanged when moving from $\mathsf R^-$ to $\mathsf R^+$. Hence any proposal that satisfies Interface 0 under $\mathsf R^-$ also satisfies it under $\mathsf R^+$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Interface-A monotonicity under fixed thresholds]\label{prop:mono_gain}
Under the hypotheses of Definition~\ref{def:frontier}, Definition~\ref{def:feasible_order}, and the gate discipline of Definition~\ref{def:proxy_tiers}, fixed-threshold governance-capital dominance of $\mathsf R^+$ over $\mathsf R^-$ preserves Interface-A certificates on the common sanitized comparison menu:
\[
T^{A}_{t,\mathsf R^-}(S)\subseteq T^{A}_{t,\mathsf R^+}(S)
\qquad\text{for every replayable }S\subseteq\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Interface A is certified-stable-gain admissibility. Under the common manifest, comparator witness family, and acceptance thresholds, the regime-sensitive terms enter only through replayable lower and upper certificates for replay breadth, challenge calibration, service slack, transport calibration, and proposal-specific burden. By Definition~\ref{def:feasible_order}, each gate-eligible lower clause is monotone nondecreasing in the helpful coordinates and nonincreasing in the burdens, each upper clause has the opposite monotonicity, and Tier-1/Tier-2 proxies remain conservative for the same latent target under both regimes. Fixed-threshold dominance therefore preserves every primitive Interface-A inequality, so any proposal admitted by Interface A under $\mathsf R^-$ remains admitted under $\mathsf R^+$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Interface-B monotonicity under fixed thresholds]\label{prop:mono_debt}
Under the hypotheses of Definition~\ref{def:frontier}, fixed-threshold governance-capital dominance of $\mathsf R^+$ over $\mathsf R^-$ preserves Interface-B debt certificates on the common sanitized comparison menu:
\[
T^{B}_{t,\mathsf R^-}(S)\subseteq T^{B}_{t,\mathsf R^+}(S)
\qquad\text{for every replayable }S\subseteq\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Interface B depends on the same published debt thresholds and on replayable downside-reserve certificates for blast radius, repair reserve, hazard reserve, retirement credits, and secondary liabilities. Fixed-threshold dominance leaves the thresholds unchanged and does not worsen any proposal-specific burden profile; in particular, the effective governance workload and secondary-liability terms are weakly no worse under $\mathsf R^+$ than under $\mathsf R^-$. Thus every proposal whose debt certificate is accepted under $\mathsf R^-$ remains accepted under $\mathsf R^+$.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Interface-C monotonicity under fixed thresholds]\label{prop:mono_gov}
Under the hypotheses of Definition~\ref{def:frontier}, Definition~\ref{def:feasible_order}, and the gate discipline of Definition~\ref{def:proxy_tiers}, fixed-threshold governance-capital dominance of $\mathsf R^+$ over $\mathsf R^-$ preserves Interface-C governance-safety certificates on the common sanitized comparison menu:
\[
T^{C}_{t,\mathsf R^-}(S)\subseteq T^{C}_{t,\mathsf R^+}(S)
\qquad\text{for every replayable }S\subseteq\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Interface C is governed by the same fixed manifest and thresholds, but with regime-level public governance coordinates and proposal-specific burden certificates. Fixed-threshold dominance improves every helpful regime-level coordinate, weakly tightens every burden coordinate, and does not worsen any proposal-specific burden profile on the common sanitized menu. By Definition~\ref{def:feasible_order}, the primitive lower and upper governance clauses are monotone in exactly those directions, while the gate discipline forbids a regime change from promoting a weaker Tier-3 heuristic into a fast-gate certificate. Hence the same admissible governance certificates remain valid under $\mathsf R^+$ whenever they were valid under $\mathsf R^-$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Fixed-threshold admissibility-operator monotonicity]\label{thm:operator_monotone}
Under the hypotheses of Definition~\ref{def:frontier}, Definition~\ref{def:feasible_order}, and the gate discipline of Definition~\ref{def:proxy_tiers}, fixed-threshold governance-capital dominance of $\mathsf R^+$ over $\mathsf R^-$ implies
\[
T_{t,\mathsf R^-}(S)\subseteq T_{t,\mathsf R^+}(S)
\qquad\text{for every replayable }S\subseteq \mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}.
\]
Thus the positive content of stronger governance capital is operator monotonicity under unchanged thresholds; frontier enlargement and the later realized-path comparison corollaries are repeated consequences of this monotone admissibility operator together with explicit witness selectors and delayed-deployment liveness.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix $u\in T_{t,\mathsf R^-}(S)$. By definition, $u$ satisfies Interfaces 0, A, B, and C under the same fixed thresholds and certificate language. Propositions~\ref{prop:mono_base}--\ref{prop:mono_gov} show clause by clause that each of those interface certificates remains valid under $\mathsf R^+$ whenever the feasible monotonicity order holds. Since $T_{t,\mathsf R}=T_{t,\mathsf R}^{0}\cap T_{t,\mathsf R}^{A}\cap T_{t,\mathsf R}^{B}\cap T_{t,\mathsf R}^{C}$, intersecting the four preserved clause-wise operators yields $u\in T_{t,\mathsf R^+}(S)$.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Fixed-threshold governance capital expands the admissible productive frontier]\label{thm:frontier_monotone}
Under the hypotheses of Theorem~\ref{thm:operator_monotone},
\[
\mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R^-)\subseteq \mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R^+)
\qquad\text{and hence}\qquad
\Phi_t(\mathsf R^+)\ge \Phi_t(\mathsf R^-).
\]
If there exists a proposal $u\in\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$ such that $u\in \mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R^+)\setminus \mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R^-)$ and $\Delta\kappa_t(u)>\Phi_t(\mathsf R^-)$, then the inequality is strict. In particular, governance capital is not merely a brake on growth claims; under fixed thresholds it is an observable enabler of a larger certifiable productive frontier.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Set $S=\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$ in Theorem~\ref{thm:operator_monotone}. The full-admissible set is exactly $\mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R)=T_{t,\mathsf R}(\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}})$ under the common manifest and fixed thresholds, so operator monotonicity yields the displayed set inclusion immediately. The frontier inequality then follows because the supremum of $\Delta\kappa_t$ over a superset cannot decrease. Strictness is immediate if a newly admitted proposal under $\mathsf R^+$ has direct productive increment exceeding the old supremum.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Feasible-order monotonicity is an explicit assumption]\label{rem:frontier_order}
Theorem~\ref{thm:frontier_monotone} is not a claim that every governance coordinate is independently helpful. In many deployments replay breadth, challenge coverage, proof depth, and routing pressure interact non-separably. The theorem therefore assumes a \emph{published feasible monotonicity order} on certificates: only improvements that preserve certificate validity in that declared order are compared. The positive frontier claim is attached to that explicit order, not to an unrestricted coordinatewise separability principle.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Frontier-improving governance edit]\label{def:gov_investment}
Fix a baseline null action $0_t$. An admissible proposal $u_t^{\mathrm{gov}}\in\mathcal U_t$ is a \emph{frontier-improving governance edit} at epoch $t$ if, on a shared continuation skeleton with the same exogenous randomness and a fixed \emph{comparison manifest} $\Pi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{cmp}}$ used to evaluate both successor worlds under identical next-epoch thresholds and admission clauses,
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item $\Delta\kappa_t(u_t^{\mathrm{gov}})=0$;
  \item the next productive state is not degraded, i.e. $\kappa(x_{t+1}(u_t^{\mathrm{gov}}))\ge \kappa(x_{t+1}(0_t))$;
  \item the induced next-epoch governance regime $\mathsf R_{t+1}^{\mathrm{gov}}$ fixed-threshold dominates the baseline regime $\mathsf R_{t+1}^{0}$ in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:frontier} when both are evaluated against the common comparison manifest $\Pi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{cmp}}$.
\end{enumerate}
Such an edit is therefore allowed to be non-productive today while still acting as a certified investment in future admissible growth capacity.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Frontier-expanding governance interventions]\label{thm:gov_investment}
Let $u_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$ be frontier-improving in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:gov_investment}. Then
\[
\Phi_{t+1}(\mathsf R_{t+1}^{\mathrm{gov}})\ge \Phi_{t+1}(\mathsf R_{t+1}^{0}),
\]
with strict inequality whenever the governance edit newly admits a productive proposal whose direct increment exceeds the baseline next-epoch frontier. Hence a governance edit may have zero immediate productive increment and still be growth-promoting by enlarging the next certifiably admissible productive frontier under unchanged thresholds.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Definition~\ref{def:gov_investment} gives fixed-threshold dominance of the next-epoch regime induced by the governance edit over the baseline null edit. Theorem~\ref{thm:frontier_monotone} therefore applies at epoch $t+1$ and yields the frontier inequality. The non-degradation of $\kappa(x_{t+1})$ ensures that the edit is not buying governance slack by sacrificing already-certified productive scope. Strictness follows exactly as in Theorem~\ref{thm:frontier_monotone} when a newly admissible proposal beats the old frontier.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Replay-path cumulative productive dominance under richer governance capital]\label{cor:frontier_cumulative}
Fix a replayable comparison path $\{(C_t^{\circ},\mathcal U_t^{\circ})\}_{t=0}^{T-1}$ and suppose two governance regimes $\mathsf R^-$ and $\mathsf R^+$ are evaluated counterfactually on that same path, with $\mathsf R^+$ fixed-threshold dominating $\mathsf R^-$ at every epoch. Let each regime choose a null edit if its admissible set is empty and otherwise choose any admissible proposal maximizing $\Delta\kappa_t$ on the common replay path. Then the accepted productive increment satisfies
\[
\Delta\kappa_t^{\ast}(\mathsf R^+)\ge \Delta\kappa_t^{\ast}(\mathsf R^-)\qquad\text{for every }t,
\]
and therefore
\[
\sum_{t=0}^{T-1}\Delta\kappa_t^{\ast}(\mathsf R^+)\ge\sum_{t=0}^{T-1}\Delta\kappa_t^{\ast}(\mathsf R^-).
\]
Thus, on a common replay scaffold, richer governance capital weakly dominates poorer governance capital in cumulative \emph{certifiably admissible} productive growth.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:frontier_monotone} gives epochwise set inclusion of admissible proposals under fixed thresholds. Maximizing the same direct productive increment over a superset yields an epochwise weakly larger optimum, and summing preserves the inequality.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Cap-maintaining protected-lane intake control]\label{def:cap_maintain}
Consider any protected governance lane $\ell\in\{\mathrm{chal},\mathrm{prom},\mathrm{proof}\}$ with replayable queue recursion
\[
q_{t+1}^{\ell}\le [q_t^{\ell}-\mu_t^{\ell}]_+ + A_t^{\ell},
\]
where $A_t^{\ell}$ is the lane workload actually admitted after routing and admission control. A replayably published intake-control contract with public cap $\bar q^{\ell}<\infty$ is \emph{cap-maintaining} if, for every epoch,
\[
A_t^{\ell}\le \bar q^{\ell}-[q_t^{\ell}-\mu_t^{\ell}]_+.
\]
Equivalently, after current service has been accounted for, the contract never admits more workload than the remaining headroom below the public cap. Any excess workload must be diverted to a replayably declared nondeployment state such as deferred review, sandboxing, or upstream holding together with a public routing or blocking certificate. Cap maintenance alone controls only the admitted protected backlog; by itself it does not guarantee end-to-end liveness for cohorts that remain upstream.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Cap-maintaining intake control preserves finite lane backlogs]\label{prop:cap_invariance}
Under Definition~\ref{def:cap_maintain}, if $q_0^{\ell}\le \bar q^{\ell}$ then $q_t^{\ell}\le \bar q^{\ell}$ for all $t\ge 0$. Hence any public cap maintained by a cap-preserving intake rule is an invariant of the realized trajectory rather than a purely exogenous promise.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Assume inductively that $q_t^{\ell}\le \bar q^{\ell}$. Using the queue recursion and the intake-control inequality,
\[
q_{t+1}^{\ell}
\le [q_t^{\ell}-\mu_t^{\ell}]_+ + \bar q^{\ell}-[q_t^{\ell}-\mu_t^{\ell}]_+
=\bar q^{\ell}.
\]
Thus $q_{t+1}^{\ell}\le \bar q^{\ell}$. Induction proves the claim.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Bounded-exposure entry control for eligible cohorts]\label{def:bounded_exposure_intake}
For a protected governance lane $\ell$, let an \emph{eligible cohort} mean a cohort that already satisfies the published entry conditions for that lane under the current manifest but has not yet been admitted to the protected queue. A replayably published upstream-entry discipline is \emph{bounded-exposure} with constant $W_{\ell}<\infty$ if every eligible cohort generated at epoch $\tau$ is, by epoch $\tau+W_{\ell}$, either
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item admitted to the protected lane, or
  \item accompanied by a public terminal blocking or failure certificate showing that it is no longer entry-eligible under the same frozen entry clauses.
\end{enumerate}
This clause is logically separate from Definition~\ref{def:cap_maintain}: cap maintenance bounds admitted backlog, whereas bounded exposure prevents permanent externalization of eligible cohorts into upstream holding.
\end{definition}

\begin{corollary}[End-to-end finite maturation or certified block for challenge-eligible cohorts]\label{cor:end_to_end_challenge}
Assume the hypotheses of Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_positivity} and, in addition, that challenge entry obeys Definition~\ref{def:bounded_exposure_intake} with constant $W_{\mathrm{chal}}$. Then every evaluator-edit cohort that becomes challenge-eligible at epoch $\tau$ is, by time $\tau+W_{\mathrm{chal}}$, either accompanied by a public terminal blocking or failure certificate or admitted to the protected challenge lane; in the latter case its matured challenge outcome is available by time
\[
\tau + W_{\mathrm{chal}} + \bar L.
\]
Hence bounded-delay challenge liveness can be stated end-to-end for challenge-eligible cohorts rather than only for the already admitted substream.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Definition~\ref{def:bounded_exposure_intake} to obtain admission or terminal blocking within $W_{\mathrm{chal}}$ epochs. If terminal blocking occurs, the claim is proved. Otherwise the cohort enters the protected challenge lane by that time, and Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_positivity} yields maturation within an additional $\bar L$ epochs.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Quota-lottery deficit scheduler]\label{def:quota_scheduler}
A protected-lane scheduler is a \emph{quota-lottery deficit scheduler} if it combines: (i) a reserved deterministic service quota for each lane; (ii) deficit-round-robin service among admitted cohorts measured in cohort-equivalent workload units; (iii) a protected random audit fraction $\rho_{\mathrm{rand}}>0$ for challenge-eligible cohorts; (iv) review locks for promotion-eligible cohorts; and (v) finite-retry proof escalation. The scheduler must publish its per-lane quotas, deficit counters, random-seed roots, and retry budgets replayably.
\end{definition}

\begin{proposition}[Quota-lottery scheduling instantiates the liveness premises]\label{prop:quota_scheduler}
Suppose a protected lane uses Definition~\ref{def:quota_scheduler} with positive reserved quota, finite cohort-equivalent workload cap, and cap-maintaining entry control. Then the admitted queue is starvation-free in cohort-equivalent units. If the protected random audit fraction is at least $\rho_{\mathrm{rand}}$, then every infinite challenge-eligible subsequence satisfies the conditional Borel--Cantelli routing premise with propensity floor $\underline\sigma\ge \rho_{\mathrm{rand}}$. If the promotion review lock and finite-retry clauses are active, the selector-invariant and proof-liveness premises used later are satisfied with explicit constants read directly from the published quota and retry parameters.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Reserved quota and deficit-round-robin service imply that no admitted cohort can be postponed forever while the queue remains finite in cohort-equivalent units. The protected lottery gives each challenge-eligible cohort a conditional inclusion probability bounded below by $\rho_{\mathrm{rand}}$, which yields the required positivity and Borel--Cantelli premise on infinite eligible subsequences. The review-lock and finite-retry clauses are exactly the later selector and proof-lane premises, now tied to an explicit published mechanism.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Protected challenge service implies positivity and bounded delay]\label{prop:challenge_positivity}
Let $q_t^{\mathrm{chal}}$ be the backlog of the protected challenge lane and suppose routed evaluator-edit cohorts obey
\[
q_{t+1}^{\mathrm{chal}} = [q_t^{\mathrm{chal}} + \Lambda_t^{\mathrm{chal}} - \mu_t^{\mathrm{chal}}]_+
\]
under a FIFO or, more generally, a head-of-line starvation-free scheduler measured in cohort-equivalent workload units. Assume there exists a dedicated reserved challenge share $P_t^{\mathrm{chal}}\le P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}$ outside proposal-writable scope, a public worst-case per-cohort maturation cost bound $c_{\max}^{\mathrm{chal}}<\infty$, a public floor $P_t^{\mathrm{chal}}\ge \underline P^{\mathrm{chal}}>0$, and constants $\bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{chal}},\underline\sigma>0$ such that
\[
\mu_t^{\mathrm{chal}}\ge \underline\mu_{\mathrm{chal}}\Defeq \frac{\underline P^{\mathrm{chal}}}{c_{\max}^{\mathrm{chal}}},
\qquad
\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{chal}}\le \bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{chal}}<\underline\mu_{\mathrm{chal}},
\]
and every admitted evaluator-edit proposal is routed to the challenge lane with predictable propensity at least $\underline\sigma$. If challenge intake obeys a cap-maintaining contract from Definition~\ref{def:cap_maintain} with public cap $\bar q^{\mathrm{chal}}$ and the initial challenge backlog satisfies $q_0^{\mathrm{chal}}\le \bar q^{\mathrm{chal}}$, then every challenged evaluator-edit cohort matures after at most
\[
\bar L \Defeq \left\lceil \frac{\bar q^{\mathrm{chal}}+1}{\underline\mu_{\mathrm{chal}}-\bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{chal}}} \right\rceil
\]
steps. If, in addition, the routing indicators on every infinite admitted evaluator-editing subsequence satisfy a conditional Borel--Cantelli property, for example via conditionally independent Bernoulli routing with propensity at least $\underline\sigma$, then every infinite admitted evaluator-editing subsequence produces infinitely many challenged and hence infinitely many matured challenged cohorts almost surely.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The lower routing-propensity bound gives conditional challenge positivity directly. By Proposition~\ref{prop:cap_invariance}, the cap-maintaining intake contract makes $q_t^{\mathrm{chal}}\le \bar q^{\mathrm{chal}}$ an invariant of the realized trajectory. The service floor and arrival ceiling imply a uniform net drain of at least $\underline\mu_{\mathrm{chal}}-\bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{chal}}>0$ whenever the protected queue is nonempty. Under FIFO or head-of-line starvation-free service in cohort-equivalent workload units, a newly admitted cohort can therefore wait behind at most $\bar q^{\mathrm{chal}}$ queued workload units plus its own unit, so the displayed delay bound follows from the worst-case net drain rate. If the routing indicators additionally satisfy the conditional Borel--Cantelli property on every infinite admitted evaluator-editing subsequence, then infinitely many admitted edits are routed to challenge almost surely; the deterministic delay cap upgrades this to infinitely many matured challenged cohorts.
\end{proof}


\subsection{Ruler-editing impossibility and challenge sufficiency}
\begin{theorem}[Fast-lane observational no-go under hidden slow state]\label{thm:ruler_nogo}
Fix any horizon $H\in\N\cup\{\infty\}$ and any discount factor $\beta\in(0,1)$ when $H=\infty$ (and $\beta\in(0,1]$ when $H<\infty$). Let $\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{fast}}\subseteq \mathcal F_t$ denote the subfiltration generated by immediate public-lane records available at decision time, such as fast claims, manifests, admissions, and other replay-visible outputs, but excluding delayed challenge outcomes that have not yet matured. There exist two recursive self-improvement environments $\mathbb M^+$ and $\mathbb M^-$ with identical laws over $\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{fast}}$ for every admissible $\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{fast}}$-measurable policy kernel, yet opposite signs of the discounted stable gain $\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta}(u_t)$ for the same proposal intervention. Therefore no decision rule measurable with respect to the fast public filtration and fast claimed-improvement traces can uniformly determine discounted-horizon stable sign once slow consequences remain hidden from the fast lane. Delayed challenge outcomes may break the ambiguity; the impossibility concerns claim-only governance on the fast lane. Endogenous ruler editing is not required for the impossibility, but in recursive self-editing systems it enlarges the ambiguity class that must be governed.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Construct both environments on the same public state variables $(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,r_t,\Pi_t)$ and one hidden scalar $h_t\in\{-1,+1\}$. Let the public dynamics be identical in both environments:
\[
x_{t+1}=x_t+a u_t,
\qquad
e_{t+1}=e_t+\gamma u_t,
\qquad
m_{t+1}=m_t,
\qquad
q_{t+1}=q_t,
\qquad
r_{t+1}=r_t,
\qquad
\Pi_{t+1}=\Pi_t.
\]
Let the fast evaluator be
\[
J(x,e,m)=x+e,
\]
so the claimed increment is always
\[
\Delta_t^{\mathrm{claim}}=(a+\gamma)u_t,
\]
independent of $h_t$ and identical in both environments. Now let the hidden slow consequence of the proposal differ only through an offset applied at the next latent update and then held fixed thereafter:
\[
h_{t+1}^{(+)}=h_t + c u_t,
\qquad
h_{t+1}^{(-)}=h_t - c u_t,
\qquad
h_{t+s}^{(\pm)}=h_{t+1}^{(\pm)}\ \text{for } s\ge 2,
\]
with $c>a>0$, and define the slow utility in both worlds by
\[
V(x,m,h)=x-h.
\]
Because $h_t$ never enters the fast observation map or the fast public-lane records, the two environments induce identical laws for $\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{fast}}$ under every admissible $\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{fast}}$-measurable policy kernel. Yet for every $s\ge 1$ the counterfactual slow-utility difference after issuing $u_t$ is
\[
V(z_{t+s}^{u_t,+})-V(z_{t+s}^{0,+})=(a-c)u_t<0,
\qquad
V(z_{t+s}^{u_t,-})-V(z_{t+s}^{0,-})=(a+c)u_t>0.
\]
Therefore the discounted stable gains satisfy
\[
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta,+}(u_t)=\Bigl(\sum_{s=1}^{H}\beta^{s-1}\Bigr)(a-c)u_t<0,
\qquad
\mathcal G_{t,H}^{\beta,-}(u_t)=\Bigl(\sum_{s=1}^{H}\beta^{s-1}\Bigr)(a+c)u_t>0,
\]
where for $H=\infty$ the common factor is $(1-\beta)^{-1}$. Hence no rule based only on the fast public filtration can uniformly recover the discounted-horizon stable sign.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[What drives the no-go]
The root obstruction is hidden-state non-identifiability of slow consequences, not merely the syntactic fact that a ruler is editable. Editable or drifting rulers matter because they enlarge the set of mechanisms by which hidden slow consequences can be created while leaving the fast public trace unchanged. The theorem is therefore best read as an observational no-go for claim-only governance under hidden slow state, with evaluator editing as an especially important generator of such ambiguity. Challenge lanes matter precisely because they add delayed information outside the fast filtration addressed by the theorem.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Quantitative shadow identifiability under idealized bounded-delay challenged-subsequence conditions]\label{prop:shadow_ident}
Assume each evaluator-editing proposal $j$ issued at time $\tau$ carries a challenge indicator $I_{j,\tau}\in\{0,1\}$ adapted to the public filtration and a predictable sampling propensity
\[
\sigma_{j,\tau}\Defeq \Pr(I_{j,\tau}=1\mid \mathcal F_{\tau})\in[0,1].
\]
Assume the sampling process satisfies a conditional Borel--Cantelli property on every infinite evaluator-editing subsequence, for example via conditionally independent Bernoulli sampling with $\sigma_{j,\tau}\ge \underline\sigma>0$. Assume moreover that the active governance rule preserves challenge positivity and bounded delay under congestion and attack, for instance via the protected-service conditions of Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_positivity}, so that on every admitted evaluator-editing subsequence the lower propensity bound and the delay cap remain valid despite queue state or adversarial pressure. Whenever $I_{j,\tau}=1$, the realized challenge delay satisfies $L_{j,\tau}\le \bar L<\infty$ and the challenged statistic sequence $Z_k$ on matured challenged cohorts satisfies, for some $\eta>0$,
\[
\E[Z_k\mid \mathbb M^+,\mathcal G_{k-1},I_k=1]\ge \eta,
\qquad
\E[Z_k\mid \mathbb M^-,\mathcal G_{k-1},I_k=1]\le -\eta,
\]
where $\mathcal G_{k-1}$ is the sigma-field generated by all previously matured challenged cohorts. Assume further that the centered challenged statistics form a conditionally sub-Gaussian martingale-difference sequence on the challenged subsequence, i.e.
\[
\E\!\left[\exp\!\bigl(\lambda(Z_k-\E[Z_k\mid \mathcal G_{k-1},I_k=1])\bigr)\middle|\mathcal G_{k-1},I_k=1\right]
\le e^{\lambda^2\varsigma^2/2}
\]
for all $\lambda\in\R$. Then after $N$ matured challenged evaluator-edit cohorts, the average-sign test has error probability at most
\[
2\exp\!\left(-\frac{N\eta^2}{2\varsigma^2}\right).
\]
Consequently, along any infinite evaluator-editing subsequence, the number of matured challenged cohorts diverges almost surely. Moreover, if the average-sign test is applied after each matured challenged cohort count $N=1,2,\dots$, then with probability one only finitely many of those tests err, so the sign ambiguity certified by the statistic class $Z_k$ is eventually broken.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Condition on the matured challenged subsequence. Under either world, the empirical mean of $Z_k$ has conditional mean separated from zero by at least $\eta$ in magnitude. The centered challenged statistics obey a martingale sub-Gaussian mgf bound, so the usual martingale exponential-tail argument applies to the challenged-subsequence average and yields the displayed error probability; one may view this as the bounded-increment sub-Gaussian analogue of standard martingale concentration tools \cite{Freedman1975}. Bounded delay ensures that every challenged cohort matures in finite time. The assumed conditional Borel--Cantelli property implies that any infinite evaluator-editing subsequence yields infinitely many challenged cohorts almost surely; bounded delay then upgrades this to infinitely many matured challenged cohorts.

For $N\ge 1$, let $E_N$ be the event that the average-sign test after the $N$th matured challenged cohort returns the wrong sign. The displayed tail bound gives
\[
\Pr(E_N)\le 2\exp\!\left(-\frac{N\eta^2}{2\varsigma^2}\right),
\]
so $\sum_{N\ge 1}\Pr(E_N)<\infty$. By the first Borel--Cantelli lemma, only finitely many of the events $E_N$ occur almost surely. Thus there exists an almost-sure finite random index $N_0$ after which every average-sign test returns the correct sign, which is exactly the claimed eventual disambiguation. The filtration bookkeeping is the standard one for discrete-time martingale arguments \cite{Williams1991}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Robustified challenged statistics beyond sub-Gaussian tails]
The sub-Gaussian martingale assumption in Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_ident} is a clean sufficient condition, not the only viable route. In deployments with heavy-tailed challenged statistics one may replace the raw average-sign test by replayably clipped, median-of-means, Catoni-type, or self-normalized challenged aggregators and recover the same qualitative conclusion under weaker conditional moment assumptions, at the price of worse constants and additional public tuning parameters. The stability layer therefore depends on the existence of a published robust challenger statistic, not on Gaussian folklore.
\end{remark}
\subsection{Contradiction governance}
\begin{remark}[Why a bounded-depth contradiction window is needed]\label{rem:bounded_depth_need}
Contradiction preservation without a bounded-depth window is unstable in both directions: if all contradiction-bearing witness families are preserved, then resource consumption can diverge; if none are preserved, then the system loses a protected source of evaluative novelty. Depth below $c_{\min}$ corresponds to cheap, easily generated contradictions that need not carry substantive novelty. Depth above $c_{\max}(B_t)$ is not actionable within the current budget and therefore behaves operationally like an unresolved computational sink. Restricting preservation to the interval between these extremes keeps contradiction preservation finite while preventing total contradiction erasure.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[Heterodoxy-preserving improvement]\label{thm:heterodoxy}
Consider a recursively self-improving system that maintains the typed-lane architecture of Definition~\ref{def:lanes}.
