If the contradiction reserve admits a positive lower policy floor, contradiction-bearing witnesses inside the bounded-depth window carry persistent contradiction obligations in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:contra_obligation}, every policy transition that would otherwise render a preserved contradiction family ineligible must either emit an explicit counted deletion event with conservation compensation or replayably transport that family to a successor contradiction family with the same challenge obligations, and for every preserved contradiction family whose survival trajectory contains infinitely many epochs at which the family remains preserved and challenge-eligible, the challenge-routing process on that infinite eligible subsequence satisfies a conditional Borel--Cantelli property with uniformly positive routing floor and uniformly bounded matured challenge delay, then every such preserved contradiction family inside the bounded-depth window is challenged infinitely often along its infinite eligible survival subsequence under future yardstick states. In particular, bounded disagreement cannot be reduced to one-shot archival theater by immediate deletion, silent relabeling, de-tagging by evaluator whim, or permanent review bypass.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Dogmatic auto-capture occurs when every bounded contradiction is removed before any slower evaluator can inspect it. The typed-lane policy prevents that exact event by preserving eligible contradiction in the heterodoxy lane, while the anti-gaming transition clause prevents the policy from making disagreement disappear merely by relabeling it out of eligibility without an explicit counted deletion. The conditional Borel--Cantelli property upgrades repeated positive routing opportunity on any infinite eligible survival subsequence into almost-sure infinitely many routed challenges, and the uniform delay bound upgrades infinitely many routed challenges into infinitely many matured challenges. Hence any contradiction family that remains preserved and challenge-eligible infinitely often also remains repeatedly inspectable by future evaluators, so the shortest path to self-sealing dogma is blocked.
\end{proof}


\begin{theorem}[Epistemic routing invariant breaks attentional bypass]\label{thm:forced_attention}
If the typed-lane architecture preserves contradiction-bearing items in storage but imposes no lower bound on heterodoxy routing load $\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}$, then there exist policies that satisfy the storage-side clauses of Theorem~\ref{thm:heterodoxy} while rendering contradiction operationally inert by setting all relevant retrieval gates to zero. In that case, bounded contradiction survives only as archival debris and no longer constrains current admissibility.

Conversely, if the forced-attention invariant of Definition~\ref{def:forced_attention} holds, then any increase in robust contradiction reserve $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ induces a proportional lower bound on live evaluation sensitivity. Hence the contradiction reserve cannot be both preserved and made collectively decision-irrelevant: total silent dogmatism by routing around the entire reserve is ruled out.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For the first statement, choose any policy that leaves the stored heterodoxy lane untouched but sets $\alpha_x=0$ for every contradiction-tagged item $x$ during current evaluation. Then $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ and storage-side preservation remain unchanged while every finite-difference sensitivity vanishes, so $\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}=0$. Thus the contradiction reserve no longer influences admissibility despite remaining on disk.

For the converse, the forced-attention invariant lower-bounds $\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}$ by a positive multiple of robust semantic volume. Therefore whenever contradiction reserve has nonzero robust volume, at least some contradiction-tagged items must continue to change the admissibility functional under retrieval ablation. The evaluation pipeline cannot silently route around the entire reserve without violating the invariant.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Protected random reserve exposure prevents familywise starvation under finite budget]\label{thm:familywise_exposure}
Assume, in addition to the forced-attention invariant, that policy exposes only a finite replayably published \emph{de-duplicated} set of contradiction families at each epoch, chosen for example as the top-$K_t$ or above-threshold preserved-and-eligible families under a public weight system $w_f(t)\ge 0$, and allocates a protected random exposure budget among those active families according to normalized lottery probabilities
\[
\rho_f(t)=\rho_0\frac{w_f(t)}{\sum_{g\in\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{act}}} w_g(t)},\qquad 0<\rho_0\le 1.
\]
Assume further that before the lottery the active-set selector applies a replayably published anti-dilution contract: near-duplicate families under the declared semantic-similarity threshold are merged or down-weighted; one-source-many-family proliferation pays a published penalty; every active family must exceed a minimum post-merge semantic-volume threshold; the resulting active-set cardinality is finite and block-frozen over declared review windows; changes in $K_t$ or threshold levels obey a replayably declared bounded-variation rule; and a preserved eligible family cannot be dropped from the de-duplicated active set except through a counted blocking, counted deletion, or compensated archival-downgrade certificate. Then every contradiction family $f$ whose eligible survival subsequence is infinite and whose \emph{post-merge} normalized weight share is bounded below by some $\underline\omega_f>0$ on that subsequence is exposed infinitely often almost surely. Combined with a replayably published challenge-routing rule that couples protected exposure to bounded matured challenge service, such a family is also challenged infinitely often. In particular, familywise starvation is blocked for every family that remains in the replayably declared active top-$K_t$ or above-threshold set with persistent positive post-merge share under the protected selector.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
At each epoch the protected random exposure mechanism chooses only among the finite de-duplicated active family set $\mathcal F_t^{\mathrm{act}}$, so the total budget is respected by construction. Because the active-set selector, anti-dilution contract, weight system, and $K_t$/threshold updates are replayably fixed over the review window, the policy cannot adversarially split one semantic family into many lottery tickets or remove a preserved eligible family from the active set without leaving a counted certificate. On the eligible survival subsequence of a family $f$ with persistent post-merge weight share $w_f(t)/\sum_g w_g(t)\ge \underline\omega_f$, the normalized lottery therefore gives conditional inclusion probability at least $\rho_0\underline\omega_f>0$. This yields a conditional Borel--Cantelli property on that subsequence, hence infinitely many protected random exposures almost surely. Bounded matured challenge delay then upgrades infinitely many exposures into infinitely many matured challenges whenever challenge routing is coupled to protected exposure.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Dynamic contradiction reserve underprovision in the asymmetric case]\label{thm:contradiction_dynamic}
Let $n\ge 2$ agents repeatedly choose contradiction-preservation efforts $a_{i,t}\in[0,\bar a_i]$ with common discount factor $\delta_c\in(0,1)$. Let the contradiction reserve stock evolve as
\[
R_{t+1}^{\mathrm{contra}} = \rho_c R_t^{\mathrm{contra}} + \sum_{i=1}^n \varphi_i a_{i,t},
\qquad
\rho_c\in[0,1),\ \varphi_i>0.
\]
Agent $i$ receives stage payoff
\[
\pi_i\bigl(R_t^{\mathrm{contra}},a_{i,t}\bigr)=\theta_i R_t^{\mathrm{contra}} - \frac{c_i}{2}a_{i,t}^2,
\qquad \theta_i,c_i>0.
\]
Then there exists a stationary Markov-perfect equilibrium with constant contributions
\[
a_i^{\mathrm{NE}}=\Pi_{[0,\bar a_i]}\!\left(\frac{\delta_c\varphi_i\theta_i}{c_i(1-\delta_c \rho_c)}\right),
\]
where $\Pi_{[0,\bar a_i]}(x)\Defeq \min\{\bar a_i,\max\{0,x\}\}$ is interval projection. For the utilitarian social planner maximizing $\sum_{i=1}^n \pi_i$, the stationary optimal contributions are
\[
a_i^{\mathrm{SO}}=\Pi_{[0,\bar a_i]}\!\left(\frac{\delta_c\varphi_i\sum_{j=1}^n\theta_j}{c_i(1-\delta_c \rho_c)}\right).
\]
Hence
\[
a_i^{\mathrm{NE}}\le a_i^{\mathrm{SO}}\qquad\text{for every }i,
\]
with strict inequality whenever agent $i$ is interior and at least one $\theta_j>0$ with $j\neq i$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Fix the actions of all agents except $i$ and write the value function of agent $i$ as $V_i(R)=A_i+B_iR$. The Bellman equation is
\[
V_i(R)=\max_{a_i\in[0,\bar a_i]}\left\{\theta_i R-\frac{c_i}{2}a_i^2+\delta_c V_i\!\left(\rho_c R+\varphi_i a_i+\sum_{j\neq i}\varphi_j a_j\right)\right\}.
\]
Matching coefficients of $R$ yields
\[
B_i=\theta_i+\delta_c\rho_c B_i,
\qquad
B_i=\frac{\theta_i}{1-\delta_c\rho_c}.
\]
The first-order condition for an interior optimum is
\[
-c_i a_i+\delta_c \varphi_i B_i=0,
\]
which gives
\[
a_i^{\mathrm{NE}}=\frac{\delta_c\varphi_i\theta_i}{c_i(1-\delta_c\rho_c)}.
\]
Projection onto $[0,\bar a_i]$ gives the displayed equilibrium formula.

For the utilitarian planner, let $W(R)=\widetilde A+\widetilde B R$. The Bellman equation is
\[
W(R)=\max_{a_1,\dots,a_n}\left\{\Bigl(\sum_{j=1}^n\theta_j\Bigr)R-\sum_{j=1}^n\frac{c_j}{2}a_j^2+\delta_c W\!\left(\rho_c R+\sum_{j=1}^n\varphi_j a_j\right)\right\}.
\]
Hence
\[
\widetilde B=\frac{\sum_{j=1}^n\theta_j}{1-\delta_c\rho_c},
\]
and the planner's first-order condition for agent $i$ is
\[
-c_i a_i+\delta_c\varphi_i\widetilde B=0,
\]
which yields
\[
a_i^{\mathrm{SO}}=\frac{\delta_c\varphi_i\sum_{j=1}^n\theta_j}{c_i(1-\delta_c\rho_c)}.
\]
The inequality is immediate because $\sum_j\theta_j\ge \theta_i$, with strict inequality when at least one other agent values the reserve positively and the interior formulas apply.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Asymmetric contradiction tragedy]\label{cor:asym_contradiction}
Contradiction reserve is underprovided not only in symmetric societies but also when agents differ in cost, productivity, and valuation. In particular, high-productivity or low-cost agents still underinvest whenever part of the future benefit of their preservation effort accrues to other agents.
\end{corollary}

\begin{remark}[Reduced-form role of the contradiction game]
The contradiction-reserve game is a reduced-form abstraction of the stability layer. It is not a full theory of semantics or commons governance. Its purpose is narrower: to show that bounded contradiction, even when socially useful for later recalibration, need not be privately supplied at the level required for loop stability.
\end{remark}

\section{Typed Memory Lanes and Promotion Rules}
\begin{proposition}[Typed lane invariants block direct semantic cross-contamination]\label{prop:typed_lanes}
Suppose a recursive self-improvement system satisfies the following lane invariants for all $t$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item only the evidentiary core may directly support current admissibility;
  \item bounded-depth contradiction is preserved in the heterodoxy lane and not immediately discarded;
  \item compressed summaries lacking context certificates are confined to the narrative lane;
  \item promotion from heterodoxy to core obeys Proposition~\ref{prop:promotion};
  \item demotion from core to narrative retires the item from direct evidentiary support.
\end{enumerate}
Then the system avoids three \emph{direct} collapse modes: uncertified narrative contamination of evidence, immediate dogmatic contradiction erasure, and silent promotion of uncertified summaries into admissibility.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Each collapse mode requires a direct type violation. Narrative contamination violates (i) and (iii). Immediate contradiction erasure violates (ii). Silent uncertified promotion violates (iv). Hence any run satisfying the invariants excludes these direct failure modes.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope of the typed-lane theorem]
The theorem blocks direct cross-contamination only. Indirect failures through parser drift, reinterpretation, or bad summarization pipelines still require separate controls. The point of the lane theorem is not to solve semantics in full, but to remove the shortest and cheapest failure paths.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Lane promotion rule with tagged reserve accounting]\label{prop:promotion}
Let $x\in\mathcal L_t^{\Het}$. A sufficient condition for promotion to $\mathcal L_t^{\Core}$ is that
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item $d_{\min}\le d_{\mathrm{prov}}(x)\le d_{\max}$,
  \item $x$ carries a replayable contradiction certificate and remains contradiction-tagged after promotion whenever it still lies inside the admissible contradiction window,
  \item adding $x$ does not reduce challenge-lane safety margin $S_t^{\mathrm{chal}}$ below policy floor,
  \item parser-family agreement $A_t^{\mathrm{parse}}(x)$ and replay success exceed policy threshold.
\end{enumerate}
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Conditions (i) and (iv) guarantee operational tractability and public interpretability. Condition (ii) prevents promotion from laundering contradiction mass out of the reserve accounting. Condition (iii) ensures that promotion does not damage the challenge process that would later check it.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Promotion-eligible delayed cohort, selector invariance, and multi-action deployment policy]\label{def:promotion_eligible}
A challenged or proof-escalated proposal cohort $u_\tau$ is \emph{promotion-eligible} at review time $s\ge \tau$ if all of the following hold on the then-active public state:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item a matured delayed certificate is available by time $s$ --- either a matured challenge certificate or a richer-proof certificate --- with calibrated lower stable-gain bound nonnegative on the declared deployment horizon;
  \item issuance-time and peak debt certificates, including any structural blast-radius bond and bundle interaction debt required by policy, remain below threshold on that horizon;
  \item base admissibility and governance-safety clauses required for deployment into the target lane hold at time $s$, including replay, parser, contradiction-tag, reserve-preservation, and any active proof-interface clauses required for that lane.
\end{enumerate}
We expose the public deployment actions
\[
a_s^{\mathrm{deploy}}\in\{\textsf{fast-accept},\textsf{defer-challenge},\textsf{escalate-proof},\textsf{sandbox},\textsf{promote},\textsf{reject}\}.
\]
A public deployment selector is \emph{eligibility-respecting} if a promotion-eligible cohort may be assigned \textsf{promote}, \textsf{sandbox}, or \textsf{escalate-proof}, but may be assigned \textsf{reject} only together with a public failure certificate showing that one of the eligibility clauses no longer holds. It is \emph{review-locked} with constants $W_{\mathrm{sel}},W_{\mathrm{audit}}<\infty$ if, once a cohort first becomes promotion-eligible at review time $s$, the target-lane thresholds and eligibility-relevant manifest clauses used to assess that cohort are frozen for the next $W_{\mathrm{sel}}$ review epochs, except that a failure certificate may be emitted under that frozen review contract and must then be audit-resolved within $W_{\mathrm{audit}}$ review epochs. It is \emph{bounded-wait} if any cohort that remains promotion-eligible under its frozen review contract and receives no validated failure certificate during that window is assigned action \textsf{promote} by the end of the window. It is \emph{exposure-bounded} with constants $W_{\mathrm{rev}},W_{\mathrm{exp}}<\infty$ if any cohort that acquires a matured delayed certificate enters review within $W_{\mathrm{rev}}$ epochs and, under the then-declared target contract, either becomes promotion-eligible or emits a public blocking or failure certificate within an additional $W_{\mathrm{exp}}$ epochs. A selector satisfying the eligibility-respecting, review-locked, and exposure-bounded clauses is called \emph{selector-invariant}: it cannot silently erase a positively certified cohort by delaying review, moving the target during review, or refusing a review-phase verdict without a public certificate. The bounded-wait clause is a separate completion property that upgrades selector invariance from review integrity to bounded-delay promotion once eligibility persists under the frozen review contract.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Selector-invariant bounded-delay deployment of positively certified delayed cohorts]\label{thm:promotion_liveness}
Let $q_t^{\mathrm{prom}}$ be the backlog of cohorts already assigned action \textsf{promote} and awaiting promotion from a protected challenge, heterodoxy, or richer-proof lane into an admissible deployment lane. Assume a work-conserving starvation-free scheduler in cohort-equivalent workload units, a public promotion service floor $\mu_t^{\mathrm{prom}}\ge \underline\mu_{\mathrm{prom}}>0$, an arrival ceiling $\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{prom}}\le \bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{prom}}<\underline\mu_{\mathrm{prom}}$, and a cap-maintaining intake-control contract from Definition~\ref{def:cap_maintain} with public cap $\bar q^{\mathrm{prom}}$, initialized with $q_0^{\mathrm{prom}}\le \bar q^{\mathrm{prom}}$. Assume also that every cohort routed to challenge satisfies Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_positivity}, that promotion uses the tag-preserving sufficient conditions of Proposition~\ref{prop:promotion}, that reserve accounting obeys Proposition~\ref{prop:reserve_conservation}, and that the deployment selector is selector-invariant and bounded-wait with constants $W_{\mathrm{rev}},W_{\mathrm{exp}},W_{\mathrm{sel}},W_{\mathrm{audit}}$. By Proposition~\ref{prop:cap_invariance}, the promotion backlog cap is then a maintained invariant rather than a free parameter. Then any cohort issued at time $\tau$ that acquires a matured delayed certificate by time $m$ satisfies one of the following alternatives:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item by time $m+W_{\mathrm{rev}}+W_{\mathrm{exp}}+W_{\mathrm{audit}}$ a validated public blocking or failure certificate is resolved, showing either that the cohort cannot satisfy the target-lane deployment clauses or that a promotion-eligibility clause fails under the frozen review contract; or
  \item by time $m+W_{\mathrm{rev}}+W_{\mathrm{exp}}+W_{\mathrm{audit}}+W_{\mathrm{sel}}$ the cohort is assigned action \textsf{promote} and is then promoted no later than
\[
 m+W_{\mathrm{rev}}+W_{\mathrm{exp}}+W_{\mathrm{audit}}+W_{\mathrm{sel}}+\bar L_{\mathrm{prom}},\qquad\bar L_{\mathrm{prom}}\Defeq\left\lceil \frac{\bar q^{\mathrm{prom}}+1}{\underline\mu_{\mathrm{prom}}-\bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{prom}}} \right\rceil.
\]
\end{enumerate}
If challenge maturity itself is available within the bound $\bar L$ of Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_positivity}, then any challenged cohort whose target contract is fixed at maturity is either invalidated by an audited certificate or deployed within at most
\[
\bar L+W_{\mathrm{rev}}+W_{\mathrm{exp}}+W_{\mathrm{audit}}+W_{\mathrm{sel}}+\bar L_{\mathrm{prom}}
\]
steps after issuance. Therefore delayed certification need not be a graveyard for good edits: under explicit review, exposure, audit, selection, and service floors it becomes a bounded-delay deployment path from the first positive delayed certificate onward.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Once a cohort acquires a matured delayed certificate at time $m$, exposure-bounded review forces it into review within $W_{\mathrm{rev}}$ epochs and then requires either a public blocking or failure certificate or a promotion-eligibility verdict within another $W_{\mathrm{exp}}$ epochs. If a blocking or failure certificate is emitted, audited resolution within $W_{\mathrm{audit}}$ epochs gives alternative (i). Otherwise the cohort becomes promotion-eligible. Review-locking then freezes the relevant target-lane clauses for $W_{\mathrm{sel}}$ review epochs, so the selector cannot make the cohort fail merely by moving thresholds or silently retyping the target contract. If no validated failure certificate appears during the audit window, bounded-wait selection forces action \textsf{promote} by the end of the frozen review window. Once assigned, the cohort joins the promotion queue with at most $\bar q^{\mathrm{prom}}$ workload units ahead of it. The service floor and arrival ceiling imply a uniform net drain of at least $\underline\mu_{\mathrm{prom}}-\bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{prom}}>0$ whenever the promotion queue is nonempty. Under work-conserving starvation-free service in cohort-equivalent units, the displayed queueing bound follows. Proposition~\ref{prop:promotion} and Proposition~\ref{prop:reserve_conservation} ensure that promotion preserves the contradiction-tag and reserve-side invariants required for the move to remain admissible.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Fast-lane impossibility becomes governed feasibility with delayed certification and selector invariance]\label{cor:governed_feasibility}
Consider any evaluator-edit proposal class for which Theorem~\ref{thm:ruler_nogo} rules out uniform sign identification on the fast public lane. Suppose such proposals are routed through Corollary~\ref{cor:end_to_end_challenge}, their matured challenge evidence yields a calibrated nonnegative stable-gain certificate via Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge} or Corollary~\ref{cor:shadow_cert}, and the resulting cohorts satisfy debt safety, governance safety, and the deployment clauses of Definition~\ref{def:promotion_eligible}. Assume moreover that, once maturity occurs, the downstream promotion lane and review process satisfy all premises of Theorem~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness}, including protected promotion service, the published backlog cap, work-conserving starvation-free scheduling, tag-preserving promotion, reserve preservation, selector invariance, and bounded-wait completion. Then those proposals remain \emph{governedly deployable}: they may be undecidable on the fast lane yet still become admissibly deployable after bounded delay unless an audited blocking or failure certificate establishes genuine ineligibility. Claim-only governance is therefore impossible in this class, but governed recursive improvement remains feasible.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Theorem~\ref{thm:ruler_nogo} blocks only fast-lane sign identification. Corollary~\ref{cor:end_to_end_challenge} guarantees that challenge-eligible cohorts are either publicly blocked within bounded time or enter and mature on the protected challenge lane within bounded end-to-end delay, the shadow-certification bridge supplies a delayed lower stable-gain certificate, and Definition~\ref{def:promotion_eligible} packages the remaining debt and governance requirements for deployment. The additional assumptions place the matured cohort exactly inside the scope of Theorem~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness}. That theorem then turns delayed certification plus protected service into bounded-delay deployment unless an audited blocking or failure certificate is validated. Hence impossibility of immediate claim-only admission does not imply impossibility of governed deployment.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Proof-carrying escalation contract]\label{def:proof_escalation}
Fix a richer replayable proof interface $\mathfrak L^{\mathrm{rich}}$. A \emph{proof-carrying escalation contract} is replayable if it specifies a finite offer deadline $W_{\mathrm{offer}}<\infty$, a finite retry cap $N_{\mathrm{retry}}<\infty$, and public success/failure packet formats such that for every escalated cohort: (i) within each offer window of length $W_{\mathrm{offer}}$, the cohort either submits one richer-proof candidate or emits a terminal escalation-failure certificate; (ii) each submitted candidate is checked by a total verifier from the declared richer interface under thermodynamic proof escrow; (iii) every successful check emits a richer-proof certificate; (iv) every failed check emits a replayable verification-failure certificate; and (v) after at most $N_{\mathrm{retry}}$ unsuccessful checked candidates without success, the cohort must emit a terminal escalation-failure certificate rather than retry indefinitely.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Proof-carrying bounded-delay deployability of proof-heavy upgrades under richer proof lanes]\label{thm:proof_liveness}
Let a proposal be \emph{proof-heavy} if its safety argument lies beyond the current constitutional proof class $\mathfrak L^{\mathrm{const}}$ but inside a richer replayable proof interface $\mathfrak L^{\mathrm{rich}}$ accepted by policy for escalation. Assume that each richer-interface checker is total and physically metered under Definition~\ref{def:thermo_escrow}, so that by Theorems~\ref{thm:godelian_ceiling} and \ref{thm:thermo_escrow} every submitted richer-proof candidate has a replayable accept/reject outcome within a public bounded physical verification cost. Assume a proof-carrying escalation contract in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:proof_escalation} with constants $W_{\mathrm{offer}}$ and $N_{\mathrm{retry}}$. Let the protected proof lane have backlog $q_t^{\mathrm{proof}}$ governed in cohort-equivalent verification workload units by a work-conserving starvation-free scheduler and queue recursion
\[
q_{t+1}^{\mathrm{proof}}\le \bigl[q_t^{\mathrm{proof}}-\mu_t^{\mathrm{proof}}\bigr]_+ + A_t^{\mathrm{proof}},
\qquad
A_t^{\mathrm{proof}}\le \Lambda_t^{\mathrm{proof}},
\]
with service floor $\mu_t^{\mathrm{proof}}\ge \underline\mu_{\mathrm{proof}}>0$, arrival ceiling $\Lambda_t^{\mathrm{proof}}\le \bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{proof}}<\underline\mu_{\mathrm{proof}}$, and a cap-maintaining intake-control contract from Definition~\ref{def:cap_maintain} with public cap $\bar q^{\mathrm{proof}}$, initialized with $q_0^{\mathrm{proof}}\le \bar q^{\mathrm{proof}}$. Assume further that once a richer-proof certificate is obtained, the downstream deployment lane satisfies all premises of Theorem~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness}. Define
\[
\bar L_{\mathrm{proof}}\Defeq\left\lceil \frac{\bar q^{\mathrm{proof}}+1}{\underline\mu_{\mathrm{proof}}-\bar\Lambda_{\mathrm{proof}}} \right\rceil.
\]
Then any proof-heavy cohort escalated at time $\tau$ satisfies one of the following alternatives:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item by time $\tau+N_{\mathrm{retry}}(W_{\mathrm{offer}}+\bar L_{\mathrm{proof}})$ it emits a terminal public escalation-failure or verification-failure certificate;
  \item by time $\tau+N_{\mathrm{retry}}(W_{\mathrm{offer}}+\bar L_{\mathrm{proof}})$ it obtains a richer-proof certificate discharging the deployment clauses of Definition~\ref{def:promotion_eligible}, enters the downstream review process of Theorem~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness}, and is therefore deployed or invalidated within at most
\[
N_{\mathrm{retry}}(W_{\mathrm{offer}}+\bar L_{\mathrm{proof}})+W_{\mathrm{rev}}+W_{\mathrm{exp}}+W_{\mathrm{audit}}+W_{\mathrm{sel}}+\bar L_{\mathrm{prom}}
\]
steps after escalation.
\end{enumerate}
Hence richer proof lanes need not be permanent freezing chambers: under proof-carrying escalation, total replayable checkers, thermodynamic proof escrow, protected proof-lane service, and finite retry budgets, proposals beyond the current fast proof regime become bounded-delay deployable or bounded-delay falsifiable. This lane design is consistent with observable-only hybrid proof/replay gating patterns, but the present theorem is a stability-layer statement about delayed deployment rather than a packet-level protocol claim.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
By Definition~\ref{def:proof_escalation}, each offer window of length $W_{\mathrm{offer}}$ ends either with submission of one candidate or with a terminal public escalation-failure certificate. Every submitted candidate enters the protected proof queue. The queue recursion, service floor, arrival ceiling, cap-maintaining intake rule, and starvation-free scheduling imply via Proposition~\ref{prop:cap_invariance} that the proof backlog never exceeds $\bar q^{\mathrm{proof}}$, so any submitted candidate is checked within at most $\bar L_{\mathrm{proof}}$ additional epochs. Because each checked candidate yields either a replayable richer-proof certificate or a replayable verification-failure certificate, and because indefinite retry is ruled out after at most $N_{\mathrm{retry}}$ unsuccessful checked candidates, the escalated cohort is resolved on the proof lane within at most $N_{\mathrm{retry}}(W_{\mathrm{offer}}+\bar L_{\mathrm{proof}})$ epochs. If resolution is failure, alternative (i) holds. If resolution is success, the cohort now satisfies the richer-proof part of the deployment contract and all premises of Theorem~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness} apply by assumption to the downstream lane, yielding the additional bounded review, audit, selection, and promotion delay in alternative (ii).
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Admissible service-scaling law]\label{def:service_scaling}
A published governance allocator is an \emph{admissible service-scaling law} if there exist per-lane protected resource counters $P_t^{\mathrm{chal}},P_t^{\mathrm{prom}},P_t^{\mathrm{proof}}$, per-cohort physical cost envelopes $c_t^{\mathrm{chal}},c_t^{\mathrm{prom}},c_t^{\mathrm{proof}}$, replayably published service floors $\underline\mu_t^{\mathrm{chal}},\underline\mu_t^{\mathrm{prom}},\underline\mu_t^{\mathrm{proof}}$, positive slack constants $\eps_{\mathrm{chal}},\eps_{\mathrm{prom}},\eps_{\mathrm{proof}}>0$, public finite caps $\bar q^{\mathrm{chal}},\bar q^{\mathrm{prom}},\bar q^{\mathrm{proof}}$, cap-maintaining intake-control contracts in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:cap_maintain}, and bounded-exposure entry controls for any upstream eligible holding states in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:bounded_exposure_intake} such that along the realized trajectory
\[
\underline\mu_t^{\ell}\le \frac{P_t^{\ell}}{c_t^{\ell}},\qquad \underline\mu_t^{\ell}-\Lambda_t^{\ell}\ge \eps_{\ell}\qquad (\ell\in\{\mathrm{chal},\mathrm{prom},\mathrm{proof}\}),
\]
with each lane initialized below its public cap. In words: governance service scaling is not treated as an exogenous miracle but as a resource-preserving allocation rule that converts protected budget and conservative cost envelopes into public service floors with positive lane slack while jointly maintaining finite queue caps through replayable intake control and preventing eligible cohorts from disappearing indefinitely into upstream holding.
\end{definition}

\begin{corollary}[Resource-coupled service scaling preserves lane-service premises and hence governed deployability]\label{cor:service_scaling}
Suppose challenge, promotion, and richer-proof lanes satisfy Definition~\ref{def:service_scaling} along the realized trajectory. Assume additionally that the non-service premises of Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_positivity}, Theorems~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness} and \ref{thm:proof_liveness}, and Corollary~\ref{cor:governed_feasibility} remain valid along that trajectory, including the routing-propensity floor, starvation-free scheduling, selector-invariant and bounded-wait review contract, proof-carrying escalation contract, total-verifier clauses, reserve-preservation clauses, and cap-maintaining intake-control contracts. Then the service-rate, queue-slack, and finite-cap premises entering those results continue to hold uniformly along the realized trajectory by Definition~\ref{def:service_scaling} and Proposition~\ref{prop:cap_invariance}. Consequently the cited bounded-delay maturity, promotion, proof-lane verification, and governed-deployability conclusions remain valid as the protected budgets scale with load. In particular, success-driven proposal throughput need not collapse the governance lanes provided service is coupled to publicly reserved resource budgets and the other structural premises are maintained.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Definition~\ref{def:service_scaling} turns protected budget and conservative per-cohort cost envelopes into explicit public service floors and positive slacks for the challenge, promotion, and proof lanes. The remaining hypotheses listed in the statement ensure that the non-service parts of the cited results are not lost when the allocator changes over time. Therefore every lane-side service premise required by Proposition~\ref{prop:challenge_positivity}, Theorems~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness} and \ref{thm:proof_liveness}, and Corollary~\ref{cor:governed_feasibility} remains satisfied uniformly along the realized trajectory, so the same bounded-delay and queue-stability arguments continue to apply.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Endogenous maintenance is external to the service law]
Corollary~\ref{cor:service_scaling} is conditional on the protected-budget allocator and intake-control contract continuing to satisfy their published floors and caps. It therefore shows that bounded-delay deployability is policy-contract compatible with success; it does not prove that an unconstrained recursive improver will endogenously preserve those contracts without a separate constitutional or resource-allocation layer.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Observable witness-comparison contract for raw realized-path dominance]\label{def:gp_class}
A pair of closed-loop regimes $(\mathsf R^-,\mathsf R^+)$ driven by a shared replayable exogenous skeleton satisfies the \emph{observable witness-comparison contract for raw realized-path dominance} if, at every epoch, all of the following hold under a common published manifest and fixed acceptance thresholds:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item the common sanitized comparison menu $\mathcal U_t^{\mathrm{cmp}}$ is replayably published and stable under the common syntax/scope/null-certificate prefilters used by both regimes, so menu engineering alone cannot create governance-capital dominance;
  \item productive proposal menus admit a replayable matching map from minus-regime admissible productive proposals to plus-regime admissible productive proposals with weakly larger direct productive increment and no worse delayed-certificate obligations;
  \item accepted matched productive proposals preserve weak dominance of productive stock and fixed-threshold governance capital at the next epoch;
  \item frontier-improving governance edits are closed under plus-regime selection and, whenever chosen against any admissible minus-regime action at the same epoch, preserve weak next-step productive-stock dominance while producing strict next-step fixed-threshold governance-capital dominance;
  \item the admissible governance edits published by the plus-regime include at least one replayable exploitation path from any strict next-step frontier gain to a later productive or delayed-deployment action whenever that enlarged frontier remains available;
  \item challenge-eligible, delayed challenge, and richer-proof cohorts are governed by bounded-exposure entry control, selector invariance, and Theorems~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness} and \ref{thm:proof_liveness};
  \item rollback, sandbox, and bounded-scope deployment actions preserve the weak productive-stock order;
  \item protected challenge, promotion, and proof services satisfy the admissible service-scaling law of Definition~\ref{def:service_scaling}.
\end{enumerate}
This definition isolates the exact explicit comparison contract under which the later realized-path claim is intended to hold. Governance is not assumed to help by rhetoric; the contract is stated so that stronger public interfaces, sanitized-menu comparison, bounded-exposure entry, delayed-certification liveness, exploitation of enlarged frontiers, and resource-coupled service preserve or expand future admissible productive opportunity under unchanged thresholds.
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Comparison-contract reading of the positive claim]
Definition~\ref{def:gp_class} is not presented as a universal law that arbitrary self-editing regimes satisfy. It is an explicit transition contract collecting the exact observable premises under which an inductive realized-path comparison is valid. The corollary below is informative only to the extent that the contract can be certified from independently published witnesses; outside that contract the paper makes no claim that stronger governance necessarily improves realized growth.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Action-induced next-step regime and post-action frontier scores]\label{def:post_action_frontier}
Fix an epoch $t$, a current regime $\mathsf R_t$, the shared replay skeleton, and an admissible current-epoch action $u$. Let $\mathsf R_{t+1}[u;\mathsf R_t]$ denote the replayably determined next-epoch regime obtained by applying $u$ under $\mathsf R_t$ together with the manifest-declared post-decision update rules. Define the \emph{post-action frontier scores}
\[
\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(u;\mathsf R_t)\Defeq \Phi_{t+1}(\mathsf R_{t+1}[u;\mathsf R_t]),
\qquad
\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net,post}}(u;\mathsf R_t)\Defeq \Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net}}(\mathsf R_{t+1}[u;\mathsf R_t]).
\]
These objects are well-typed one-step look-ahead frontier scores attached to current actions; they are not shorthand for evaluating the current frontier at an action argument.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Replayable comparison-witness selectors]\label{def:witness_selector}
Fix a regime pair in Definition~\ref{def:gp_class}, an epoch $t$, and a replayable admissible minus-regime selector $\pi_t^-$. For the realized minus action $u_t^-=\pi_t^-(C_t)$, let $\mathcal W_t(u_t^-)$ denote a replayably published nonempty set of admissible plus-regime \emph{comparison witnesses}, each of which certifies one of the comparison clauses of Definition~\ref{def:gp_class} against $u_t^-$: a matched productive action, a frontier-improving governance edit together with its next-step frontier certificate, a delayed challenge or richer-proof deployment witness once eligible, or a rollback/sandbox witness preserving weak productive order. A plus-regime selector $\pi_t^+$ is \emph{comparison-witness dominating} relative to $\pi_t^-$ if, for every realized state and minus action $u_t^-$, the chosen admissible plus action $u_t^+=\pi_t^+(C_t,u_t^-)$ satisfies
\[
(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(u_t^+;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t(u_t^+))\succcurlyeq_{\mathrm{lex}}
(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(w;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t(w))
\]
for at least one witness action $w\in\mathcal W_t(u_t^-)$. Exact lexicographic maximization over all admissible plus actions is sufficient but not required.
\end{definition}

\begin{corollary}[Inductive raw realized-path productive dominance under the explicit witness-comparison contract]\label{cor:realized_growth}
Consider two closed-loop regime-policy pairs $(\mathsf R_t^-,\pi_t^-)$ and $(\mathsf R_t^+,\pi_t^+)_{t\ge 0}$ such that $(\mathsf R_t^-,\mathsf R_t^+)$ belongs to the observable growth-promoting sufficient-condition class of Definition~\ref{def:gp_class} at every epoch, $\pi_t^-$ is any replayable admissible selector for the minus-regime, and $\pi_t^+$ is a replayable comparison-witness-dominating selector relative to $\pi_t^-$ in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:witness_selector}. Then, pathwise on the shared replay skeleton,
\[
\Phi_t(\mathsf R_t^+)\ge \Phi_t(\mathsf R_t^-)\qquad\text{and}\qquad\kappa(x_t^+)\ge \kappa(x_t^-)\qquad \forall t\ge 0.
\]
If at some epoch the chosen plus action is a productive proposal whose direct productive increment strictly exceeds that of the replayably compared minus action and the productive-transition clause maps that strict increment into strict next-step productive-state dominance, then $\kappa(x_{t+1}^+)>\kappa(x_{t+1}^-)$. If instead the chosen plus action is a strict frontier-improving governance edit, then
\[
\Phi_{t+1}(\mathsf R_{t+1}^+)>\Phi_{t+1}(\mathsf R_{t+1}^-).
\]
Later productive-state strictness then requires subsequent exploitation of that strict frontier advantage by a later productive or delayed deployment witness. Persistent strictness is not claimed without an additional strictness-preserving transition clause.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Proceed by induction on $t$. The base case is immediate because the initial public state is shared. Assume the displayed weak inequalities hold at epoch $t$. Let $u_t^-=\pi_t^-(C_t)$ be the realized minus action. By Definition~\ref{def:witness_selector}, the chosen plus action $u_t^+=\pi_t^+(C_t,u_t^-)$ is lexicographically no worse than at least one replayably published witness action guaranteed by Definition~\ref{def:gp_class}. If the witness is a matched productive action, the productive-transition clause propagates weak productive-stock and governance-capital dominance to epoch $t+1$. If the witness is a frontier-improving governance edit, the governance-edit clause yields weak next-step productive-stock dominance relative to $u_t^-$, while Theorem~\ref{thm:gov_investment} gives strict next-step frontier improvement under the common comparison manifest. If the witness is an eligible delayed deployment from the challenge or richer-proof lanes, then bounded-exposure entry control together with Theorems~\ref{thm:promotion_liveness} and \ref{thm:proof_liveness} ensures that positively certified delayed cohorts cannot remain stuck forever: once the relevant delayed certificate exists, entry, review, and protected service force audited invalidation or bounded-delay deployment. If the witness is a rollback or sandbox action, the corresponding clause preserves weak productive order by assumption. In every case the chosen plus action is no worse than some valid witness, so both displayed weak inequalities propagate to epoch $t+1$. The strict claims are exactly the immediate strict consequences stated in the corollary, and no stronger persistence statement is used.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Comparison-sound replayable surrogate selector]\label{def:surrogate_selector}
Fix an epoch $t$, a realized minus action $u_t^-$, and the replayably published witness set $\mathcal W_t(u_t^-)$ from Definition~\ref{def:witness_selector}. A replayably published surrogate score $\Sigma_t(u\,;\,u_t^-)$ for admissible plus-regime actions is \emph{comparison-sound} for the raw lexicographic objective $(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(\cdot;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t)$ if every admissible surrogate maximizer $\hat u_t$ satisfies
\[
(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(\hat u_t;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t(\hat u_t))\succcurlyeq_{\mathrm{lex}}
(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(w;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t(w))
\]
for at least one witness action $w\in\mathcal W_t(u_t^-)$ on every trajectory in the comparison class. The surrogate is \emph{complete} if a surrogate maximizer exists whenever the witness set is nonempty. Typical surrogates are replayable lower envelopes or myopic lower bounds that are only required to dominate a certified witness action, not to recover the exact global action ordering over the full admissible menu.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Comparison-sound replayable surrogate selectors preserve realized-path growth dominance]\label{thm:surrogate_realized_growth}
Under the hypotheses of Corollary~\ref{cor:realized_growth}, the conclusion remains valid if the plus-regime selector $\pi_t^+$ is implemented by maximizing any replayably published surrogate score $\Sigma_t(\cdot\,;\,u_t^-)$ that is complete and comparison-sound in the sense of Definition~\ref{def:surrogate_selector}. In particular, the plus-regime need not solve the exact one-step frontier maximization problem on line; it suffices to maximize a replayable surrogate strong enough to dominate at least one certified comparison witness for the realized minus action.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
At each epoch the witness set is nonempty by Definition~\ref{def:witness_selector}. Completeness yields at least one admissible surrogate maximizer. Comparison-soundness implies that the selected action is lexicographically no worse in the true pair $(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(\cdot;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t)$ than at least one certified witness action for the realized minus action. The proof of Corollary~\ref{cor:realized_growth} uses only this witness-dominating property, not exact maximization over the full admissible menu. Therefore the same inductive argument goes through after replacing direct witness selection by a comparison-sound surrogate selector.
\end{proof}

\begin{definition}[Admissible governance burden accounting and resource-priced frontier]\label{def:net_growth_metric}
A replayably published governance-resource burden functional $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}\ge 0$ is \emph{admissible} if it satisfies all of the following axioms along the realized trajectory:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item (Physical lower bound) there exist public constants $a_{\mathrm{cpu}},a_{\mathrm{mem}},a_{\mathrm{wall}},a_{\mathrm{eng}}>0$ such that
  \[
  B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}\ge a_{\mathrm{cpu}}C_t^{\mathrm{cpu}}+a_{\mathrm{mem}}C_t^{\mathrm{mem}}+a_{\mathrm{wall}}C_t^{\mathrm{wall}}+a_{\mathrm{eng}}C_t^{\mathrm{eng}},
  \]
  where the $C_t^{\cdot}$ are replayably logged protected governance compute, memory, wall-clock, and energy usage counters;
  \item (Monotonicity) $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$ is monotone in protected challenge, promotion, and proof service commitments, in verification and proof workload, and in any thermodynamic proof-escrow budget consumed by the current governance regime;
  \item (Bounded interaction overhead) there exists a replayably published nonnegative interaction-overhead envelope $\Delta_t^{\mathrm{int}}$ such that combining two governance commitments costs at most the sum of their separately published burdens plus $\Delta_t^{\mathrm{int}}$;
  \item (Null normalization) $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}=0$ under the null governance load with no protected challenge, promotion, proof, escrow, or verification burden.
\end{enumerate}
For a price parameter $\lambda\ge 0$, define the \emph{resource-priced productive state}
\[
\kappa_t^{\mathrm{net}}\Defeq \kappa(x_t)-\lambda B_t^{\mathrm{gov}},
\]
and for any admissible action $u_t$ define its \emph{resource-priced increment}
\[
\Delta\kappa_t^{\mathrm{net}}(u_t)\Defeq \kappa(x_{t+1}(u_t)) - \kappa(x_t) - \lambda\bigl(B_{t+1}^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t)-B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}\bigr).
\]
The corresponding \emph{net admissible frontier} is
\[
\Phi_t^{\mathrm{net}}(\mathsf R)\Defeq \sup_{u\in\mathcal A_t^{\mathrm{full}}(\mathsf R)} \Delta\kappa_t^{\mathrm{net}}(u),
\qquad \sup\varnothing\Defeq 0.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Policy relativity of resource-priced growth]
The burden functional $B_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$ and the price parameter $\lambda$ are part of the declared accounting regime. Net-frontier and net-state comparisons are therefore relative to a chosen replayably published lower-bounding price functional; they do not assert a unique architecture-independent welfare order across all possible resource prices.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Observable witness-comparison contract for resource-priced realized-path dominance]\label{def:gp_net_class}
An observable growth-promoting regime pair satisfies the \emph{observable witness-comparison contract for resource-priced realized-path dominance} if, in addition to Definition~\ref{def:gp_class}, it uses an admissible burden functional from Definition~\ref{def:net_growth_metric} and satisfies the following net analogues at every epoch:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item every productive proposal admissible in $\mathsf R_t^-$ has a matched admissible proposal in $\mathsf R_t^+$ with weakly larger resource-priced increment $\Delta\kappa_t^{\mathrm{net}}$;
  \item any strict net-frontier improvement generated by a plus-regime governance edit remains replayably exploitable by some later admissible productive or delayed-deployment path whenever the net frontier advantage persists;
  \item every frontier-improving governance edit chosen in $\mathsf R_t^+$ weakly increases the next-step net frontier, with strict improvement whenever the certified future frontier expansion outweighs the increase in admissible governance burden under price $\lambda$;
  \item accepting matched productive proposals and successful delayed deployments from challenge or proof lanes preserves weak dominance of the resource-priced productive state at the next epoch.
\end{enumerate}
\end{definition}

\begin{remark}[Comparison-class reading of the net positive claim]
Definition~\ref{def:gp_net_class} adds one further layer beyond Definition~\ref{def:gp_class}: the public accounting regime must certify that governance-resource cost is priced in a way that preserves the stated net-dominance transitions. The resulting corollary is again a comparison under an explicit contract, not a claim that every governance burden is net-promotive under every price functional. The same comparison-sound surrogate-selector idea applies to the net corollary after replacing $(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{post}}(\cdot;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t)$ by $(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net,post}}(\cdot;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t^{\mathrm{net}})$.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Inductive resource-priced realized-path productive dominance under the explicit net witness-comparison contract]\label{cor:net_realized_growth}
Consider two closed-loop regime-policy pairs $(\mathsf R_t^-,\pi_t^-)$ and $(\mathsf R_t^+,\pi_t^+)_{t\ge 0}$ such that $(\mathsf R_t^-,\mathsf R_t^+)$ belongs to the observable net growth-promoting sufficient-condition class of Definition~\ref{def:gp_net_class} at every epoch, $\pi_t^-$ is any replayable admissible minus selector, and $\pi_t^+$ is any replayable plus selector that, for each realized minus action $u_t^-=\pi_t^-(C_t)$, chooses an admissible plus action lexicographically no worse in $(\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net,post}}(\cdot;\mathsf R_t^+),\Delta\kappa_t^{\mathrm{net}})$ than at least one replayably published net witness action guaranteed by Definition~\ref{def:gp_net_class}. Then, pathwise on the shared replay skeleton,
\[
\Phi_t^{\mathrm{net}}(\mathsf R_t^+)\ge \Phi_t^{\mathrm{net}}(\mathsf R_t^-)\qquad\text{and}\qquad\kappa_t^{\mathrm{net},+}\ge \kappa_t^{\mathrm{net},-}\qquad \forall t\ge 0.
\]
If at some epoch the chosen plus action has strictly larger resource-priced increment than the replayably compared minus action and the net transition clause maps that strict increment into strict next-step net productive-state dominance, then $\kappa_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net},+}>\kappa_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net},-}$. If instead the chosen plus action is a strict net frontier-improving governance edit, then
\[
\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net}}(\mathsf R_{t+1}^+)>\Phi_{t+1}^{\mathrm{net}}(\mathsf R_{t+1}^-).
\]
Later strict net productive-state separation again requires subsequent exploitation of that strict net frontier advantage. Hence the framework can be growth-promoting even after pricing governance resources with an accounting functional that lower-bounds real protected compute, memory, wall-clock, and energy usage.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
The proof repeats the inductive structure of Corollary~\ref{cor:realized_growth} with $\kappa$ and $\Phi$ replaced by their resource-priced counterparts from Definition~\ref{def:net_growth_metric}. At each epoch the chosen plus action is, by assumption, lexicographically no worse in the net objective than at least one replayably published net witness action for the realized minus action. The net matching clause of Definition~\ref{def:gp_net_class} supplies such a witness whenever the minus-regime chooses a productive action. The net governance-edit clause supplies the witness when the compared plus move is a frontier-improving governance edit. Bounded-exposure entry, selector-invariant review, and Corollary~\ref{cor:service_scaling} keep the delayed challenge, promotion, and proof-lane premises valid along the realized plus trajectory, so delayed good cohorts still enter the deployed state after finite time without invalidating the net accounting. Therefore the same inductive step propagates weak resource-priced dominance to epoch $t+1$. The strict claims are only the immediate strict consequences stated in the corollary; no persistence beyond those steps is asserted without an additional strictness-preserving clause.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Tagged contradiction reserve conservation under admissible lane retyping]\label{prop:reserve_conservation}
Suppose every admissible promotion or demotion preserves an item's contradiction tag, policy weight, replayability status, and provenance metadata whenever the item remains inside the bounded contradiction window. Then admissible lane retyping leaves $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ invariant. In particular, contradiction mass cannot be silently erased by promoting an item from $\mathcal L_t^{\Het}$ to $\mathcal L_t^{\Core}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
By definition, $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ sums policy weights over contradiction-tagged replayable items in $\mathcal L_t^{\Het}\cup\mathcal L_t^{\Core}$ that satisfy the window and provenance requirements. Under admissible retyping, each qualifying item's indicator and weight are preserved. Hence retyping only changes the lane label, not the membership of the item in the reserve sum. Therefore the total reserve is invariant under such retyping.
\end{proof}

\begin{theorem}[Cross-basis semantic-volume anti-dilution law relative to the active fingerprint family]\label{thm:semantic_volume}
Let $E_t$ be the current contradiction reserve and let $A_{t,N}$ denote the set of contradiction-tagged items that are newly admitted during an attack window from $t$ to $t+N$ and still satisfy the reserve-admissibility conditions at time $t+N$. Assume the terminal tagged mass of the admitted attack set is
\[
T_N\Defeq \sum_{x\in A_{t,N}} w_{t+N}(x).
\]
Assume further that during the attack window every pre-existing reserve item preserves its reserve membership and tagged weight, no contradiction-tagged non-attack entry is added to the reserve, and there exists at least one uncaptured fingerprint family $j\in\{1,\dots,K_t^{\psi}\}$ whose encoder remains replay-compatible with the retained audit family. Let the post-attack kernel for that surviving basis, written on the common terminal index set $E_t\cup A_{t,N}$, have block form
\[
L_{t+N}^{(j)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
L & B\\
B^\top & C
\end{pmatrix},
\]
where $L$ is the zero-padded pre-attack kernel on $E_t$, $C\succeq 0$ is the new-item self-kernel, and $B$ encodes cross interactions between pre-existing and newly admitted items. Define the Schur-complement increment
\[
S\Defeq C-B^\top(I+L)^{-1}B\succeq 0.
\]
Assume
\[
\operatorname{rank}(S)\le r,
\qquad
\operatorname{tr}(S)\le T_N.
\]
Then the tagged mass increment is exactly
\[
R_{t+N}^{\mathrm{contra}}-R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}=T_N,
\]
while the basis-specific semantic-volume increment satisfies the exact identity
\[
\mathcal V_{t+N}^{(j)}-\mathcal V_t^{(j)}
=
\log\det\!\bigl(I+S\bigr)
\le
B_r(T_N),
\qquad
B_r(T)\Defeq
\begin{cases}
0, & r=0,\\
r\log\!\left(1+\frac{T}{r}\right), & r\ge 1.
\end{cases}
\]
Hence
\[
\bar{\mathcal V}_{t+N}^{\mathrm{contra}}-\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}\le B_r(T_N).
\]
Consequently, mass-dilution spam cannot create arbitrarily large robust semantic volume unless the attack simultaneously captures every basis in $\Psi_t$. The conclusion is explicitly relative to the currently active fingerprint family and its replay-compatibility contract; if every basis co-collapses or the transport certificates fail, the theorem becomes inapplicable rather than magically false.
\end{theorem}

\begin{remark}[Blind-spot scope of the semantic-volume law]
Theorem~\ref{thm:semantic_volume} does not identify semantically meaningful diversity in an ontology-free sense. It certifies anti-dilution only relative to the active replay-compatible basis family and the assumption that at least one basis remains uncaptured. A simultaneous co-collapse of all bases, or a transport failure that prevents comparison across basis updates, must therefore be handled by the separate basis-refresh and audit-family interfaces rather than being smuggled into the semantic-volume bound.
\end{remark}

\begin{proof}
By the bookkeeping-isolation assumption, every pre-existing reserve item keeps its membership and weight and no contradiction-tagged non-attack inflow occurs during the attack window. Hence the only contribution to the tagged reserve-mass increment comes from the terminal admitted attack set $A_{t,N}$, so
\[
R_{t+N}^{\mathrm{contra}}-R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}=T_N.
\]
For the surviving uncaptured basis $j$, apply the block determinant identity to the post-attack kernel:
\[
\det(I+L_{t+N}^{(j)})=
\det(I+L)\,\det\!\bigl(I+C-B^\top(I+L)^{-1}B\bigr)=\det(I+L)\,\det(I+S).
\]
Taking logs gives the exact increment identity
\[
\mathcal V_{t+N}^{(j)}-\mathcal V_t^{(j)}=\log\det(I+S).
\]
If $r=0$, then $S=0$ and the increment vanishes. For $r\ge1$, the nonzero eigenvalues of $S$ are nonnegative, have rank at most $r$, and sum to at most $T_N$. The AM--GM eigenvalue bound therefore yields
\[
\log\det(I+S)\le r\log\!\left(1+\frac{T_N}{r}\right)=B_r(T_N).
\]
Because $\bar{\mathcal V}^{\mathrm{contra}}$ is the minimum across bases, it is no larger than the surviving basis-specific volume, giving the displayed robust bound.
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Operational sufficient conditions for the Schur anti-dilution parameters]\label{prop:semantic_volume_operational}
Under the hypotheses of Theorem~\ref{thm:semantic_volume}, suppose the newly admitted contradiction items admit basis-specific fingerprint vectors $\psi_j(x)$ satisfying $\|\psi_j(x)\|\le 1$ for every uncaptured basis $j$, and suppose their weighted fingerprint matrix $F_j$ on the admitted attack set obeys a replayably published effective-novelty bound
\[
\operatorname{rank}(F_j)\le r
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\sum_{x\in A_{t,N}} w_{t+N}(x)\|\psi_j(x)\|^2\le T_N.
\]
Then the Schur increment $S=C-B^\top(I+L)^{-1}B$ of Theorem~\ref{thm:semantic_volume} satisfies
\[
\operatorname{rank}(S)\le r,
\qquad
\operatorname{tr}(S)\le T_N.
\]
Hence the anti-dilution conclusion of Theorem~\ref{thm:semantic_volume} follows from replayably checkable norm, weight-sum, and effective-novelty-dimension certificates on the newly admitted fingerprints.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Because $I+L\succeq I$, we have $(I+L)^{-1}\preceq I$, hence
\[
0\preceq S=C-B^\top(I+L)^{-1}B\preceq C.
\]
The Schur complement therefore cannot have larger rank than the new-item self-kernel $C$, and under the effective-novelty certificate the latter has rank at most $r$. Likewise $\operatorname{tr}(S)\le \operatorname{tr}(C)$, while the bounded-norm and weight-sum assumptions imply $\operatorname{tr}(C)\le T_N$. The displayed inequalities follow immediately.
\end{proof}


\begin{corollary}[Mass-only and single-basis reserve floors are spoof-vulnerable]\label{cor:mass_only_spam}
A governance rule that constrains only $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ can be satisfied by sufficiently many near-duplicate contradiction artifacts even when the reserve contributes negligible new semantic directions. A rule that constrains only a \emph{single} basis-specific semantic volume can also be spoofed by rewriting that basis to output artificially orthogonal fingerprints. Requiring cross-basis robust semantic-volume floors or marginal-volume admission thresholds blocks both failure modes, up to simultaneous capture of the full basis family.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proposition}[Basis-transport comparability of robust semantic volume]\label{prop:semantic_transport}
Suppose successive fingerprint families are linked by a replayable transport injection $\vartheta_t:[K_t^{\psi}]\hookrightarrow [K_{t+1}^{\psi}]$ such that for every active predecessor basis $k$,
\[
\underline\theta\,\mathcal V_t^{(k)} - \delta_t \le \mathcal V_{t+1}^{(\vartheta_t(k)),\mathrm{tr}} \le \bar\theta\,\mathcal V_t^{(k)} + \delta_t,
\qquad
0<\underline\theta\le \bar\theta<\infty,
\]
for some public distortion budget $\delta_t\ge 0$. Then the transported robust semantic volume satisfies
\[
\underline\theta\,\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}-\delta_t
\le
\bar{\mathcal V}_{t+1}^{\mathrm{contra},\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\bar\theta\,\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}+\delta_t.
\]
Hence any reserve-conservation or garbage-collection statement phrased in terms of the transported robust volume is invariant up to the declared transport envelopes and cannot be made to hold merely by silently changing the fingerprint basis. Extra newly introduced bases may lower the full successor minimum $\bar{\mathcal V}_{t+1}^{\mathrm{contra}}$, but they cannot retroactively alter the transported comparison with the predecessor family.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Take the minimum of the transported basis-wise inequalities over the predecessor index set $k\in[K_t^{\psi}]$. Because $\vartheta_t$ is an injection, the transported robust volume is exactly the minimum over the successor bases reached from the predecessor family, so the displayed lower and upper bounds follow immediately. The final sentence is then just a restatement that only replayably transported comparisons may be used for temporal semantic-volume accounting.
\end{proof}
\begin{corollary}[Multi-step transport and cocycle accumulation]\label{cor:semantic_transport_cocycle}
Suppose Proposition~\ref{prop:semantic_transport} holds along a replayably composable sequence of basis updates from time $t$ to time $t+n-1$, with per-step parameters $(\underline\theta_s,\bar\theta_s,\delta_s)$ and successor injections whose compositions remain replayably defined. Then the transported robust semantic volume satisfies
\[
\Bigl(\prod_{s=t}^{t+n-1}\underline\theta_s\Bigr)\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}} - \sum_{j=0}^{n-1}\Bigl(\prod_{s=t+j+1}^{t+n-1}\underline\theta_s\Bigr)\delta_{t+j}
\le
\bar{\mathcal V}_{t+n}^{\mathrm{contra},\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\Bigl(\prod_{s=t}^{t+n-1}\bar\theta_s\Bigr)\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}} + \sum_{j=0}^{n-1}\Bigl(\prod_{s=t+j+1}^{t+n-1}\bar\theta_s\Bigr)\delta_{t+j}.
\]
Hence temporal semantic accounting obeys a cocycle law: long-run comparison error is the multiplicative transport distortion plus an accumulated additive defect, not an arbitrary free reparameterization at each step.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Proposition~\ref{prop:semantic_transport} recursively. The upper bound after two steps is
\[
\bar{\mathcal V}_{t+2}^{\mathrm{contra},\mathrm{tr}}
\le
\bar\theta_{t+1}(\bar\theta_t\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}+\delta_t)+\delta_{t+1},
\]
and likewise for the lower bound with $\underline\theta$. Iterating this affine recursion and using replayable composability of the injections yields the displayed products and sums. The result is precisely the cocycle accumulation law for multiplicative distortion plus additive defect.
\end{proof}

\section{Sharpened Toy Models}
\subsection{Single-agent scalar versioned code-and-retrieval commons}
\begin{example}[Scalar code-and-retrieval commons]\label{ex:toy_single}
At time $t$, the state is
\[
(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,r_t)\in\R\times\R\times\R_+\times\R_+\times\R_+.
\]
Interpretation:
\begin{itemize}[leftmargin=1.8em]
  \item $x_t$ is task capability,
  \item $e_t$ is evaluator drift or ruler bias,
  \item $m_t$ is memory distortion load,
  \item $q_t$ is verification backlog,
  \item $r_t$ is aggregate latent error debt.
\end{itemize}
A proposal chooses a nonnegative step size $u_t\in[0,\bar u]$. Dynamics are
\begin{align}
  x_{t+1} &= x_t + a u_t, \\
  e_{t+1} &= e_t + \gamma u_t, \\
  m_{t+1} &= \rho_m m_t + \kappa u_t, \\
  q_{t+1} &= \bigl[q_t + \nu u_t - \mu\bigr]_+, 
\end{align}
with fast public score $J_t=x_t+e_t$, so the claimed improvement is
\[
\Delta_t^{\mathrm{claim}}=(a+\gamma)u_t.
\]
Debt is tracked cohort by cohort using the revised downside-reserve semantics. Let the structural bond be
\[
\mathcal B_\tau(u_\tau)=\lambda_B u_\tau,
\]
let the repair reserve be $U_\tau^{\mathrm{rep}}=\lambda_{\mathrm{rep}}\nu u_\tau$, and let the persistent hazard reserve be $U_\tau^{\mathrm{haz}}=\lambda_{\mathrm{haz}}\gamma u_\tau$, with nonnegative policy constants $\lambda_B,\lambda_{\mathrm{rep}},\lambda_{\mathrm{haz}}$. For each cohort $\tau$, let $g_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}}\ge 0$ be nondecreasing cumulative matched retirement, let $a_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{sec}}\ge 0$ be secondary liability, and let $b_{\tau,t}\ge 0$ satisfy $\sum_{\tau\le t}b_{\tau,t}\le q_t$. Then
\[
\eta_{\tau,\tau}=\lambda_B u_\tau+\lambda_{\mathrm{rep}}\nu u_\tau+\lambda_{\mathrm{haz}}\gamma u_\tau,
\]
\[
\eta_{\tau,t+1}=\Bigl[(1-\rho_{\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{ret}})\alpha_r\eta_{\tau,t}-(g_{\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{chal}}-g_{\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}})+a_{\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{sec}}+\lambda_q b_{\tau,t}\Bigr]_+,
\qquad
r_t=\sum_{\tau<t}\eta_{\tau,t}.
\]
This toy now instantiates the main text's downside-reserve debt semantics rather than the earlier claim-residual bookkeeping variant. The strict-conservation specialization of Theorem~\ref{thm:strict_conservation} appears as the limit $\alpha_r\uparrow 1$ with separate repair throughput.
The slower utility surrogate is
\[
V_t = x_t - c_e\abs{e_t} - c_m m_t - c_q q_t,
\]
with $c_e,c_m,c_q>0$.
\end{example}
\begin{proposition}[Single-agent full and marginal stable increments]\label{prop:toy_single_threshold}
Assume $e_t\ge0$. In Example~\ref{ex:toy_single}, the full one-step stable increment is
\[
\Delta_t^{\mathrm{full}}
=
a u_t - c_e\gamma u_t - c_m\bigl((\rho_m-1)m_t+\kappa u_t\bigr)-c_q\bigl(q_{t+1}-q_t\bigr).
\]
In the active-backlog regime $q_t+\nu u_t\ge \mu$, this simplifies to
\[
\Delta_t^{\mathrm{full}}
=
a u_t - c_e\gamma u_t - c_m\bigl((\rho_m-1)m_t+\kappa u_t\bigr)-c_q(\nu u_t-\mu).
\]
The marginal stable increment obtained by suppressing state-retention terms is
\[
\Delta_t^{\mathrm{marg}}
=
a u_t - c_e\gamma u_t - c_m\kappa u_t - c_q\nu u_t.
\]
Hence every positive proposal $u_t>0$ has positive claimed improvement and positive marginal stable increment whenever
\[
a > c_e\gamma + c_m\kappa + c_q\nu.
\]
If instead
\[
a+\gamma>0
\quad\text{but}\quad
a < c_e\gamma + c_m\kappa + c_q\nu,
\]
then every positive proposal has positive claimed improvement but negative marginal stable increment.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The claimed increment follows from $J_t=x_t+e_t$. For the slower utility,
\[
V_{t+1}-V_t = a u_t - c_e(e_{t+1}-e_t) - c_m(m_{t+1}-m_t) - c_q(q_{t+1}-q_t),
\]
which gives the displayed full increment after substitution. The marginal increment drops the state-retention contributions $(\rho_m-1)m_t$ and $-\mu$. The sign statements then follow immediately.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Stochastic shared-yardstick multi-agent commons with agent-dependent delayed challenge policy}
\begin{example}[Stochastic multi-agent shared-yardstick toy model with adaptive challenge policy]\label{ex:toy_multi}
Let $n$ agents share one fast evaluator, one memory substrate, and one verification queue. Agent $i$ proposes a step of magnitude $u_i>0$ whenever a Bernoulli arrival $A_{i,t}\in\{0,1\}$ fires at time $t$, with
\[
\Prob(A_{i,t}=1\mid \mathcal F_t)=p_{i,t},
\qquad
0\le p_{i,t}\le \bar p_i.
\]
The aggregate proposal mass is
\[
M_t^{\mathrm{prop}}\Defeq \sum_{i=1}^n u_i A_{i,t}.
\]
The shared fast state is
\[
(x_t,e_t,m_t,q_t,r_t)\in\R\times\R\times\R_+\times\R_+\times\R_+,
\]
and the dynamics are
\begin{align}
  x_{t+1} &= x_t + \sum_{i=1}^n a_i u_i A_{i,t}, \\
  e_{t+1} &= e_t + \sum_{i=1}^n \gamma_i u_i A_{i,t}, \\
  m_{t+1} &= \rho_m m_t + \sum_{i=1}^n \kappa_i u_i A_{i,t}, \\
  q_{t+1} &= \Bigl[q_t + \sum_{i=1}^n \nu_i u_i A_{i,t} - \mu\Bigr]_+,
\end{align}
with fast score $J_t=x_t+e_t$ and slow utility surrogate
\[
V_t = x_t - c_e\abs{e_t} - c_m m_t - c_q q_t.
\]
For each realized proposal $(i,\tau)$, an agent-dependent delayed challenge policy selects it for shadow evaluation with predictable probability
\[
\sigma_{i,\tau}=\pi_i(C_\tau)\in[\underline\sigma_i,\bar\sigma_i]\subset(0,1],
\]
and assigns a predictable integer delay
\[
L_{i,\tau}=\ell_i(C_\tau)\in\{1,2,\dots,\bar L_i\}.
\]
Let $\widetilde S_{i,\tau}\in\{0,1\}$ denote the conditional sampling flag with
\[
\Prob(\widetilde S_{i,\tau}=1\mid \mathcal F_\tau,A_{i,\tau}=1)=\sigma_{i,\tau},
\]
and define $S_{i,\tau}\Defeq A_{i,\tau}\widetilde S_{i,\tau}$ so that $S_{i,\tau}=0$ whenever the proposal is not admitted. A sampled proposal from agent $i$ at cohort time $\tau$ yields, at maturity time $t=\tau+L_{i,\tau}$, a high-fidelity shadow outcome $Y_{i,\tau\to t}$ satisfying
\[
\E\bigl[Y_{i,\tau\to t}\mid \mathcal F_\tau, A_{i,\tau}=1,\widetilde S_{i,\tau}=1\bigr] = g_i u_i,
\qquad
g_i\Defeq a_i-c_e\gamma_i-c_m\kappa_i-c_q\nu_i.
\]
Define the cohort-wise Horvitz--Thompson clean-shadow estimator \cite{HorvitzThompson1952}
\[
\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}}\Defeq \sum_{i=1}^n \frac{S_{i,\tau}}{\sigma_{i,\tau}}Y_{i,\tau\to \tau+L_{i,\tau}}.
\]
Let the actually observed shadow monitor be
\[
\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{shad}}\Defeq \widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}} + B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}},
\]
where $B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}$ is the integrity disturbance induced by cross-proposal evaluator capture or shadow-family collusion. For debt, let the structural bond, repair reserve, and hazard reserve of a realized proposal $(i,\tau)$ be
\[
\mathcal B_{i,\tau}=\lambda_{B,i}u_iA_{i,\tau},
\qquad
U_{i,\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}=\lambda_{\mathrm{rep},i}\nu_i u_iA_{i,\tau},
\qquad
U_{i,\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}}=\lambda_{\mathrm{haz},i}\gamma_i u_iA_{i,\tau},
\]
with nonnegative policy constants. Let $g_{i,\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}}$ be a predictable nondecreasing matched-retirement process and let $a_{i,\tau,t}^{\mathrm{sec}}\ge 0$ be secondary liability. The challenge estimator $\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{shad}}$ is a monitoring statistic for stable gain; it need not equal the matched retirement process used in debt accounting. Let $b_{i,\tau,t}\ge0$ be a backlog-attribution kernel satisfying
\[
\sum_{i=1}^n\sum_{\tau\le t} b_{i,\tau,t}\le q_t.
\]
Then proposal-local escrow debt evolves by
\[
\eta_{i,\tau,\tau}=\mathcal B_{i,\tau}+U_{i,\tau}^{\mathrm{rep}}+U_{i,\tau}^{\mathrm{haz}},
\qquad
\eta_{i,\tau,t+1}
=
\Bigl[
(1-\rho_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{ret}})\alpha_r\eta_{i,\tau,t}
-(g_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{chal}}-g_{i,\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}})
+a_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{sec}}
+\lambda_q b_{i,\tau,t}
\Bigr]_+,
\]
and aggregate debt is
\[
r_t\Defeq \sum_{i=1}^n\sum_{\tau<t}\eta_{i,\tau,t}.
\]
Finally, define the per-step downside-reserve inflow
\[
G_t^{\mathrm{res}}
\Defeq
\sum_{i=1}^n
A_{i,t}\Bigl(
\lambda_{B,i}u_i+\lambda_{\mathrm{rep},i}\nu_i u_i+\lambda_{\mathrm{haz},i}\gamma_i u_i
\Bigr),
\]
and the aggregate secondary-liability inflow
\[
A_t^{\mathrm{sec}}\Defeq \sum_{i=1}^n\sum_{\tau\le t} a_{i,\tau,t}^{\mathrm{sec}}.
\]
These are the reserve-side inflow variables relevant for debt ceilings in the revised semantics; claim mass remains useful for fast-score accounting but is not the debt initializer.
\end{example}

\begin{proposition}[Expected one-step stable increments under adaptive challenge policy]\label{prop:toym_increment}
Assume $e_t\ge0$. In Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi},
\[
\E[\Delta_t^{\mathrm{claim}}\mid \mathcal F_t]=\sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}(a_i+\gamma_i)u_i.
\]
The full stable increment satisfies
\[
\E[\Delta_t^{\mathrm{full}}\mid \mathcal F_t]
=
\sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}(a_i-c_e\gamma_i-c_m\kappa_i)u_i
-c_m(\rho_m-1)m_t
-c_q\E[q_{t+1}-q_t\mid\mathcal F_t].
\]
In the active-queue regime, where reflection is inactive, this becomes
\[
\E[\Delta_t^{\mathrm{full}}\mid \mathcal F_t]
=
\sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}g_i u_i
-c_m(\rho_m-1)m_t
+c_q\mu.
\]
The marginal stable increment is
\[
\E[\Delta_t^{\mathrm{marg}}\mid \mathcal F_t]=\sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}g_i u_i.
\]
Hence positive expected claimed improvement can coexist with negative expected marginal stable improvement whenever
\[
\sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}(a_i+\gamma_i)u_i >0
\quad\text{but}\quad
\sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}g_i u_i <0.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Taking conditional expectations in the state equations and using $\E[A_{i,t}\mid\mathcal F_t]=p_{i,t}$ yields the stated formulas. The active-queue simplification uses $q_{t+1}-q_t=\sum_i\nu_i u_iA_{i,t}-\mu$ when the reflected queue stays strictly positive.
\end{proof}


\begin{proposition}[Delayed clean-shadow estimator under agent-dependent sampling and delay]\label{prop:shadow_unbiased}
For every proposal cohort at time $\tau$ in Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi},
\[
\E\bigl[\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau\bigr] = \sum_{i=1}^n g_i u_i A_{i,\tau}.
\]
Let
\[
X_{i,\tau}\Defeq \frac{S_{i,\tau}}{\sigma_{i,\tau}}Y_{i,\tau\to \tau+L_{i,\tau}}-g_i u_i A_{i,\tau}.
\]
If, in addition,
\[
\Var(Y_{i,\tau\to \tau+L_{i,\tau}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau,S_{i,\tau}=1,A_{i,\tau}=1)\le \bar v_i u_i^2,
\]
and there exists a predictable positive-semidefinite matrix envelope $\bar\Sigma_\tau\in\R_+^{n\times n}$ such that
\[
\Cov\bigl((X_{1,\tau},\dots,X_{n,\tau})\mid \mathcal F_\tau\bigr)\preceq \bar\Sigma_\tau,
\]
then
\[
\Var\bigl(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau\bigr)
\le
\mathbf 1^{\top}\bar\Sigma_\tau\mathbf 1.
\]
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Unbiasedness follows from the predictability of $\sigma_{i,\tau}$ and $L_{i,\tau}$:
\[
\E\left[\frac{S_{i,\tau}}{\sigma_{i,\tau}}Y_{i,\tau\to \tau+L_{i,\tau}}\middle|\mathcal F_\tau\right]=g_i u_i A_{i,\tau}.
\]
The centered sum of the $X_{i,\tau}$ is exactly $\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}}-\sum_i g_i u_i A_{i,\tau}$. Therefore
\[
\Var\bigl(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau\bigr)
=
\mathbf 1^{\top}\Cov\bigl((X_{1,\tau},\dots,X_{n,\tau})\mid \mathcal F_\tau\bigr)\mathbf 1
\le
\mathbf 1^{\top}\bar\Sigma_\tau\mathbf 1.
\]
\end{proof}

\begin{proposition}[Collusion-robust shadow monitor]\label{prop:collusion_shadow}
Under Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi}, the observed shadow monitor satisfies
\[
\abs{\E\bigl[\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{shad}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau\bigr]-\sum_{i=1}^n g_i u_i A_{i,\tau}}
\le
\Gamma_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}.
\]
If, moreover,
\[
\Var(B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau)\le v_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}
\]
and
\[
\abs{\Cov(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}},B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau)}\le c_\tau^{\mathrm{cross}},
\]
then
\[
\Var(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{shad}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau)
\le
\mathbf 1^{\top}\bar\Sigma_\tau\mathbf 1 + v_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}} + 2c_\tau^{\mathrm{cross}}.
\]
Consequently any sign certification rule based on the observed shadow monitor must subtract not only calibration error but also the integrity budget $\Gamma_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The expectation statement is immediate from
\[
\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{shad}}=\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}}+B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}
\]
and Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_unbiased}. The variance identity expands as
\[
\Var(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{shad}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau)
=
\Var(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau)+\Var(B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau)+2\Cov(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{clean}},B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau),
\]
then apply the displayed bounds. The final statement follows because a positive observed margin smaller than $\Gamma_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}$ can still be explained entirely by evaluator capture.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[From oracle collusion budgets to endogenous audit envelopes]
Proposition~\ref{prop:collusion_shadow} is an interface theorem: it says how much certified margin must be subtracted once an integrity budget is available. In the endogenous-audit formulation that budget is no longer interpreted as an externally gifted constant. Theorem~\ref{thm:epistemic_singularity} supplies an endogenous replacement from cross-shadow disagreement, audit-family overlap, and declared attack reach.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Pairwise-uncorrelated specialization]\label{cor:shadow_var_pairwise}
Under the assumptions of Proposition~\ref{prop:collusion_shadow}, if the centered weighted clean contributions are conditionally pairwise uncorrelated given $\mathcal F_\tau$, then
\[
\Var\bigl(\widehat G_\tau^{\mathrm{shad}}\mid \mathcal F_\tau\bigr)
\le
\sum_{i=1}^n A_{i,\tau}u_i^2\left(\frac{\bar v_i}{\sigma_{i,\tau}}+\frac{1-\sigma_{i,\tau}}{\sigma_{i,\tau}}g_i^2\right)+v_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}+2c_\tau^{\mathrm{cross}}.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Under pairwise conditional uncorrelatedness of the centered weighted clean contributions, the matrix envelope in Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_unbiased} may be chosen diagonal with entries bounded by the displayed per-agent terms. Substituting that diagonal envelope into Proposition~\ref{prop:collusion_shadow} and then adding the collusion-variance and cross-covariance envelopes yields the result.
\end{proof}


\begin{remark}[What debt anti-masking does and does not solve]
Proposition~\ref{prop:anti_masking} blocks one failure mode --- netting a bad proposal's liability against unrelated good cohorts. It does \emph{not} by itself prevent evaluator capture or collusive score inflation. Those risks enter through the integrity disturbance $B_\tau^{\mathrm{coll}}$ and must be budgeted separately, as in Proposition~\ref{prop:collusion_shadow}.
\end{remark}

\begin{proposition}[Cohort-escrow anti-masking]\label{prop:anti_masking}
In Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi}, the debt coordinate for proposal $(i,\tau)$ is a measurable function only of the tuple
\[
\bigl(\eta_{i,\tau,t},g_{i,\tau,t}^{\mathrm{chal}},g_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{chal}},a_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{sec}},b_{i,\tau,t},\rho_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{ret}}\bigr).
\]
In particular, matched corrections or strong shadow outcomes generated by other proposals never enter the update for $\eta_{i,\tau,t+1}$ with a negative sign. Hence cross-cohort masking is impossible: unrelated good cohorts cannot retire the discounted liability stock created by proposal $(i,\tau)$.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Read the recursion for $\eta_{i,\tau,t+1}$ in Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi}. Only proposal-local retirement, proposal-local secondary liability, and proposal-local backlog attribution appear. Terms from other cohorts are absent from this coordinate and therefore cannot reduce it.
\end{proof}
\begin{theorem}[Predictable verification queue phase diagram]\label{thm:toym_queue}
Consider the queue process in Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi} and let
\[
B_t\Defeq \sum_{i=1}^n \nu_i u_i A_{i,t}
\]
be the random proposal workload arriving at time $t$. Define the predictable expected proposal load
\[
\Lambda_t\Defeq \sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}\nu_i u_i.
\]
Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=(\roman*), leftmargin=2em]
  \item If there exists $\eps_\Lambda>0$ such that $\Lambda_t\ge \mu+\eps_\Lambda$ whenever $q_t>0$, then on every active step,
  \[
  \E[q_{t+1}-q_t\mid \mathcal F_t] \ge \eps_\Lambda.
  \]
  Consequently, any policy that keeps the queue active over a nonvanishing fraction of time incurs at least linear expected backlog growth on that active subsequence.
  \item If there exists $\eps_\mu>0$ such that $\Lambda_t\le \mu-\eps_\mu$ for all $t$ and the centered workload has uniformly bounded conditional second moment, then the quadratic drift inequality of Proposition~\ref{prop:queue_first_moment} holds, yielding bounded time-average backlog. This is the correct non-Markov statement for the predictable-load setting; no positive-recurrence claim is needed.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
