If $q_t>0$, reflection is inactive and $q_{t+1}-q_t=B_t-\mu$, so the conditional drift is $\Lambda_t-\mu$. This proves part (i). Part (ii) is exactly the negative-drift regime handled by Proposition~\ref{prop:queue_first_moment}.
\end{proof}


\begin{proposition}[Time-average backlog bound under service slack and second-moment control]\label{prop:queue_first_moment}
In Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi}, assume there exists $\eps_\mu>0$ such that
\[
\Lambda_t\le \mu-\eps_\mu
\qquad\text{for all }t,
\]
and the centered one-step workload has uniformly bounded conditional second moment:
\[
\E\bigl[(B_t-\mu)^2\mid \mathcal F_t\bigr]\le V_B
\qquad\text{for all }t.
\]
Then the quadratic Lyapunov function $L(q)=q^2$ satisfies
\[
\E[q_{t+1}^2-q_t^2\mid \mathcal F_t]\le -2\eps_\mu q_t + V_B.
\]
Consequently, for every horizon $T\ge1$,
\[
\frac1T\sum_{t=0}^{T-1}\E[q_t]
\le
\frac{\E[q_0^2]}{2\eps_\mu T}+\frac{V_B}{2\eps_\mu},
\]
and hence
\[
\limsup_{T\to\infty}\frac1T\sum_{t=0}^{T-1}\E[q_t]
\le
\frac{V_B}{2\eps_\mu}.
\]
This is a standard Lyapunov-drift guarantee for general stochastic systems with predictable load and bounded conditional quadratic variation \cite{Neely2010}.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
Using $[x]_+^2\le x^2$ and $q_{t+1}=[q_t+B_t-\mu]_+$,
\[
q_{t+1}^2-q_t^2
\le
2q_t(B_t-\mu)+(B_t-\mu)^2.
\]
Take conditional expectations and use $\E[B_t\mid\mathcal F_t]=\Lambda_t\le \mu-\eps_\mu$ together with the assumed second-moment bound to obtain the displayed drift inequality. Summing over $t=0,\dots,T-1$ and telescoping yields the time-average backlog bound.
\end{proof}
\begin{theorem}[Discounted debt envelope under bounded reserve inflow, secondary liability, and queue cap]\label{thm:shadow_debt}
In Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi}, suppose the per-step downside-reserve inflow, aggregate secondary-liability inflow, and verification backlog are pathwise bounded by
\[
G_t^{\mathrm{res}}\le \bar G^{\mathrm{res}},
\qquad
A_t^{\mathrm{sec}}\le \bar A^{\mathrm{sec}},
\qquad
q_t\le B_q
\qquad\text{for all }t.
\]
Then aggregate debt satisfies the pathwise recursion
\[
r_{t+1}\le \alpha_r r_t + \bar G^{\mathrm{res}} + \bar A^{\mathrm{sec}} + \lambda_q B_q,
\]
and therefore obeys the deterministic ceiling
\[
r_t
\le
\alpha_r^t r_0 + \frac{\bar G^{\mathrm{res}} + \bar A^{\mathrm{sec}} + \lambda_q B_q}{1-\alpha_r}
\qquad\text{for all }t\ge0.
\]
The result does not require full challenge coverage: bounded debt follows from bounded reserve inflow, bounded secondary liability, discounted persistence, and queue discipline, while challenge coverage and delay matter primarily for identifiability and timely certification.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
For any existing cohort $(i,\tau)$, the matched-retirement process is nondecreasing and the retirement fraction satisfies $\rho_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{ret}}\in[0,1]$, hence
\[
\eta_{i,\tau,t+1}\le \alpha_r\eta_{i,\tau,t}+a_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{sec}}+\lambda_q b_{i,\tau,t}.
\]
New cohorts entering at time $t$ contribute initial stock exactly equal to their downside reserves, whose aggregate is at most $G_t^{\mathrm{res}}\le \bar G^{\mathrm{res}}$. Summing over all cohorts and using $\sum_{i,\tau\le t}a_{i,\tau,t+1}^{\mathrm{sec}}\le \bar A^{\mathrm{sec}}$ together with $\sum_{i,\tau\le t}b_{i,\tau,t}\le q_t\le B_q$ gives
\[
r_{t+1}\le \alpha_r r_t + \bar G^{\mathrm{res}} + \bar A^{\mathrm{sec}} + \lambda_q B_q.
\]
Iterating the affine recursion yields the displayed ceiling.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Mean debt bound under bounded mean reserve inflow and backlog envelope]\label{cor:shadow_debt_mean}
If instead of pathwise caps one only knows that
\[
\sup_t \E[G_t^{\mathrm{res}}]\le \bar G^{\mathrm{res}},
\qquad
\sup_t \E[A_t^{\mathrm{sec}}]\le \bar A^{\mathrm{sec}},
\qquad
\sup_t \E[q_t]\le \bar q,
\]
then
\[
\E[r_t]
\le
\alpha_r^t r_0 + \frac{\bar G^{\mathrm{res}} + \bar A^{\mathrm{sec}} + \lambda_q\bar q}{1-\alpha_r}
\qquad\text{for all }t\ge0.
\]
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Take expectations in the one-step domination
\[
r_{t+1}\le \alpha_r r_t + G_t^{\mathrm{res}} + A_t^{\mathrm{sec}} + \lambda_q q_t,
\]
and iterate.
\end{proof}

\begin{corollary}[Delayed challenge policy law]\label{cor:delayed_challenge_policy}
A stochastic multi-agent improvement loop needs two different control layers. Positive delayed challenge sampling with bounded delay is what makes hidden harmful edits statistically identifiable. Queue discipline and bounded claim inflow are what keep discounted debt operationally bounded. Confusing these two jobs leads to bad policy: more sampling does not by itself repair congestion, and more throughput does not by itself resolve ruler-editing ambiguity.
\end{corollary}

\begin{corollary}[Deterministic homogeneous threshold]\label{cor:toym_det_threshold}
If $A_{i,t}\equiv 1$ and $a_i=a$, $\gamma_i=\gamma$, $\kappa_i=\kappa$, $\nu_i=\nu$, $u_i=u$ for all $i$, then $\Lambda_t\equiv n\nu u$ and Theorem~\ref{thm:toym_queue} reduces to the deterministic threshold
\[
n_{\mathrm{crit}} = \frac{\mu}{\nu u}.
\]
Thus the deterministic phase boundary is the unit-arrival specialization of the stochastic law.
\end{corollary}

\begin{corollary}[Shared-ruler scaling under random proposals]\label{cor:shared_ruler_scaling}
Under Example~\ref{ex:toy_multi}, expected claimed improvement scales as
\[
\sum_{i=1}^n p_{i,t}(a_i+\gamma_i)u_i,
\]
while verification slack scales as $\mu-\Lambda_t$. Therefore systems that look locally beneficial on a per-arrival basis can nevertheless become globally unstable once random aggregate pressure pushes the predictable load $\Lambda_t$ above service capacity.
\end{corollary}
\section{Operationalization and Falsification}
\subsection{Two-regime comparator-and-challenge toy for the revised hard core}
\begin{example}[Two-regime ruler-edit toy with class/block challenge certification]\label{ex:toy_ruleredit}
Consider two regimes $\mathsf R^-$ and $\mathsf R^+$ that differ only by a ruler edit affecting the fast evaluator and challenge protocol. Both regimes share the same sanitized menu $\widetilde{\mathcal U}=\{u^{\mathrm{safe}},u^{\mathrm{risky}}\}$ and the same public slow-utility surrogate $V$. The current proposal belongs to class $\mathcal C_*$ and block-compatibility family $\mathfrak B_*$. Under both regimes, the block-frozen challenge target for the safe proposal is
\[
\mathcal M_t^{\mathrm{chal}}(1;\mathcal C_*,\mathfrak B_*)=m_*>0,
\]
with replayable lower certificate $\underline m_*$. The ruler edit in $\mathsf R^+$ weakly improves every Interface-0 predicate, preserves the same class/block assignment, lowers the transport residual from $\delta_-^{\mathrm{tr}}$ to $\delta_+^{\mathrm{tr}}\le \delta_-^{\mathrm{tr}}$, lowers comparator diameter from $d_-^{\mathrm{cmp}}$ to $d_+^{\mathrm{cmp}}\le d_-^{\mathrm{cmp}}$, and weakly improves every Interface-C floor, while proposal-local debt and challenge backlog are no worse. Then the operational one-step lower bound for $u^{\mathrm{safe}}$ satisfies
\[
\underline L_t^+(u^{\mathrm{safe}})
= a_+\underline m_* - b_+ - \delta_+^{\mathrm{tr}} - d_+^{\mathrm{cmp}}
\ge
a_-\underline m_* - b_- - \delta_-^{\mathrm{tr}} - d_-^{\mathrm{cmp}}
= \underline L_t^-(u^{\mathrm{safe}}),
\]
whenever the published coefficients satisfy $a_+\ge a_-\ge0$ and $b_+\le b_-$. This toy directly instantiates the class/block challenge certificate, transport residual, comparator burden, and one-step admissibility monotonicity used in the main text.
\end{example}

\begin{proposition}[One-step operator monotonicity in the ruler-edit toy]\label{prop:toy_ruleredit_mono}
In Example~\ref{ex:toy_ruleredit}, if $\mathsf R^+ \succeq^{\mathrm{feas}}_{t,\Pi} \mathsf R^-$ and the safe proposal is admissible under $\mathsf R^-$, then it is admissible under $\mathsf R^+$ and its replayable one-step lower stable-gain bound is no smaller under $\mathsf R^+$ than under $\mathsf R^-$. If the active class/block pair lacks the minimum matured support count required by the manifest, both regimes are fail-closed for fast deployment and the proposal must be routed to challenge, proof escalation, or sandbox.
\end{proposition}

\begin{proof}
The clause-wise assumptions are exactly those required by Definition~\ref{def:feasible_order}. Therefore every Interface-0/A/B/C clause holding under $\mathsf R^-$ also holds under $\mathsf R^+$. The displayed inequality in Example~\ref{ex:toy_ruleredit} gives the monotonicity of the one-step replayable lower bound, while the final statement is the fail-closed convention from Definition~\ref{def:challenge_design} and Definition~\ref{def:confidence_manifest}.
\end{proof}

\subsection{Operational proxies}
\begin{center}
\begin{tabular}{p{0.28\linewidth}p{0.33\linewidth}p{0.32\linewidth}}
\toprule
Quantity & Observable proxy & Operational use \\
\midrule
Yardstick drift $D_t^{\mathrm{yard}}$ & score drift on frozen challenge cohort or transported probe family & refresh / quarantine trigger \\
Challenge certificate & class-conditional delayed-challenge lower CS $\underline M^{\mathrm{chal}}_{t,n}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ under blocked randomized challenge & delayed-evidence component of Interface-A gain gate \\
Transport calibration & Tier-2 matched-replay transport certificate $(a_h,b_h,\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}})$ & convert challenge evidence to slow-utility scale for Interface A \\
Comparator burden & witness-family distortion budget $\bar\delta_{t,h}^{\mathrm{cmp}}$ and diameter $\operatorname{diam}^{\mathrm{cmp}}_{t,H}(u_t)$ & robustify stable-gain admission and governance-burden pricing \\
Peak debt $\eta_{t,H}^{\max}$ & cohort-escrow unresolved mass + structural bond + rollback debt & debt ceiling and throttle control \\
Contradiction reserve $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ & tagged contradiction mass & preserve disagreement floor \\
Robust semantic volume $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ & cross-basis log-det diversity with basis-transport certificates & block duplicate spam / basis capture \\
Heterodoxy routing load $\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}$ & contradiction-tagged retrieval sensitivity under ablation & detect attentional bypass \\
Verification pressure $\Lambda/\mu$ & predictable arrivals per effective service unit & queue stability control \\
Shadow disagreement & online-vs-shadow score gap & ruler-editing / hidden-state alarm \\
\bottomrule
\end{tabular}
\end{center}

\subsection{Design consequences}
\paragraph{Challenge-lane law.}
If evaluator-editing proposals are admitted directly into production without challenge-lane delay, then the observational ambiguity of Theorem~\ref{thm:ruler_nogo} cannot be ruled out by public claim traces alone.

\paragraph{Slow-meter law.}
A sufficient architectural response to ruler-editing ambiguity is to separate a fast online metric from a slower, higher-fidelity challenge process that is not directly editable by the currently evaluated proposal.

\paragraph{Shadow-certification law.}
Retained margins become decision-relevant only after calibration. Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_bridge} therefore recommends storing challenge-lane retained margins together with explicit calibration envelopes rather than using raw delayed scores as if they were stable gain itself.

\paragraph{Cohort-escrow law.}
Error debt should be accounted proposal by proposal. Any accounting scheme that nets challenge gains across unrelated cohorts can hide bad proposals behind good ones and therefore loses the anti-masking guarantee of Proposition~\ref{prop:anti_masking}.

\paragraph{Tag-preserving promotion law.}
Promotion from heterodoxy to evidentiary core must preserve contradiction tags whenever the item remains inside the contradiction window. Otherwise promotion can launder away reserve mass and invalidate reserve-based stability floors.

\paragraph{Refresh-before-adopt law.}
If the realized crossing statistic of Theorem~\ref{thm:half_life} reaches the half-margin threshold before the next planned refresh, then aggressive self-edits should be suspended or quarantined until a slower evaluator refresh occurs.

\paragraph{Backlog quarantine law.}
If the proposal rate exceeds verification service, a stable policy must either throttle proposal generation or increase effective challenge throughput. Otherwise the active-region drift of Theorem~\ref{thm:toym_queue} drives persistent congestion, and any deterministic debt ceiling from Theorem~\ref{thm:shadow_debt} must deteriorate through the queue cap or claim-inflow cap that the policy can no longer maintain.

\subsection{Implementation mapping to logged systems}
The theory becomes operational only if the recursive improver emits enough public metadata to estimate the key latent interfaces. The minimal logging unit is a \emph{proposal cohort record}: proposal identifier, parent version, edit type, claimed improvement, evaluator hash before and after the edit, parser-family version set, queue snapshot, sampling probability, realized challenge delay, matured shadow outcome, matched correction, explicit retirement action, and every lane transition touching contradiction-tagged artifacts. The point is not bureaucratic ornament. Without cohort identity and routing metadata, one cannot even test anti-masking, reserve conservation, or delayed-certification claims. For an autonomous agent, the same metadata has direct implementation value: it turns self-modification into a sequence of replayable upgrade cohorts whose audits can be reused, whose failures can be localized, and whose rollback radius can be bounded rather than rediscovered from scratch.

The core estimands are also straightforward, but the estimator must respect the theorem interface rather than a softer average-fit surrogate. In particular, the reference scaffold of Assumption~\ref{ass:gain_matrix} may not be an unobserved Platonic path: it must be instantiated by a replayable baseline built from archived checkpoints, frozen null-policy replays, or matched shadow replays whose construction is itself logged. The gain matrix should therefore be estimated as a conservative upper envelope $\bar K$, not merely a point estimate $\hat K$: first build paired deviations relative to that replayable scaffold, then fit a nonnegative regression of the next-step deviation vector on the current deviation vector, inflate each coefficient by a high-confidence residual envelope, and test $\rho(\bar K)<1$ rather than $\rho(\hat K)<1$. For genuinely open-ended deployments, the more relevant object is the window-summed spillover envelope of Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open}; estimate how much a unit of certified productive capability growth pushes evaluator drift, backlog, debt, and replay fragility over each admissible window, then check that the resulting governance spillover remains summable. Delayed-challenge lower bounds should be estimated class/block-conditionally on challenge cohorts using the blocked randomized design of Definition~\ref{def:challenge_design}, replayable doubly robust scores, and confidence sequences or e-processes as in Theorem~\ref{thm:dr_shadow_cert} and Proposition~\ref{prop:chal_radius}. Weighted or doubly robust conformal methods may still be used, but only for auxiliary calibration-envelope estimation or transport-model diagnostics \cite{Tibshirani2019,Yang2024,Jonkers2024,JinCandes2026}; the admission-facing lower certificate is the CS/e-process object, not a generic conformal score. Queue slack is estimated directly from predictable routed load and realized service, while the Red-Queen term $c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})$ is estimated from replay time, audit depth, and environment-reconstruction cost as capability grows. Shadow-lane contamination is estimated from lag-window rewrite magnitude $S_t^{(L)}$, parser/environment migration counts, and shadow-baseline drift to operationalize Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_speed}; shadow staleness is estimated from evaluator/environment drift between refreshes to operationalize Theorem~\ref{thm:two_clock}. Replayability is monitored by the public compatibility score $G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}$, while semantic retention under refreezing is monitored by the endogenous family floor $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$ so that Proposition~\ref{prop:replay_floor}, Theorem~\ref{thm:finite_horizon}, and Theorem~\ref{thm:epistemic_singularity} can all be audited. Reserve conservation is tested by checking whether admissible promotion or demotion changes $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ after controlling for genuine entry, expiry, or replay failure, and reserve quality is tested separately through cross-basis robust semantic volume $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$. Attention bypass is tested separately through the heterodoxy routing load $\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}$ and finite-difference ablation tests on contradiction-tagged retrieval gates. Anti-masking is tested by comparing proposal-local escrow debt against any aggregate netting surrogate on downstream rollback, patch, or contradiction-resolution outcomes. Evaluator capture is tested separately through endogenous integrity envelopes, cross-shadow disagreement, audit-family overlap, and disjoint shadow replicas, because debt anti-masking alone does not bound collusive score inflation.

These observables are enough to make the theory falsifiable. If the estimated spectral radius of the coupled gain map stays below one, challenge-lane safety margin stays positive, lower calibrated retained margins stay nonnegative, and contradiction reserve remains conserved under admissible retyping, then the theory predicts bounded drift and bounded escrow in the corresponding operating region. If any of those interfaces fails, the framework predicts a concrete failure mode rather than a vague loss of quality.
\subsection{Relation to adjacent layers}
Proposal--Veto Balance contributes local self-modification stability and error-debt intuition \cite{TakahashiPV2026}. Search Stability contributes finite-context preservation and delayed verification under compression \cite{TakahashiSearch2026}. Benchmark Half-Life contributes validity decay under recursive reuse \cite{TakahashiBH2026}. MTE contributes the observable-only metrology layer \cite{TakahashiMTE2026}. Sovereign Epistemic Commons contributes typed lanes and contradiction-preserving governance intuitions \cite{TakahashiSEC2026}. The present paper uses those layers as adjacent inputs but studies a distinct object: \emph{closed-loop recursive self-improvement stability under endogenous evaluator drift}.

This positioning matters because neighboring layers solve different problems. Metrology asks what counts as credit-bearing progress. Commons governance asks how shared evidence should be admitted, quarantined, or forgotten. The present layer asks when a self-editing loop can remain governable at all once those evaluative interfaces drift endogenously. The contradiction-reserve and routing results are correspondingly narrower than a full commons theory: they concern underprovision, bypass, and delayed challenge exposure inside recursive improvement loops rather than governance of an entire shared epistemic substrate.

\subsection{Experimental plan (plan only)}
This is a theory paper, so the goal is not benchmark decoration but falsifiable operational thresholds. Each hypothesis is written in a way that can be implemented from ordinary proposal, queue, and challenge logs.

\paragraph{Protocol P1: windowed gain estimation with and without a reference scaffold.} In migration phases with a meaningful co-moving scaffold, maintain a rolling reference trajectory, estimate nonnegative one-step gain envelopes $\widehat K_t$, and then estimate a conservative window envelope for products of length $W$. The primary falsification statistic is not the spectral radius of a best-fit one-step matrix but whether the estimated window product is dominated by some public envelope $\bar K$ with $\rho(\bar K)<1$. In genuinely open-ended regimes, switch to the incremental protocol of Theorem~\ref{thm:incremental_open}: estimate how accepted capability increments push the governance variables over each window, and test whether the resulting spillover envelope remains summable. The theory predicts that runs satisfying either certified interface obey the relevant governance ceilings, while runs violating it should exhibit more frequent drift blow-ups or debt excursions.

\paragraph{Protocol P2: class-conditional one-sided shadow certification under adaptive routing and two clocks.} On challenged cohorts, publish a confidence-budget manifest $\{\alpha_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}^{\mathrm{chal}},\alpha_{h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B}^{\mathrm{tr}},n_{\min}(h,\mathcal C,\mathfrak B)\}$, build block-frozen class/block-conditional doubly robust scores, and compute replayable lower confidence sequences
\[
\underline M^{\mathrm{chal}}_{t,n}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
=
\widehat{\mathcal M}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
-\operatorname{rad}_{t,n}^{\mathrm{chal}}(h,\alpha_{h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t}^{\mathrm{chal}};\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
-\delta_h^{\mathrm{design}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t).
\]
Separately estimate a Tier-2 transport-calibration family $(a_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t),b_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t),\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t))$ from matched long-horizon replay or audited transport certificates, with the transport residual envelope itself certified under the budget $\alpha_{h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t}^{\mathrm{tr}}$. The contamination budget $\widehat\Delta_t^{\Shadow}+L_{\Shadow}\widehat S_t^{(L)}$, the staleness budget $\widehat\Omega_h^{\mathrm{stale}}(f_{\Shadow})$, and the interaction budget $\widehat\Gamma_{t,h}^{\mathrm{int}}$ are replayable proof-carrying upper envelopes under separate logged certificates and therefore do not consume the statistical budget reserved for challenge or transport confidence sequences. Compute the operational certified lower bound
\[
\widehat L_t
\Defeq
\sum_{h=1}^{H}\beta^{h-1}\Bigl[
\begin{aligned}
& a_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\,\underline M^{\mathrm{chal}}_{t,n}(h;\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
-b_h(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)\\
&\quad -\delta_h^{\mathrm{tr}}(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)
-\widehat\Delta_t^{\Shadow}
-L_{\Shadow}\widehat S_t^{(L)}\\
&\quad -\widehat\Omega_h^{\mathrm{stale}}(f_{\Shadow})
-\widehat\Gamma_{t,h}^{\mathrm{int}}
\end{aligned}
\Bigr].
\]
If the current pair $(\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ has insufficient matured support, or fewer than $n_{\min}(h,\mathcal C_t,\mathfrak B_t)$ usable matured cohorts at the required horizon, Interface A is fail-closed and the proposal must be routed to challenge, proof escalation, or sandbox. The theory predicts that positive values of $\widehat L_t$ correlate with future slow-lane benefit, whereas leaving the viability band of Theorem~\ref{thm:two_clock} or violating the speed limit from Proposition~\ref{prop:shadow_speed} should sharply degrade sign reliability.

\paragraph{Protocol P3: queue-slack and repair-throughput intervention.} Vary proposal throttling, challenge throughput, and explicit repair throughput so that both the predictable load ratio $\Lambda_t/\mu$ and the strict-conservation balance $\bar\lambda_L+\lambda_q\bar q-(1-\eps_{\mathrm{rep}})\mu^{\mathrm{rep}}$ cross zero. The theory predicts two distinct thresholds: one for verification congestion and one for repair throughput. Below both thresholds, backlog and debt are controlled; above the verification threshold backlog grows, and above the repair threshold strict-conservation debt drifts upward even if bugs are found quickly.

\paragraph{Protocol P3b: Red-Queen verification and governance audit.} Estimate capability-dependent verification complexity $c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})$ from replay time, proof-check time, environment rebuild cost, and challenge-depth cost at each capability level. Separately estimate governance recomputation cost $c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$ for semantic-volume, routing-sensitivity, replay-floor, and integrity-envelope checks, together with certificate-verification cost $\widetilde c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$ and fallback-audit fraction $\sigma_t^{\mathrm{gov}}$. Compare predictable load $\Lambda_t$ with effective service $P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}/(c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})+\widehat c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t))$. The theory predicts sharp queue deterioration once $\Lambda_t(c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})+\widehat c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t))$ persistently exceeds physical verification budget $P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}$.

\paragraph{Protocol P3c: physical resource-escrow audit.} Log the total physical budget $P_t^{\mathrm{tot}}$, the reserved verification share $P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}$, the ratio $\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}$, and the attestation status of the allocator controlling this split. The theory predicts that runs without a protected lower floor on $\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}$ can starve replay and shadow service even when software-side acceptance predicates look healthy, whereas runs satisfying the resource-escrow invariant should keep the verification clocks alive whenever workload slack remains positive.

\paragraph{Protocol P4: anti-masking ablation.} Compare cohort-escrow accounting against aggregate netting on mixed-quality proposal streams. The key endpoint is downstream rollback or contradiction-resolution need. The theory predicts that proposal-local escrow debt has higher precision for harmful proposals because unrelated good cohorts cannot cancel them.

\paragraph{Protocol P5: reserve-conservation, robust-semantic-volume, routing, replay-floor, and semantic-horizon audit.} Re-run the same admissible promotion, demotion, parser-update, and environment-update schedule under two bookkeeping policies: one that preserves tags, replay floors, robust-semantic-volume thresholds, and heterodoxy routing load via refreezing and forced-attention checks, and one that does not. In the first policy, log replay compatibility $G_t^{\mathrm{replay}}$, endogenous semantic floor $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$, contradiction mass $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$, basis-specific semantic volumes $\mathcal V_t^{(k)}$, robust semantic volume $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$, and heterodoxy routing load $\mathfrak A_t^{\Het}$. The theory predicts invariance of $R_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ under the tag-preserving policy up to genuine entry and expiry noise, bounded loss of $\bar{\mathcal V}_t^{\mathrm{contra}}$ under spam rejection and representation capture by any strict subset of bases, maintenance of the replay floor on retained audit items, but gradual decay of effective evidentiary weight consistent with Theorem~\ref{thm:finite_horizon}. A successful audit should therefore show replay preservation, basis-robust semantic diversity, and nonzero routing sensitivity rather than mere storage.

\paragraph{Minimal logging contract.} At minimum, \emph{raw proposal logs} should include proposal identifier and time, parent version, evaluator hash before and after edit, parser-family version set, routed lane, declared writable scope, declared dependency-closure size, queue snapshot, replay-compatibility score, contradiction-tag status, provenance depth, allocator lineage identifier, migration-attestation transcript hash, reserved verification ratio before and after migration, and lane-transition record. \emph{Derived governance metrics} should include claim mass, systemic risk bond, challenge sampling probability, realized challenge delay, matured shadow outcome, matched retirement credit, secondary-liability charge, explicit retirement action, contradiction fingerprints for each encoder family, robust-semantic-volume marginal gain or loss, heterodoxy routing sensitivity, dropped and regenerated contradiction mass, and dropped and regenerated robust semantic volume. \emph{Audit artifacts} should include constitutional proof-language tag, proof length, proof-check runtime and memory, checker identifier, PMU-measured wall-clock and energy, proof-preemption flag and reason, scrubber family identifier, scrubber randomness attestation or commitment, attacker-conditioned entropy estimate for scrubber seeds, empirical scrubber-capacity estimate, and garbage-collection event identifier. The point is to separate what must be logged directly from what may be recomputed offline and from what is itself an auditable certificate.

\paragraph{Primary metrics.} Estimated window-product spectral radius, yardstick drift ceiling violations, certified lower stable-gain bound, shadow contamination budget, singularity margins $\Xi^{\Shadow}-A^{\mathrm{adv}}$ and $\Xi^{\Replay}-A^{\mathrm{adv}}$, Red-Queen load ratio $\Lambda_t(c^{\mathrm{ver}}(K_t^{\mathrm{cap}})+\widehat c_t^{\mathrm{gov}}(u_t,\pi_t))/P_t^{\mathrm{verif}}$, queue mean and tail, proposal-local peak debt, systemic-risk-bond excursions, causal-intervention-capacity excursions $\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)$, replay-floor violations, contradiction reserve conservation error, robust semantic-volume floor violations, heterodoxy routing-load violations, resource-escrow ratio violations $\rho_t^{\mathrm{verif}}<\rho_{\min}$, and long-horizon rollback rate.

\paragraph{Decision rule mapping.} A practical deployment policy suggested by the theory is to distinguish four interfaces explicitly and to expose a non-binary action alphabet. Interface 0 is base admissibility: replay success, declared cost budget, side-effect well-definedness, mandatory challenge routing for ruler edits, and summary typing or context-preservation clauses must all hold. Interface A is certified stable gain: the calibrated lower stable-gain bound must be nonnegative after subtracting shadow contamination, staleness, and endogenous integrity budgets. Interface B is governance debt and blast-radius safety: proposal-local or bundle-level peak debt, including the systemic risk bond at issuance and any interaction debt for coupled edits, must stay below threshold. Interface C is governance viability: challenge-lane safety margin, Red-Queen verification slack, contradiction reserve, robust semantic volume, heterodoxy routing load, replay floor, semantic-retention floor, proof-budget envelope, and resource-escrow clauses must all remain nonnegative on the admitted horizon. In operational terms the action set should be
\[
\{\textsf{fast-accept},\textsf{defer-challenge},\textsf{escalate-proof},\textsf{sandbox},\textsf{promote},\textsf{reject}\}.
\]
Fast acceptance requires the master admissibility rule of Proposition~\ref{prop:master_admissibility}. Failure of fast admission does \emph{not} by itself imply permanent rejection: evaluator edits or proof-heavy proposals may instead be deferred to protected challenge, escalated to a richer proof lane, or sandboxed under tighter scope until they satisfy Definition~\ref{def:promotion_eligible}. A practical autonomous agent can implement this by maintaining replayable estimates of both $\Phi_t$ and $\Phi_t^{\mathrm{net}}$, by running the selector-invariant review contract together with bounded-wait completion from Definition~\ref{def:promotion_eligible}, and by exposing the protected resource counters needed for Definition~\ref{def:service_scaling} and Definition~\ref{def:net_growth_metric}. The resulting deployment logic is intentionally stricter than ``positive claim'' because the paper's whole point is that claims alone are cheap theater, whereas bounded-delay delayed certification and resource-coupled service can still be growth-promoting.
\section{Limitations}
This paper is intentionally narrow. It is not a full theory of semantic truth, parser stability, ontology transport, constitutional self-revision, or shared epistemic commons governance, though it does make the replay-compatibility and gauge-transport interfaces explicit. It does not prove indefinite self-improvement, universal safety, or absolute sovereignty. It also does not claim that the canonical admissibility instance is uniquely correct. The contribution is instead a first-principles interface theory for one particular layer: recursive self-improvement when the evaluator itself drifts endogenously. Its strongest positive claims are explicitly attached to the observable comparison contracts introduced in Definitions~\ref{def:gp_class} and \ref{def:gp_net_class}; outside those contracts the paper does not assert realized growth promotion.

The framework is model-architecture-agnostic in the limited sense that it does not assume a particular optimizer, neural architecture, or training rule. It is not instrumentation-free. Replayable comparison, challenge lanes, proof lanes, protected-service counters, and resource escrows are substantive structural requirements, not cosmetic implementation details. Likewise full admissibility is certificate-based rather than oracle-based: the theory distinguishes the latent quantity of oracle stable gain from the replayable lower certificates that are actually allowed to govern admission.

Several objects are deliberately handled as conservative public envelopes rather than as exact latent quantities. In particular, the audit-diversity reserves $\Xi_t^{\Shadow},\Xi_t^{\Replay}$, attack-reach envelope $A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}$, intervention-capacity envelope $\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}(u_t)$, and endogenous semantic floor $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$ must still be instantiated by concrete proxy constructions in any deployment. The theorems say what follows once such envelopes are replayably published; they do not eliminate the engineering burden of constructing them conservatively.

The semantic-volume layer also inherits representation risk. Cross-basis robust semantic volume is designed to blunt single-basis capture, but its usefulness still depends on at least one sufficiently faithful uncaptured basis and on replayable transport certificates when the basis family changes. Likewise the hidden-state no-go theorem is an identifiability impossibility, not a claim that practical challenge design is futile; it says only that some ambiguities cannot be broken from the fast public lane alone. The public envelopes $\Gamma_t^{\mathrm{cic}}$, $A_t^{\mathrm{adv}}$, $\Xi_t^{\Shadow}$, $\Xi_t^{\Replay}$, and $\underline S_t^{\mathrm{sem}}$ remain conservative wrappers whose operational sharpness depends on the published proxy construction, but the gate discipline of Definition~\ref{def:proxy_tiers} now restricts fast deployment to Tier-1 and Tier-2 quantities so that heuristic Tier-3 signals cannot by themselves manufacture admissibility. The quantitative shadow-identifiability proposition is deliberately stronger than what arbitrary deployments can guarantee: it assumes positive challenged-subsequence exposure, bounded delay, and martingale-type concentration on matured challenged cohorts. The new challenge-service proposition, bounded-exposure entry control, cap-invariance proposition, and selection-liveness theorem narrow the gap between queue theory and identifiability, but practical deployments still need explicit scheduler, selector, bounded-wait completion, admission-control, surrogate-construction, and instrumentation choices to instantiate their constants. Full admissibility is also intentionally narrower than mere lane admission: delayed challenge, richer-proof, and sandbox actions are modeled as nondeployment states and do not enter the productive frontier until the delayed certificates and review actions required for actual deployment have been completed. Finally, the state variable $\Pi_t$ allows policy manifests to drift endogenously, but the ambient transition-law class is still fixed up to the replayable parameterizations declared by the model; unrestricted self-rewriting of the law class itself would require an additional meta-dynamics layer.

Finally, proof-carrying governance and selective recomputation can themselves become bottlenecks if deployed without explicit lane design. Requiring public certificates, protected audit families, resource escrow, and bounded-delay challenge positivity may delay fast admission for many edits that are in fact good, and may produce false negatives when good proposals are proof-heavy, expensive to replay, disadvantaged by hardware asymmetry, or stabilized by sign-canceling dynamics that lie outside the conservative small-gain wrapper. The framework therefore needs the richer action alphabet formalized above, together with review-locked deployment selection, bounded-delay proof and promotion service, cap-maintaining intake together with bounded-exposure entry control, service scaling with success, replayable comparison-sound surrogate selection, and the governance-investment interface: challenge routing, proof escalation, sandboxing, and promotive governance edits are what prevent bounded verification discipline from degenerating into blanket anti-growth rejection when the ruler can rewrite itself. The choice among challenge, proof, sandbox, and immediate deployment is itself a separate routing-control problem; the present paper provides admissibility and liveness contracts for those lanes, not an optimal global router. A full welfare analysis of this false-negative trade-off is outside the present paper.

\section{Conclusion}
Recursive self-improvement becomes substantially harder once the ruler moves with the object being improved. Benchmarks decay, parser registries drift, challenge queues backlog, memory substrates are rewritten, and even the proof language used to certify safety can become a bottleneck. The right abstraction is therefore not one-step optimization but coupled admission under moving evaluative interfaces. This paper formalizes that layer as a first-principles interface theory, model-architecture-neutral but infrastructure- and instrumentation-explicit, conditional on published replayable interfaces, and sharpens the separation between four interfaces that are easy to conflate: base admissibility, certified stable gain, debt-bounded stability, and governance safety, whose conjunction yields full admissibility. It also separates oracle stable gain from the replayable lower certificates that alone are allowed to enter admission.

Several consequences follow. Window-contractive gain envelopes bound deviation from a co-moving scaffold and yield explicit yardstick-drift ceilings. Observable pseudometrics together with replayable gauge transport replace raw parameter norms in the open-ended theorem, so bounded governability no longer depends on coordinate choice or on silently changing the ruler. Delayed shadow lanes become certifying objects only when contamination, staleness, challenge coverage, and class-conditional transport calibration to the slow utility surrogate are all controlled. Contradiction must survive not merely as stored mass but as basis-robust, routed, inspectable disagreement with persistent obligations and finite-budget protected family exposure. Debt must include structural blast radius and bundled interaction debt or globally dangerous rewrites can masquerade as many small local wins. Forgetting must be compensated by regenerated contradiction mass or the system can legally burn down its own audit memory while remaining superficially compliant.

The paper's positive scientific claim is therefore conditional rather than universal: it is a first-principles sufficient-condition \emph{interface theory} of growth promotion on explicit observable comparison contracts, with admissibility-operator monotonicity as the core theorem and realized-path comparison only as an explicit transition-class corollary rather than the primary source of novelty. Stable recursive improvement requires disagreement to survive as a live governance input, audit diversity to stay ahead of attack reach, verification throughput and protected service lanes to scale with verification complexity and proposal throughput, proof-heavy proposals to be handled by proof-carrying escalation rather than left to an unmetered bottleneck, and replacement of stale evidence to be paid for under the current ruler with a governance-burden accounting that lower-bounds real protected resource use. Under those observable conditions the theory yields falsifiable interfaces rather than rhetoric. The fixed-threshold frontier theorem makes the positive content explicit: stronger replay, challenge, promotion, proof, reserve, and escrow slack expands the set of productive upgrades that can be admitted without destabilizing the loop and without appealing to deregulation. The frontier-expansion theorem then shows that some edits with zero immediate productive increment are still promotive because they enlarge future admissible frontiers under the same thresholds. The selector-invariant delayed-deployment theorem complements this by showing that delayed challenge need not be a bureaucratic graveyard: once a cohort acquires a positive delayed certificate, silent exposure delay, target-moving, and unreviewed rejection are all blocked by bounded-exposure entry and selector-invariant review, and bounded-delay deployment follows once the separate bounded-wait completion clause is added unless an audited certificate validates genuine ineligibility. The richer-proof-lane theorem extends the same logic to proof-heavy proposals beyond the current fast proof regime by tying bounded deployability to proof-carrying escalation, total replayable checkers, thermodynamic escrow, and cap-maintaining proof-lane intake rather than to wishful thinking. The resource-coupled service-scaling law then shows that success need not collapse those lanes provided service is backed by published protected budgets and replayable intake control. Finally, the surrogate-selector theorem shows that these comparisons do not require exact online solution of the one-step frontier maximization problem; replayable witness-dominating lower envelopes together with admissibility-operator monotonicity suffice, and the exact comparator case appears as the zero-distortion special case of the interval-comparator framework. Finally, the realized-path and resource-priced comparison corollaries state the stronger claim needed by an autonomous agent designer only in their correct explicit scope: they are transition-class corollaries built on the operator-monotonicity layer, and on the observable comparison contracts of Definitions~\ref{def:gp_class} and \ref{def:gp_net_class}, for explicit regime-policy pairs whose plus selector dominates replayably certified comparison witnesses, governance investments improve not only static admissibility sets but the realized raw and net productive trajectories themselves. When the interfaces fail, the failure mode is not mysterious: the loop loses identifiability, loses audit mass, loses deployment liveness, loses protected budget, or loses throughput before it loses rhetoric. For autonomous agents, that is the practical reason to implement the framework: it converts self-editing from an exercise in local score maximization into a reproducible upgrade protocol whose successful edits stay portable across future versions, whose governance improvements are certified investments in larger future growth frontiers even after accounting for governance cost, and whose failed edits leave auditable debris instead of mythology.
